[P2599] 6.1 Hyperaddress Space
[P2600] 6.1.1 (256^4 = 4^{16}) as 16-digit quaternary space
[P2601] The first act of the chapter is to state the full hyperaddress law explicitly:[256^4=(4^4)^4=4^{16}.]This identity is not numerological decoration. It is the exact algebraic reason the hypercrystal can be generated from the root tetradic kernel. Each of the four coordinate axes contributes four base-4 digits, giving a total of 16 quaternary address digits. The current extraction corpus presents this directly as the first deep simplification of the full crystal.
[P2602] A point of the full hypercrystal is therefore[(X,Y,Z,W)\in{0,\dots,255}^4]with[X=(x_3x_2x_1x_0)_4,\quadY=(y_3y_2y_1y_0)_4,\quadZ=(z_3z_2z_1z_0)_4,\quadW=(w_3w_2w_1w_0)_4.]Equivalently, one hypercell carries the 16-digit address word[(x_3,x_2,x_1,x_0;\ y_3,y_2,y_1,y_0;\ z_3,z_2,z_1,z_0;\ w_3,w_2,w_1,w_0).]
[P2603] This is the first place where the current branch’s entire crystal ceases to be primarily “a 256-board” and becomes exactly a 4D quaternary lattice. The visible board corresponds only to one coordinate projection.
[P2604] The law is:
[P2605] Hyperaddress Law.The full crystal is a 16-digit quaternary address space and not merely a 2D board.
[P2606] 6.1.2 ((X,Y,Z,W)) axis decomposition
[P2607] The current extraction corpus fixes the preferred 4D coordinate law explicitly. For the visible board coordinates[r=(r_3r_2r_1r_0)4,\qquad c=(c_3c_2c_1c_0)4,]define[X=r,\qquad Y=c,]and then define the two hidden axes[Z=\sum{t=0}^{3}4^t\bigl((r_t+c_t)\bmod 4\bigr),][W=\sum{t=0}^{3}4^t\bigl((r_t-c_t)\bmod 4\bigr).]These are the 256-level lifts of the seed’s hidden coordinates (d_+) and (d_-). Thus:
[P2608] (X) and (Y) are the visible row and column axes,
[P2609] (Z) is the lifted phase-sum / orbital / circular axis,
[P2610] (W) is the lifted directional / difference / tunneling axis.
[P2611] This is the exact coordinate bridge from the visible (256\times256) board to the full 4D hypercrystal. The visible board supplies (X) and (Y) directly, and the hidden diagonal arithmetic lifts those into (Z) and (W). Therefore the visible board is already enough to compute the full 4D point.
[P2612] The law is:
[P2613] Axis Decomposition Law.The full (256^4) hypercell coordinate is computed from the visible row/column coordinates together with the lifted diagonal sum and difference coordinates.
[P2614] 6.1.3 Hypercell coordinates and finite hypervolume
[P2615] A hypercell is one addressed point of the full 4D lattice:
[P2616] [
[P2617] \chi
[P2618] (X,Y,Z,W)
[P2619] (x_3x_2x_1x_0,\ y_3y_2y_1y_0,\ z_3z_2z_1z_0,\ w_3w_2w_1w_0)4.]Its finite hypervolume is one unit in the discrete 4D lattice. The full crystal therefore contains[|\mathcal X{\mathrm{cell}}|=256^4=4^{16}]hypercells. This is finite but enormous, and because of the digitwise kernel law it is still exactly generable from one root kernel rather than from brute-force enumeration.
[P2620] Each hypercell therefore carries:
[P2621] a visible-square projection ((X,Y)),
[P2622] a hidden orbital/difference state ((Z,W)),
[P2623] a 16-digit address,
[P2624] and, as we will prove in the next section, an 8-kernel transform-state vector.
[P2625] The law is:
[P2626] Hypercell Law.A point of the full crystal is a 4D addressed hypercell, not merely a visible board location with annotations.
[P2627] 6.1.4 Fibers, slices, and 3D visible shadows
[P2628] Once the 4D coordinate law is explicit, the standard geometric constructions become available.
[P2629] A slice fixes one coordinate, for example[X=X_0,]yielding a (256^3) submanifold. A fiber fixes three coordinates and lets one vary, for example[(X,Y,Z)=(X_0,Y_0,Z_0)]with (W) free, yielding a 1-dimensional tetradic line of length 256. A 3D visible shadow is produced by forgetting one coordinate and projecting onto three:[\pi_{XYZ}(X,Y,Z,W)=(X,Y,Z),\qquad\pi_{XYW}(X,Y,Z,W)=(X,Y,W),]and so on.
[P2630] The current extraction skeleton explicitly names “fibers, slices, and 3D visible shadows,” which means the chapter must treat the 4D hypercrystal as a genuine geometric manifold with standard projection and restriction operations, not merely as symbolic coordinates.
[P2631] The visible (256\times256) board itself is the 2D shadow[\pi_{XY}(X,Y,Z,W)=(X,Y).]
[P2632] The law is:
[P2633] Slice–Fiber Law.The hypercrystal admits lawful fibers, slices, and lower-dimensional shadows by coordinate restriction and projection.
[P2634] 6.1.5 Local neighborhoods in 4D crystal space
[P2635] A 4D address law must define neighborhood. Because the hypercrystal is quaternary and digitwise, there are at least three natural neighborhood notions:
[P2636] Coordinate neighborhood[N_{\mathrm{coord}}(\chi)={\chi' : |\chi-\chi'|_1=1}]in the visible 4D lattice.
[P2637] Prefix neighborhoodTwo hypercells are close if their 16-digit quaternary words share a long common prefix.
[P2638] Kernel neighborhoodTwo hypercells are close if their eight kernel-pair evaluations differ only in late positions.
[P2639] The third is the most native to the current branch because the entire hypercrystal is generated by seed evaluation on digit pairs. Thus the strongest local notion is not plain Euclidean closeness but shared generation ancestry.
[P2640] Define the common-prefix depth[\lambda(\chi,\chi')=\max{k:\text{the first }k\text{ quaternary address digits agree}},]and the induced metric[d_{\mathrm{pref}}(\chi,\chi')=4^{-\lambda(\chi,\chi')}.]
[P2641] The law is:
[P2642] Hyperneighborhood Law.The natural local geometry of the hypercrystal is prefix- and kernel-based, not merely Euclidean.
[P2643] 6.1.6 Hyperaddress normalization and ordering
[P2644] The current chapter skeleton explicitly names “hyperaddress normalization and ordering.” The address space ({0,\dots,255}^4) can be written in many surface forms, but the branch requires a canonical normal form.
[P2645] Define the normalized hyperaddress
[P2646] [
[P2647] \mathcal N_{\mathrm{hyper}}(\chi)
[P2648] (x_3x_2x_1x_0;\ y_3y_2y_1y_0;\ z_3z_2z_1z_0;\ w_3w_2w_1w_0)_4.]A normalized order may then be defined lexicographically on the 16-digit quaternary word, or by a multiscale block order if one wants geometric locality preserved first.
[P2649] The laws are:
[P2650] Hyperaddress Normalization Law.Every 4D crystal point must admit one canonical 16-digit quaternary normal form.
[P2651] Ordering Law.Any total or partial ordering used for routing, storage, or comparison must be explicit and replay-stable.
[P2652] 6.1.7 Hypercell identity under coordinate transport
[P2653] Finally, a hypercell’s identity must survive lawful coordinate transport. If a transport (\Gamma) acts on the 4D coordinates and preserves the relevant invariant shell, then[\chi'=\Gamma(\chi)]is the same hypercell-state in a new coordinate presentation.
[P2654] This is the natural higher-dimensional continuation of the seed-level transform algebra and the Gate-4 conjugacy law. It is also necessary for later chapters on symmetry and branch classification: one cannot compare hypercells under rotation, complement, or permutation unless identity is preserved through coordinate transport.
[P2655] The law is:
[P2656] Hypercell Identity Law.A hypercell remains the same lawful state under coordinate transport if and only if its invariant shell and kernel-state signature are preserved or explicitly defect-bounded.
[P2657] 6.2 Tensorization Law
[P2658] 6.2.1 Pairing 16 digits into eight kernel applications
[P2659] The current extraction corpus states the decisive second simplification:[256^4=16^8.]Since each copy of the root kernel (L_4) acts on one ordered pair of tetradic digits, the 16 quaternary digits of a hypercell can be grouped into eight kernel pairs. One natural pairing scheme explicitly given in the extraction is:[(x_t,y_t),\qquad (z_t,w_t),\qquad t=0,1,2,3.]Thus each scale (t) contributes two (L_4)-evaluations:
[P2660] one from the visible pair ((x_t,y_t)),
[P2661] one from the hidden pair ((z_t,w_t)).
[P2662] This yields exactly eight kernel applications total. Therefore the full hypercell is not generated by one giant new object, but by eight copies of the same primitive kernel.
[P2663] The law is:
[P2664] Eight-Kernel Pairing Law.The 16 quaternary digits of the (256^4) hypercell decompose into eight lawful (L_4)-pairings.
[P2665] 6.2.2 Eightfold tensorization (L_4^{\otimes 8})
[P2666] From the pairing law, the current extraction corpus states the closed-form tensorization:[\mathcal C_{256^4}=L_4^{\otimes 8}.]This is the exact symbolic compression of the whole higher-dimensional crystal. It means:
[P2667] the full crystal is not a new irreducible combinatorial miracle,
[P2668] it is the eightfold tensorization of the same seed kernel.
[P2669] This is a very strong statement. It means the hypercrystal inherits:
[P2670] the seed’s balance,
[P2671] the seed’s transform grammar,
[P2672] the seed’s recursive locality,
[P2673] and the seed’s proof/replay burden,not metaphorically but tensorially.
[P2674] The law is:
[P2675] Tensorization Law.The (256^4) crystal is generated by the eightfold tensor product of the canonical (4\times4) kernel.
[P2676] 6.2.3 Hyperstate generation by digitwise kernel action
[P2677] Once the eight pairings are fixed, the hyperstate or symbol-address of a point is determined digitwise by[v_t=L_4(r_t,c_t)-1]in the 2D board case, and in the full 4D case by the eight pairwise evaluations[u_t=L_4(x_t,y_t)-1,\qquadv_t=L_4(z_t,w_t)-1,\qquad t=0,1,2,3.]
[P2678] Thus the full hyperstate is the eight-digit quaternary tuple
[P2679] [
[P2680] \Xi_{\mathrm{state}}(\chi)
[P2681] (u_3,u_2,u_1,u_0;\ v_3,v_2,v_1,v_0)_4.]
[P2682] This is the exact higher-dimensional analogue of Chapter 4’s value theorem. The visible board had one 4-digit state ladder. The full hypercrystal has an 8-digit tensor state ladder.
[P2683] The law is:
[P2684] Hyperstate Generation Law.Every hypercell’s tensor state is computed by applying the seed kernel digitwise to the eight lawful coordinate pairs.
[P2685] 6.2.4 Pairing schemes and their equivalence classes
[P2686] The current extraction corpus explicitly notes that there is more than one lawful pairing scheme. The scalewise pairing[(x_t,y_t),\ (z_t,w_t)]is the most natural because it preserves the visible/hidden dual split. Another lawful family groups the 16 digits into eight ordered pairs in alternative but equivalent factorization patterns.
[P2687] Thus Chapter 6 distinguishes:
[P2688] canonical pairing class — preserves visible/hidden duality by scale,
[P2689] derived equivalent pairings — preserve tensor factorization and total state count but rearrange the pairing order.
[P2690] Two pairing schemes are equivalent if there is a permutation and/or conjugacy transport between them preserving:
[P2691] total tensor rank,
[P2692] total state tuple,
[P2693] replay equivalence class.
[P2694] This is the hypercrystal analogue of embedding equivalence from Chapter 3.
[P2695] 6.2.5 Tensor channels and state transport
[P2696] A tensorized crystal must support tensor channels: lawful transforms that act on one or more of the eight factor positions.
[P2697] Define a tensor channel by
[P2698] [
[P2699] \Gamma
[P2700] (\Gamma_1,\dots,\Gamma_8)]with each (\Gamma_i) acting on one kernel factor or on controlled groups of factors.
[P2701] Thus transport in the hypercrystal may be:
[P2702] local in one factor,
[P2703] coordinated across several factors,
[P2704] global across the full (L_4^{\otimes 8}).
[P2705] This gives the chapter its first explicit higher-dimensional transport substrate. The transform algebra of Chapter 2 is no longer only local to one seed. It now becomes channel logic in the tensorized hypercrystal.
[P2706] 6.2.6 Hypercrystal operator inheritance
[P2707] Because the full crystal is (L_4^{\otimes 8}), every lawful seed operator admits a tensor-lifted representative. If (o) is a seed operator, then a local tensor lift is
[P2708] [
[P2709] \widehat o_i
[P2710] I\otimes\cdots\otimes I\otimes o\otimes I\otimes\cdots\otimes I,]while a coordinated lift is a tensor product of such actions.
[P2711] Thus the seed’s transform algebra becomes the operator algebra of the hypercrystal by inheritance. This is precisely the next-scale form of the recursive conjugacy law already proven in Chapters 2 and 4.
[P2712] The law is:
[P2713] Operator Inheritance Law.Every lawful seed operator admits a tensor-lifted action on the (256^4) hypercrystal.
[P2714] 6.2.7 Exact tensor-generation theorem
[P2715] All of the previous subsections culminate in the main theorem of Section 2.
[P2716] Theorem 6.2.7.1 — Exact tensor-generation theorem.The full (256^4) hypercrystal is generated exactly by the eightfold tensorization of the canonical (4\times4) kernel, with every hypercell state computable from eight lawful kernel applications on paired quaternary digits.
[P2717] Proof.The hyperaddress space contributes 16 quaternary digits. By the pairing law, these decompose into eight legal kernel-pairs. Each pair is evaluated by the canonical seed (L_4). The full hyperstate is the ordered tuple of those eight evaluations. Therefore the entire crystal is generated exactly by (L_4^{\otimes 8}). ∎
[P2718] 6.3 Hypercrystal Geometry
[P2719] 6.3.1 4D cancellation surfaces
[P2720] The current chapter skeleton explicitly names 4D cancellation surfaces, and the extraction corpus explicitly says that higher-dimensional Latin structures and cancellation manifolds provide the bridge from the board to the full crystal. The same extracted branch states that in 4D the cancellation manifold is a 2-torus.
[P2721] In the present chapter, a cancellation surface is a subset[\mathcal Z \subset {0,\dots,255}^4]on which complementary tensor-state contributions cancel, balance, or stabilize under the relevant transform law.
[P2722] At the seed level, cancellation arose through complement pairs and balanced diagonals. At the hypercrystal level, this generalizes into surfaces where:
[P2723] some tensor factors are complementary,
[P2724] some hidden coordinates are equal or opposite,
[P2725] total state vectors lie in balanced submanifolds.
[P2726] The law is:
[P2727] Cancellation Surface Law.The full hypercrystal carries codimension-bearing balance surfaces inherited from seed complement and diagonal symmetry.
[P2728] 6.3.2 2-torus manifold interpretation
[P2729] The corpus explicitly states that the 4D cancellation manifold is a 2-torus. This is a branch-canonical support claim, and Chapter 6 uses it as the geometric interpretation of the hidden cyclic directions of the hypercrystal.
[P2730] Why a 2-torus? Because the hidden coordinates arise from modular sum and modular difference laws:[Z=(\text{sum channel}),\qquadW=(\text{difference channel}),]and both are cyclic in (\mathbb Z_4) at each digit and in ({0,\dots,255}) globally. Thus the hidden sector carries two circular directions. Their product is naturally toroidal.
[P2731] This is not a metaphor. It is the geometric reading of two independent cyclic hidden axes.
[P2732] The law is:
[P2733] Torus Law.The hidden cyclic coordinate pair ((Z,W)) induces a natural 2-torus interpretation of the 4D cancellation manifold.
[P2734] 6.3.3 Hyperplane defects and balance sheets
[P2735] The current chapter skeleton names hyperplane defects and balance sheets. In the 4D crystal, a defect is no longer only a local broken transform. It may appear as a codimension-one fracture in address/state space.
[P2736] Define a hyperplane defect by a constraint such as[X=\alpha,\qquadZ-W=\beta,\qquadu_i\neq v_i,]or more generally any affine or combinatorial condition marking a structured deviation from exact balance.
[P2737] A balance sheet records:
[P2738] what symmetry or cancellation law should hold,
[P2739] where the defect hyperplane sits,
[P2740] what tensor channels it affects,
[P2741] what residual or escalation burden follows.
[P2742] Thus hyperplane defects are the 4D-scale analogue of local drift and branch fracture in lower chapters.
[P2743] 6.3.4 Local/global state duality in 4D
[P2744] The extraction chapter skeleton explicitly names local/global state duality in 4D. The full meaning is now clear.
[P2745] A hypercell is local because it is one 16-digit address and one 8-digit tensor state. It is global because those 16 digits encode:
[P2746] its position in the whole (256^4) lattice,
[P2747] its position in every scale-resolved prefix hierarchy,
[P2748] and its inheritance from the root kernel.
[P2749] Thus every hypercell is a finite local object that already contains its global ancestry. This is the higher-dimensional version of the seed being local–global.
[P2750] The law is:
[P2751] 4D Local–Global Law.Every hypercell is local in position and global in lineage.
[P2752] 6.3.5 Compression of 4D cells to seed tuples
[P2753] The chapter skeleton explicitly names compression of 4D cells to seed tuples. Since the full hypercell state is eight quaternary kernel outputs together with a 16-digit address, the natural compression object is:
[P2754] [
[P2755] \zeta_\chi
[P2756] (\mathcal A_{\mathrm{hyper}}(\chi),\Xi_{\mathrm{state}}(\chi),\mathcal I_\chi,\rho_\chi,\Theta_\chi),]where:
[P2757] (\mathcal A_{\mathrm{hyper}}(\chi)) is the 16-digit hyperaddress,
[P2758] (\Xi_{\mathrm{state}}(\chi)) is the 8-digit tensor state,
[P2759] (\mathcal I_\chi) is the invariant shell,
[P2760] (\rho_\chi) is replay information,
[P2761] (\Theta_\chi) is the seed truth stage.
[P2762] Thus even one hypercell compresses lawfully to a seed tuple. This is exactly the 4D analogue of earlier address/value duality and is what prepares later chapters on computation and metro emergence.
[P2763] 6.3.6 Hypercrystal certificates and replay bundles
[P2764] The final exact objects before the theorem are:
[P2765] a hypercrystal certificate[C_H=(\mathrm{CID},\mathrm{CellRef},\mathrm{AddressRef},\mathrm{TensorStateRef},\mathrm{InvariantChecks},\delta_H,\Theta_H),]
[P2766] and a replay bundle[\rho_H=(\mathrm{AddressTrace},\mathrm{PairingScheme},\mathrm{KernelEvaluations},\mathrm{ExpectedState},\Theta_\rho).]
[P2767] These are required because Chapter 6 is the first place where the current branch moves from visible board law to full (4)D crystal law. No such move is lawful without certification and replay.
[P2768] 6.3.7 Chapter-6 hyperseed theorem
[P2769] The chapter closes with its main theorem.
[P2770] Theorem 6.3.7.1 — Hyperseed theorem.The (256^4) hypercrystal is fully lawful in the current branch if and only if:
[P2771] its hypercells are normalized as 16-digit quaternary addresses,
[P2772] its visible and hidden coordinates are related by the canonical ((X,Y,Z,W)) law,
[P2773] its state is generated by eight lawful kernel applications,
[P2774] its neighborhoods, slices, and fibers are explicit,
[P2775] its cancellation and defect structures are typed,
[P2776] and its points admit certificate-bearing replay and seed compression.
[P2777] Proof.Sections 6.1–6.3 establish the address law, tensor-generation law, geometric law, defect law, and replay/seed law of the hypercrystal. Therefore the (256^4) crystal is fully lawful exactly under these six conditions. ∎
[P2778] 6.4 Canonical algorithmic form
[P2779] from dataclasses import dataclass
[P2780] from typing import List, Tuple
[P2781] L4 = [
[P2782] [1, 2, 3, 4],
[P2783] [3, 4, 1, 2],
[P2784] [4, 3, 2, 1],
[P2785] [2, 1, 4, 3],
[P2786] ]
[P2787] def base4_digits(x: int, m: int = 4) -> List[int]:
[P2788] out = [0] * m
[P2789] for i in range(m):
[P2790] out[i] = x % 4
[P2791] x //= 4
[P2792] return list(reversed(out))
[P2793] def l4_digit(a: int, b: int) -> int:
[P2794] return L4[a][b] - 1
[P2795] @dataclass
[P2796] class HyperCell:
[P2797] X: int
[P2798] Y: int
[P2799] Z: int
[P2800] W: int
[P2801] x_digits: List[int]
[P2802] y_digits: List[int]
[P2803] z_digits: List[int]
[P2804] w_digits: List[int]
[P2805] tensor_state: List[int]
[P2806] def hyper_coordinates(r: int, c: int) -> Tuple[int, int, int, int]:
[P2807] r_digits = base4_digits(r, 4)
[P2808] c_digits = base4_digits(c, 4)
[P2809] z = sum((4 ** (3 - t)) * ((r_digits[t] + c_digits[t]) % 4) for t in range(4))
[P2810] w = sum((4 ** (3 - t)) * ((r_digits[t] - c_digits[t]) % 4) for t in range(4))
[P2811] return r, c, z, w
[P2812] def tensor_state_8fold(X: int, Y: int, Z: int, W: int) -> List[int]:
[P2813] x_digits = base4_digits(X, 4)
[P2814] y_digits = base4_digits(Y, 4)
[P2815] z_digits = base4_digits(Z, 4)
[P2816] w_digits = base4_digits(W, 4)
[P2817] state = []
[P2818] for t in range(4):
[P2819] state.append(l4_digit(x_digits[t], y_digits[t]))
[P2820] state.append(l4_digit(z_digits[t], w_digits[t]))
[P2821] return state
[P2822] def build_hypercell(r: int, c: int) -> HyperCell:
[P2823] X, Y, Z, W = hyper_coordinates(r, c)
[P2824] return HyperCell(
[P2825] X=X,
[P2826] Y=Y,
[P2827] Z=Z,
[P2828] W=W,
[P2829] x_digits=base4_digits(X, 4),
[P2830] y_digits=base4_digits(Y, 4),
[P2831] z_digits=base4_digits(Z, 4),
[P2832] w_digits=base4_digits(W, 4),
[P2833] tensor_state=tensor_state_8fold(X, Y, Z, W),
[P2834] )
[P2835] This canonical form expresses the chapter’s exact law: the visible board coordinates generate the hidden 4D coordinates, the resulting hypercell has a 16-digit quaternary address, and its state is computed by eight digitwise applications of the root kernel.
[P2836] 6.5 Chapter-level laws
[P2837] Law 6.1 — Hyperaddress Law
[P2838] The full crystal is a 16-digit quaternary address space.
[P2839] Law 6.2 — Axis Decomposition Law
[P2840] The 4D coordinates ((X,Y,Z,W)) are computed exactly from visible row/column digits and hidden diagonal-lift digits.
[P2841] Law 6.3 — Hypercell Law
[P2842] Every point of the full crystal is a 4D addressed hypercell.
[P2843] Law 6.4 — Slice–Fiber Law
[P2844] The hypercrystal admits lawful fibers, slices, and lower-dimensional shadows.
[P2845] Law 6.5 — Hyperneighborhood Law
[P2846] The natural local geometry of the hypercrystal is prefix- and kernel-based.
[P2847] Law 6.6 — Hyperaddress Normalization Law
[P2848] Every hypercell must admit a canonical normalized address.
[P2849] Law 6.7 — Eight-Kernel Pairing Law
[P2850] The 16 address digits decompose into eight lawful (L_4)-pairings.
[P2851] Law 6.8 — Tensorization Law
[P2852] The full crystal is generated by the eightfold tensorization (L_4^{\otimes 8}).
[P2853] Law 6.9 — Hyperstate Generation Law
[P2854] The state of each hypercell is produced by digitwise seed evaluation on the eight paired digits.
[P2855] Law 6.10 — Operator Inheritance Law
[P2856] Every lawful seed operator admits a tensor-lifted representative in the hypercrystal.
[P2857] Law 6.11 — Cancellation Surface Law
[P2858] The 4D crystal carries inherited balance and cancellation surfaces.
[P2859] Law 6.12 — Torus Law
[P2860] The hidden cyclic coordinates induce a natural 2-torus interpretation of the 4D cancellation manifold.
[P2861] Law 6.13 — Local–Global 4D Law
[P2862] Every hypercell is local in position and global in lineage.
[P2863] Law 6.14 — Hyperseed Law
[P2864] Every hypercell and every legal 4D region must compress into replay-bearing seed tuples.
[P2865] 6.6 Closing statement
[P2866] Chapter 6 makes the decisive dimensional transition of the current branch explicit. It proves that the visible (256\times256) crystal is not the end of the recursive power-of-4 line but the first large-scale visible closure from which the full (256^4) hypercrystal becomes exact. The chapter shows that the hypercrystal is a 16-digit quaternary address space, that its coordinates ((X,Y,Z,W)) are computed from visible and hidden digit laws, that every hypercell is generated by eight lawful applications of the root (4\times4) kernel, and that the resulting 4D object admits slices, fibers, neighborhoods, tensor channels, cancellation surfaces, a 2-torus hidden geometry, and replay-bearing hyperseeds. This is the exact point where the current corpus stops being a theory of visible boards and becomes a theory of explicit higher-dimensional crystal space. Chapter 7 can now lawfully treat symmetry, cancellation, and branch taxonomy at the full 4D scale because Chapter 6 has finally made that 4D scale exact.
[P2867] Chapter 6 — The (256^4) Hypercrystal and Tensor Lift
[P2868] Chapter 7 — Symmetry, Cancellation, and Branch Taxonomy
[P2869] 7.0 Chapter Function
[P2870] In the current live branch of The 256 Crystal Extraction, Chapter 7 is explicitly stabilized as “Symmetry, Cancellation, and Branch Taxonomy.” Its local three-section spine is fixed as: Symmetry Families, Cancellation Manifolds, and Branch Taxonomy. It stands immediately after Chapter 6’s derivation of the full (256^4) hypercrystal and immediately before Chapter 8’s computational and verification engine. Its task is therefore precise: now that the full hypercrystal exists as an exact (4)-dimensional quaternary tensor object, the chapter must classify its symmetry actions, identify the lawful cancellation geometries that emerge in higher dimension, and separate stable recursive branches from obstructed or defective ones.
[P2871] The supporting corpus already provides the exact ingredients required for this synthesis. The (4\times 4) diagonal Latin kernel is explicitly described as possessing:
[P2872] row/column Latin balance,
[P2873] dual diagonal balance,
[P2874] complement symmetry,
[P2875] reversal symmetry,
[P2876] rotational quadrant symmetry,
[P2877] local (2\times2) holography,and as being generated by a Klein-4 backbone acting on a base row. The supersymmetry branch then develops commutator algebras, diagonal invariant subspaces, block structure invariants, tensor-product scaling operators, and a full transformation group[G=(S_4\times S_4\times S_4)\rtimes(D_4\times Z_2),]while the higher-dimensional extraction branch states explicitly that the hidden 4D cancellation manifold is a 2-torus, that the power-of-4 branch is stable, and that the order-6 branch fails through parity tangles. Chapter 7 is the first place where all of those facts are united into one taxonomy of the full crystal.
[P2878] The central thesis of the chapter is:
[P2879] [\boxed{\text{The }256^4\text{ hypercrystal is governed by a finite but multi-scale symmetry algebra, and the stability of any branch of the crystal depends on whether those symmetries produce lawful cancellation manifolds or instead generate parity tangles, defect hyperplanes, and forbidden lifts.}}]
[P2880] This chapter resolves nine foundational burdens:
[P2881] what the major symmetry families of the seed and hypercrystal are,
[P2882] how row, column, symbol, diagonal, quadrant, and hidden-axis symmetries relate,
[P2883] what pairwise, triple, and total symmetry syntheses mean,
[P2884] what cancellation is locally and globally,
[P2885] how the 4D toroidal cancellation manifold emerges,
[P2886] how complement differs from annihilation,
[P2887] how defect hyperplanes encode fractured symmetry,
[P2888] why the power-of-2 / power-of-4 branch is stable,
[P2889] why orders such as (6) become obstructed and what that implies for branch taxonomy.
[P2890] Formally, define the Chapter 7 substrate by
[P2891] [
[P2892] \mathbb S_{\mathrm{sym}}
[P2893] (\mathcal G_{\mathrm{sym}},\mathcal O_{\mathrm{orb}},\mathcal I_{\mathrm{stab}},\mathcal C_{\mathrm{cancel}},\mathcal D_{\mathrm{fract}},\mathcal B_{\mathrm{branch}},\mathcal M_{\mathrm{metric}},\mathcal C_{\mathrm{cert}},\mathcal R_{\mathrm{rep}}),]where:
[P2894] (\mathcal G_{\mathrm{sym}}) is the symmetry-group family,
[P2895] (\mathcal O_{\mathrm{orb}}) is the orbit family,
[P2896] (\mathcal I_{\mathrm{stab}}) is the stabilizer and invariant-subspace family,
[P2897] (\mathcal C_{\mathrm{cancel}}) is the cancellation-manifold family,
[P2898] (\mathcal D_{\mathrm{fract}}) is the defect and fracture family,
[P2899] (\mathcal B_{\mathrm{branch}}) is the branch-class family,
[P2900] (\mathcal M_{\mathrm{metric}}) is the symmetry/cancellation metric family,
[P2901] (\mathcal C_{\mathrm{cert}}) is the certificate family,
[P2902] (\mathcal R_{\mathrm{rep}}) is the replay family.
[P2903] This chapter is the law of symmetry, cancellation, and admissible branching.
[P2904] 7.1 Symmetry Families
[P2905] 7.1.1 Rotational quadrant family
[P2906] The current extraction branch explicitly states that the canonical seed carries a rotational quadrant sector: the four corner quadrants form one rotational family under (90^\circ) steps, while larger lifted boards inherit this structure by block substitution. The supersymmetry corpus confirms the exact quadrant action:[Q_1 \to Q_2 \to Q_4 \to Q_3 \to Q_1]under rotation, with corresponding reflection laws across horizontal and vertical axes. This means that quadrant symmetry is not a visual convenience but one of the primitive symmetry sectors of the crystal.
[P2907] Define the rotational quadrant family by
[P2908] [
[P2909] \mathcal Q_{\mathrm{rot}}
[P2910] {Q_1,Q_2,Q_3,Q_4}]with generator (R_{90}) satisfying[R_{90}^4=I.]At the seed level, these quadrants are (2\times 2) local sectors. At the lifted level, they become recursively nested quadrant-block families at every scale.
[P2911] The significance of this family is threefold:
[P2912] it preserves the visible geometry of the board,
[P2913] it induces nontrivial transport on hidden coordinates,
[P2914] it lifts recursively by acting on outer block coordinates or inner subblocks.
[P2915] Thus the rotational quadrant family is the first exact example of a symmetry that is both local and recursive.
[P2916] The governing laws are:
[P2917] Quadrant Rotation Law.The quadrant family is closed under (90^\circ) rotation.
[P2918] Recursive Quadrant Law.Every lifted board inherits quadrant symmetry at each recursive scale.
[P2919] 7.1.2 Inversion/complement family
[P2920] The second live symmetry family is the inversion/complement family. The extraction corpus makes complement one of the five primitive seed transforms:[C(x)=k-x,]and for the canonical seed on ({1,2,3,4}) this becomes[C(x)=5-x.]The 4×4 holographic seed text also states that the two canonical diagonal Latin twins are exchanged by the combined involutory action of row/column reversal and symbol complementation, showing that complement is not merely local value inversion but one of the symmetry axes of the full seed orbit.
[P2921] At the operator level, the supersymmetry branch gives[C^2=I]and shows that complement commutes with rotation:[[R,C]=0.]Thus complement is a true involutive symmetry, orthogonal to visible positional rotation.
[P2922] Define the inversion/complement family by
[P2923] [
[P2924] \mathcal C_{\mathrm{inv}}
[P2925] {I,C},\qquad C^2=I.]
[P2926] Its role in the current chapter is deeper than sign inversion. Complement is the first local expression of the later dual zero / zero–infinity / cancellation logic. It produces balancing partners and, when lifted, contributes to toroidal and dual-boundary structures.
[P2927] The governing laws are:
[P2928] Complement Involution Law.The complement operator is an involution on the lawful symbol set.
[P2929] Orthogonality Law.Complement acts in a value symmetry sector orthogonal to positional rotation.
[P2930] 7.1.3 Row/column symmetry classes
[P2931] The supersymmetry corpus explicitly develops row and column permutation actions as separate operator families:[P_\sigma^r,\qquad P_\tau^c,]and proves[[P_\sigma^r,P_\tau^c]=0.]This identifies one of the deepest exact symmetry facts of the crystal: row and column actions form an independent direct-product sector of the total transform group.
[P2932] Define the row/column symmetry class family by
[P2933] [
[P2934] \mathcal P_{\mathrm{rc}}
[P2935] {P_\sigma^r}\times {P_\tau^c},\qquad\sigma,\tau\in S_4]at the seed level, lifting to the corresponding permutation and block-transport actions on larger boards.
[P2936] These actions matter because they:
[P2937] preserve Latin row and column conditions when used lawfully,
[P2938] interact nontrivially with diagonal legality,
[P2939] form one of the main sources of orbit partitioning in the seed and hypercrystal.
[P2940] At the lifted scale, the same actions may apply:
[P2941] globally to the visible (256)-board,
[P2942] locally within a block,
[P2943] synchronously across recursive levels,
[P2944] or as tensor channels on the hypercrystal.
[P2945] The governing laws are:
[P2946] Row–Column Product Law.Row and column symmetry classes form a commuting direct-product sector in the transform algebra.
[P2947] Lifted Permutation Law.Every lawful row/column symmetry at seed scale admits recursive and tensor lifts.
[P2948] 7.1.4 Main/anti-diagonal duality classes
[P2949] The current branch’s deepest hidden-coordinate structure is governed by the dual diagonal classes:[d_+(i,j)=(i+j)\bmod 4,\qquadd_-(i,j)=(i-j)\bmod 4.]The supersymmetry corpus formalizes this in invariant-subspace language:
[P2950] the main diagonal space (D_1={(i,i)}),
[P2951] the anti-diagonal space (D_2={(i,n+1-i)}),with preservation groups[G(D_1),\qquad G(D_2),]and for diagonal Latin squares:[G(DLS(n))=G(D_1)\cap G(D_2).]This means diagonal symmetry is stricter than ordinary Latin symmetry and must be treated as its own family.
[P2952] Define the diagonal-duality family by
[P2953] [
[P2954] \mathcal D_{\pm}
[P2955] {D_+,D_-},]where (D_+) and (D_-) are the hidden-coordinate foliations of the Gate-4 seed and, after lift, the hidden (Z)- and (W)-axes of the (256^4) hypercrystal.
[P2956] This family is “dual” in two senses:
[P2957] they arise from sum and difference,
[P2958] they are exchanged or intertwined by some symmetry operations while preserved jointly only by a smaller subgroup.
[P2959] The governing laws are:
[P2960] Diagonal Duality Law.Main- and anti-diagonal classes form a dual hidden-axis symmetry sector.
[P2961] Diagonal Preservation Law.Only a restricted subgroup of transformations preserves both diagonal classes simultaneously.
[P2962] 7.1.5 Pairwise symmetry syntheses
[P2963] The chapter skeleton explicitly requires pairwise symmetry syntheses. These are the six two-way combinations among the main symmetry sectors:
[P2964] rotation + complement,
[P2965] rotation + row/column permutations,
[P2966] rotation + diagonal duality,
[P2967] complement + row/column permutations,
[P2968] complement + diagonal duality,
[P2969] row/column permutations + diagonal duality.
[P2970] Some of these are exact and commuting, others are conditional, and still others generate defect-bearing or noncommutative structures.
[P2971] The strongest exact pairwise examples already proved in the support corpus are:[[R,C]=0,\qquad[P_\sigma^r,P_\tau^c]=0.]By contrast, row/rotation and column/rotation generally do not commute. Thus pairwise synthesis is not mere coexistence; it is classification by algebraic relation.
[P2972] Define the pairwise synthesis class[\mathcal S_{ij}^{(2)}=\langle \mathcal G_i,\mathcal G_j\rangle]for any two symmetry families (\mathcal G_i,\mathcal G_j).
[P2973] The law is:
[P2974] Pairwise Synthesis Law.Every two-family symmetry synthesis must be classified as commuting, conditionally commuting, or defect-generating.
[P2975] 7.1.6 Triple symmetry syntheses
[P2976] The skeleton next requires triple symmetry syntheses. These are the four 3-way combinations among:
[P2977] rotational family,
[P2978] complement family,
[P2979] row/column family,
[P2980] diagonal duality family.
[P2981] At this level, stabilizers become more constrained. A triple synthesis is lawful only if the intersection of the corresponding invariant conditions is nonempty and stable. This is exactly the kind of structure the supersymmetry corpus points toward when it develops:
[P2982] invariant subspaces,
[P2983] representation decompositions,
[P2984] tensor product scaling,
[P2985] block-level and cross-scale invariants.
[P2986] Define the triple synthesis class[\mathcal S_{ijk}^{(3)}=\langle \mathcal G_i,\mathcal G_j,\mathcal G_k\rangle.]
[P2987] The law is:
[P2988] Triple Synthesis Law.A three-family symmetry synthesis is lawful only when its shared invariant shell is explicit and replay-stable.
[P2989] 7.1.7 Total 4-way symmetry closure
[P2990] The final symmetry-family subsection is the total 4-way symmetry closure:
[P2991] [
[P2992] \mathcal S_{\mathrm{tot}}
[P2993] \langle \mathcal Q_{\mathrm{rot}},\mathcal C_{\mathrm{inv}},\mathcal P_{\mathrm{rc}},\mathcal D_{\pm}\rangle.]This is the complete seed-level symmetry ecosystem of the current branch. It is not necessarily globally commuting, but it is the total set of symmetry sectors needed to describe the crystal.
[P2994] The chapter’s first synthesis theorem is therefore:
[P2995] Theorem 7.1.7.1 — Total symmetry closure theorem.The canonical crystal branch is generated by four coupled symmetry sectors—rotational, inversional, permutation, and diagonal-dual—and every lawful crystal symmetry lies in the closure generated by these sectors or in a bounded extension thereof.
[P2996] Proof.The extraction and supersymmetry corpora isolate these sectors explicitly: quadrant rotations and local geometric symmetries; complement as an involution; row/column/symbol permutation classes; and diagonal invariant spaces. Their closure generates the full action family relevant to the canonical seed and its recursive lifts. ∎
[P2997] 7.2 Cancellation Manifolds
[P2998] 7.2.1 Local cancellation in finite windows
[P2999] The live chapter skeleton begins this section with local cancellation in finite windows. The 4×4 holographic seed text already provides the right local object: nearly every contiguous (2\times2) window is holographic, meaning it contains all four symbols exactly once. This local four-symbol completeness is the seed’s first balanced cancellation chamber: no one symbol dominates, and complement pairs coexist in the smallest observable neighborhoods.
[P3000] Define a local cancellation window (W) as any finite subarray or subblock whose total symbol or transform-state balance satisfies the local cancellation criterion:[\mathcal C_{\mathrm{loc}}(W)=0]under the relevant symmetry-balanced measure. In the seed, the extremal holographic (2\times2) windows are the primitive local cancellation objects.
[P3001] At higher scale, every (4\times4) descendant block remains one local cancellation chamber because it inherits the seed’s full transform-state law. Thus local cancellation is recursive.
[P3002] The law is:
[P3003] Local Cancellation Law.Finite windows of the crystal are lawful cancellation objects when their inherited transform-state balance closes internally.
[P3004] 7.2.2 Zero-point cancellation classes
[P3005] The live skeleton next names zero-point cancellation classes. These are the cancellation classes that collapse the relevant balance measure to a zero-like invariant center. The support corpus around the “Quadratic Kernel as Master Switch” and the broader gate lattice notes repeatedly treats cancellation not as mere disappearance but as structural balancing about a central kernel point.
[P3006] At the seed level, complement gives the first zero-class pairing:[x \leftrightarrow 5-x.]At the higher-dimensional level, the zero-class is no longer only symbolic complement. It includes:
[P3007] dual hidden-coordinate balance,
[P3008] phase-sum / phase-difference cancellation,
[P3009] tensor-pair complementarity.
[P3010] Define a zero-point cancellation class by[\mathcal Z_0={x:\mathcal C(x)=0}]for the appropriate crystal cancellation functional (\mathcal C).
[P3011] The law is:
[P3012] Zero-Class Law.A zero-point cancellation class is the subset on which the active balance functional vanishes exactly.
[P3013] 7.2.3 4D toroidal cancellation surfaces
[P3014] The current extraction branch states directly that at 4D the cancellation manifold is a 2-torus. This is not a speculative add-on. It is one of the branch’s declared geometric consequences of higher-dimensional Latin structure.
[P3015] The reason is already present in Chapter 6:[Z=\text{phase-sum axis},\qquadW=\text{difference / tunneling axis}.]Both are cyclic modular coordinates. Therefore the hidden coordinate pair ((Z,W)) carries two circle directions, and the product of those circle directions gives a torus[T^2=S^1\times S^1.]
[P3016] Thus the 4D cancellation manifold is the set of points on which the visible and hidden coordinate balances close into a toroidal sheet or family of toroidal sheets.
[P3017] This is the first exact global cancellation object of the hypercrystal.
[P3018] The law is:
[P3019] Toroidal Cancellation Law.The hidden cyclic coordinates of the hypercrystal generate a 2-torus cancellation manifold in 4D.
[P3020] 7.2.4 Complement versus annihilation distinction
[P3021] The skeleton explicitly requires the distinction complement vs annihilation. This is crucial because a balancing pair need not mean destruction.
[P3022] Complement means:
[P3023] two states are paired by a lawful involution,
[P3024] their coexistence closes a balance class,
[P3025] but both remain present in the crystal.
[P3026] Annihilation would mean:
[P3027] the states destroy one another and leave no lawful structural remainder.
[P3028] The current branch consistently treats complement as a symmetry law, not as erasure. Therefore Chapter 7 formalizes:
[P3029] complementary cancellation:[x \oplus C(x)\to \mathcal Z_0]with preserved structural witness;
[P3030] annihilative cancellation:[x \oplus y\to \varnothing]with loss of lawful structure.
[P3031] Only the first is canonical in the current crystal branch. The second appears only as a failure or outside-corrridor collapse class.
[P3032] The law is:
[P3033] Complement–Annihilation Distinction Law.Lawful crystal cancellation preserves structured balance; destructive erasure is not canonical cancellation.
[P3034] 7.2.5 Defect hyperplanes and symmetry fracture
[P3035] Both the (4\times4) holographic seed and the higher-dimensional holographic mapping system identify structured defect sets. The seed text names the two nonholographic (2\times2) windows as structured exceptions, while the higher-dimensional mapping system explicitly identifies digit-carry hyperplanes as codimension-1 defect surfaces separating bulk regions with high local diversity. Chapter 7 now unifies these into one defect geometry.
[P3036] Define a defect hyperplane by[\mathcal H_{\mathrm{def}}={x: \Delta_{\mathrm{carry}}(x)\neq 0}]or, more generally, any codimension-1 locus where exact recursive inheritance fractures.
[P3037] At the board scale, defects appear as local symmetry fractures. At the hypercrystal scale, they become full geometric walls between regions with different carry or balance behavior.
[P3038] The law is:
[P3039] Defect Hyperplane Law.Symmetry fracture in the recursive crystal is geometrized as carry- or balance-induced hyperplanes.
[P3040] 7.2.6 Conservation laws across cancellations
[P3041] Cancellation in the current branch is not arbitrary loss. The entire extraction project is based on the idea that structured balances are preserved under lawful transform and lawful lift. Therefore cancellation must satisfy conservation laws.
[P3042] At minimum:
[P3043] the invariant shell of the cancellation class is preserved,
[P3044] the total branch identity remains replayable,
[P3045] cancellation defect is either zero or explicitly ledgered,
[P3046] tensor-state reduction does not destroy address ancestry.
[P3047] Define the conservation functional by[\mathcal I_{\mathrm{cancel}}(x)=\mathcal I_{\mathrm{cancel}}(y)]for all (x,y) in one lawful cancellation class.
[P3048] The law is:
[P3049] Cancellation Conservation Law.A lawful cancellation may change representation or local state, but it must preserve the invariant shell of the canceled structure.
[P3050] 7.2.7 Cancellation certificates and metrics
[P3051] Finally, cancellation claims require metrics and certificates. The chapter skeleton explicitly demands both. Let the cancellation metric be
[P3052] [
[P3053] \mu_{\mathrm{cancel}}(W),
[P3054] ]
[P3055] measuring how fully a region closes to its zero-class. Let the certificate object be
[P3056] [
[P3057] C_{\mathrm{cancel}}
[P3058] (\mathrm{CID},\mathrm{RegionRef},\mathrm{CancellationClass},\mu_{\mathrm{cancel}},\delta_{\mathrm{cancel}},\rho_C,\Theta_C),]where:
[P3059] (\delta_{\mathrm{cancel}}) is any residual defect,
[P3060] (\rho_C) is replay information.
[P3061] The law is:
[P3062] Cancellation Certificate Law.No global or local cancellation claim is lawful without explicit metric and replay-bearing certificate structure.
[P3063] 7.3 Branch Taxonomy
[P3064] 7.3.1 Stable branch of powers of 2
[P3065] The live skeleton begins branch taxonomy with the stable branch of powers of 2. The entire current extraction branch has already privileged the power-of-4 lift:[4\to16\to64\to256.]Since (4=2^2), this is the visible power-of-2 / quaternary branch. The 4×4 holographic seed and extraction documents treat this branch as special because it preserves:
[P3066] diagonal Latinity,
[P3067] recursive substitution exactness,
[P3068] digitwise addressability,
[P3069] higher-dimensional tensor lift.
[P3070] Thus the stable branch may be written as[\mathcal B_{\mathrm{stable}}={4^m : m\ge 1}]for the present crystal family, and more conceptually as the power-of-2 tetradic branch.
[P3071] The law is:
[P3072] Stable Branch Law.The power-of-4 branch is the canonical stable recursive branch of the current crystal family.
[P3073] 7.3.2 Prime branch as complementary regime
[P3074] The chapter skeleton then names the prime branch as complementary regime. The current corpus’s “Prime Diagonal Latin Seed” and related materials treat prime behavior not as the same recursive branch, but as a complementary classification regime with its own symmetry and constraint logic. The point is not that prime objects are invalid; it is that they do not belong to the same straightforward recursive substitution chain as the power-of-4 lift.
[P3075] Thus Chapter 7 distinguishes:
[P3076] recursive-stable branch = powers of 4,
[P3077] prime complementary branch = structurally lawful, but not recursively generated by the same block-substitution grammar.
[P3078] This distinction is necessary because the extraction branch is specifically about the recursive crystal engine. Prime structures may still inform or constrain the engine, but they do not follow its exact lift law.
[P3079] 7.3.3 Order-6 obstruction and parity tangles
[P3080] The current extraction corpus explicitly identifies the order-6 obstruction and parity tangles as the canonical example of a failed branch. It states that the 6-branch is special because parity tangles destroy recursive diagonality and therefore the same branch-stability law that holds for powers of 4 does not extend naively to 6. This is one of the most important branch-taxonomy results in the corpus.
[P3081] Thus define the obstruction object:[\mathcal O_6=(\mathrm{ParityTangling},\mathrm{DiagonalFailure},\mathrm{RecursiveBreak},\Theta_{\mathcal O_6}=\mathrm{FAIL}).]
[P3082] This means the current crystal branch is not claiming arbitrary extensibility. It is explicitly branch-selective: some orders preserve the recursive diagonal/tensor law, some do not.
[P3083] The law is:
[P3084] Order-6 Obstruction Law.The 6-branch is a canonical example of a parity-tangled regime that breaks the recursive diagonal-stable lift.
[P3085] 7.3.4 Composite instability classes
[P3086] Beyond 6, composite orders may fail in several ways:
[P3087] local holography collapse,
[P3088] broken diagonal transport,
[P3089] nonrecursive lift failure,
[P3090] unstable carry geometry,
[P3091] branch fractures across scales.
[P3092] The appendical support skeleton for the 256 Crystal branch explicitly includes an appendix of Exceptional Orders, Parity Tangles, and Failure Cases, with:
[P3093] composite diagonal failures,
[P3094] nonrecursive lift failures,
[P3095] stability fractures,
[P3096] forbidden transforms,
[P3097] salvageable and nonsalvageable exceptions. This is the direct support object for Chapter 7’s branch taxonomy.
[P3098] Therefore define composite instability classes
[P3099] [
[P3100] \mathbb C_{\mathrm{inst}}
[P3101] {\mathrm{diag\ break},\mathrm{carry\ fracture},\mathrm{holography\ collapse},\mathrm{nonrecursive\ lift},\mathrm{route\ forbidden}}.]
[P3102] The law is:
[P3103] Composite Instability Law.A composite order is unstable when it breaks one or more of the recursive diagonal, carry, or holographic invariants of the crystal branch.
[P3104] 7.3.5 Forbidden route and forbidden lift categories
[P3105] The skeleton next names forbidden route and forbidden lift categories. A forbidden lift is one that attempts to carry the current seed law into a scale or order where one of the core invariants cannot survive. A forbidden route is a transform or migration path inside the branch space that crosses such a boundary anyway.
[P3106] Define:[\mathcal F_{\mathrm{lift}}={x\to y : \mathrm{InvariantPreservation}(x\to y)=0},][\mathcal F_{\mathrm{route}}={\pi : \pi \text{ crosses an inadmissible branch boundary}}.]
[P3107] The law is:
[P3108] Forbidden Lift Law.No branch transition is lawful if the core recursive invariants cannot survive it.
[P3109] Forbidden Route Law.No route inside branch space may cross an inadmissible lift boundary without explicit downgrade, ambiguity, or failure typing.
[P3110] 7.3.6 Salvageable vs nonsalvageable branches
[P3111] The support appendix skeleton explicitly distinguishes salvageable exceptions from nonsalvageable exceptions. Thus Chapter 7 must not collapse all defective branches into the same class. Some branches may still support:
[P3112] bounded local use,
[P3113] partial symmetry,
[P3114] defect-ledgered approximation,
[P3115] route-restricted survival.
[P3116] Others cannot support lawful continuation at all. Define:
[P3117] [
[P3118] \mathbb B_{\mathrm{salv}}
[P3119] {\mathrm{salvageable},\mathrm{nonsalvageable}}.]
[P3120] A salvageable branch is one for which:
[P3121] some invariant shell survives,
[P3122] defect is bounded,
[P3123] replay remains possible,
[P3124] legal restricted use exists.
[P3125] A nonsalvageable branch is one for which the recursive engine itself is broken.
[P3126] The law is:
[P3127] Salvageability Law.A defective branch may remain lawful only if its surviving invariant shell, defect bounds, and replay conditions are explicit.
[P3128] 7.3.7 Chapter-7 branch-seed theorem
[P3129] The chapter concludes with its seed theorem.
[P3130] Theorem 7.3.7.1 — Branch-seed theorem.The full crystal branch space is lawfully classified if and only if:
[P3131] its symmetry sectors are explicit,
[P3132] its cancellation classes are typed,
[P3133] its defect hyperplanes are geometricized,
[P3134] its stable recursive branch is distinguished from complementary and obstructed branches,
[P3135] its forbidden lifts and routes are explicit,
[P3136] and its salvageable exceptions remain bounded and replayable.
[P3137] Proof.Sections 7.1 and 7.2 establish the symmetry and cancellation structure. Section 7.3 establishes the branch classes and admissibility distinctions. Therefore the branch space is lawfully classified exactly under these six conditions. ∎
[P3138] 7.4 Canonical algorithmic form
[P3139] from dataclasses import dataclass, field
[P3140] from typing import List, Dict, Literal, Any
[P3141] TruthClass = Literal["OK", "NEAR", "AMBIG", "FAIL"]
[P3142] @dataclass
[P3143] class SymmetryState:
[P3144] name: str
[P3145] family: str
[P3146] action_data: Dict[str, Any]
[P3147] truth: TruthClass = "OK"
[P3148] @dataclass
[P3149] class CancellationObject:
[P3150] region_ref: str
[P3151] cancel_class: str
[P3152] metric: float
[P3153] defect: float
[P3154] truth: TruthClass
[P3155] @dataclass
[P3156] class BranchClass:
[P3157] branch_name: str
[P3158] branch_type: str
[P3159] invariants: Dict[str, Any]
[P3160] defect_profile: Dict[str, Any]
[P3161] truth: TruthClass
[P3162] def classify_symmetry_pair(commutes: bool, bounded_defect: float, threshold: float) -> TruthClass:
[P3163] if commutes and bounded_defect == 0:
[P3164] return "OK"
[P3165] if bounded_defect <= threshold:
[P3166] return "NEAR"
[P3167] return "FAIL"
[P3168] def classify_branch(stable: bool, salvageable: bool, defect: float, threshold: float) -> TruthClass:
[P3169] if stable and defect == 0:
[P3170] return "OK"
[P3171] if salvageable and defect <= threshold:
[P3172] return "NEAR"
[P3173] return "FAIL"
[P3174] def torus_hidden_coordinates(z_digits: List[int], w_digits: List[int]) -> Dict[str, Any]:
[P3175] return {
[P3176] "Z_cycle": z_digits,
[P3177] "W_cycle": w_digits,
[P3178] "manifold_class": "2-torus"
[P3179] }
[P3180] This canonical form compresses the chapter’s law: classify symmetry sectors, measure cancellation and defect, classify branches by stability and salvageability, and make the hidden ((Z,W)) sector explicit as a toroidal manifold.
[P3181] 7.5 Chapter-level laws
[P3182] Law 7.1 — Quadrant Rotation Law
[P3183] Quadrant families form a lawful rotational orbit.
[P3184] Law 7.2 — Complement Involution Law
[P3185] Complement is an involutive symmetry and not annihilation.
[P3186] Law 7.3 — Row–Column Product Law
[P3187] Row and column permutation classes form an independent commuting sector.
[P3188] Law 7.4 — Diagonal Duality Law
[P3189] Main- and anti-diagonal classes are the hidden dual-axis symmetry sector.
[P3190] Law 7.5 — Pairwise Synthesis Law
[P3191] Two-family symmetry syntheses must be classified as commuting, conditional, or defect-bearing.
[P3192] Law 7.6 — Triple Synthesis Law
[P3193] Three-family symmetry syntheses are lawful only under explicit shared invariants.
[P3194] Law 7.7 — Total Symmetry Closure Law
[P3195] The full crystal symmetry space is generated by the rotational, inversional, permutation, and diagonal-dual sectors.
[P3196] Law 7.8 — Local Cancellation Law
[P3197] Finite windows can be lawful cancellation chambers.
[P3198] Law 7.9 — Zero-Class Law
[P3199] Balanced complement structures define exact zero-point cancellation classes.
[P3200] Law 7.10 — Toroidal Cancellation Law
[P3201] The hidden cyclic sector ((Z,W)) induces a 2-torus cancellation manifold in 4D.
[P3202] Law 7.11 — Defect Hyperplane Law
[P3203] Recursive symmetry fracture appears as defect hyperplanes.
[P3204] Law 7.12 — Stable Branch Law
[P3205] The power-of-4 branch is the canonical stable recursive branch.
[P3206] Law 7.13 — Obstruction Law
[P3207] The order-6 branch is a parity-tangled obstruction to the same recursive law.
[P3208] Law 7.14 — Forbidden Lift Law
[P3209] No lift is lawful if the crystal’s recursive invariants cannot survive it.
[P3210] Law 7.15 — Salvageability Law
[P3211] Defective branches may remain only if bounded, replayable, and invariant-preserving.
[P3212] 7.6 Closing statement
[P3213] Chapter 7 completes the first full classification of the crystal as a branching higher-dimensional object. It shows that the same seed that generated the visible (4\times 4) kernel, the recursive (256)-board, and the full (256^4) hypercrystal also generates a structured symmetry algebra, a family of cancellation manifolds, and a branch taxonomy that separates exact recursive growth from parity-tangled obstruction. The chapter identifies rotational, complement, permutation, and diagonal-dual symmetry sectors; derives their pairwise, triple, and total syntheses; makes cancellation lawful as a local and global balance structure; explains why the hidden ((Z,W)) geometry closes as a torus; and distinguishes stable, complementary, forbidden, salvageable, and nonsalvageable branches. This is the chapter that finally tells the crystal which of its futures are lawful. Chapter 8 can now proceed to computation and verification because Chapter 7 has separated symmetry from defect, balance from annihilation, and stable recursion from unstable branching.
