[P5211] The final theorem of Appendix D is therefore:
[P5212] [\boxed{\text{The recursive crystal lift is fully lawful only when its seed, substitution law, digitwise value formula, prefix block grammar, proof family, logs, replay bundles, and lift seed form one coherent replayable recursion grammar.}}]
[P5213] D.17 Canonical algorithmic form
[P5214] from dataclasses import dataclass
[P5215] from typing import List, Tuple, Dict, Any
[P5216] L4 = [
[P5217] [1, 2, 3, 4],
[P5218] [3, 4, 1, 2],
[P5219] [4, 3, 2, 1],
[P5220] [2, 1, 4, 3],
[P5221] ]
[P5222] def base4_digits(x: int, m: int) -> List[int]:
[P5223] out = [0] * m
[P5224] for i in range(m):
[P5225] out[i] = x % 4
[P5226] x //= 4
[P5227] return list(reversed(out))
[P5228] def lifted_value(r: int, c: int, m: int) -> int:
[P5229] r_digits = base4_digits(r, m)
[P5230] c_digits = base4_digits(c, m)
[P5231] value = 0
[P5232] for rd, cd in zip(r_digits, c_digits):
[P5233] value = 4 * value + (L4[rd][cd] - 1)
[P5234] return value + 1
[P5235] @dataclass
[P5236] class LiftLog:
[P5237] target_ref: str
[P5238] depth: int
[P5239] prefix_path: List[Tuple[int, int]]
[P5240] substitution_trace: List[Dict[str, Any]]
[P5241] truth_stage: str
[P5242] def block_prefix(r: int, c: int, m: int, k: int) -> Tuple[List[int], List[int]]:
[P5243] rd = base4_digits(r, m)
[P5244] cd = base4_digits(c, m)
[P5245] return rd[:m-k], cd[:m-k]
[P5246] def build_lift_log(r: int, c: int, m: int) -> LiftLog:
[P5247] rd = base4_digits(r, m)
[P5248] cd = base4_digits(c, m)
[P5249] trace = []
[P5250] for t, (a, b) in enumerate(zip(rd, cd)):
[P5251] trace.append({"scale": t, "row_digit": a, "col_digit": b, "seed_value": L4[a][b]})
[P5252] return LiftLog(
[P5253] target_ref=f"L_{4**m}({r},{c})",
[P5254] depth=m,
[P5255] prefix_path=list(zip(rd, cd)),
[P5256] substitution_trace=trace,
[P5257] truth_stage="OK"
[P5258] )
[P5259] This canonical form compresses the appendix’s law: every lifted cell is evaluated digitwise from the seed, every block is a prefix region, and every evaluation can emit a replay-bearing lift log.
[P5260] D.18 Appendix-level laws
[P5261] Base Recursion Law — all visible boards in the branch are built from exact substitution into (L_4).
[P5262] Induction Base Law — the root of the lift is the canonical diagonal-Latin seed.
[P5263] Induction Step Law — row, column, and diagonal legality are preserved under recursive substitution.
[P5264] Closed Recursive Formula Law — every lifted value is a digitwise recomposition of seed evaluations.
[P5265] Prefix Block Law — every block is addressed by a row/column prefix.
[P5266] Digitwise Value Law — (L_{256}) is exactly four seed evaluations recomposed in base 4.
[P5267] 16-Board Construction Law — (L_{16}) is the first recursive bloom.
[P5268] 64-Board Construction Law — (L_{64}) is the second recursive bloom.
[P5269] 256-Board Construction Law — (L_{256}) is the full visible board closure.
[P5270] Local–Global Inheritance Law — the same seed law is preserved at every scale.
[P5271] Block Boundary Law — block interfaces are both geometric and transform-state boundaries.
[P5272] Memory Compression Law — the branch is stored lawfully by generator plus sparse residuals.
[P5273] Lift Proof Law — strong lift claims require seed and recursion references.
[P5274] Lift Log Law — recursive ancestry must be recorded explicitly.
[P5275] Lift Seed Law — the whole recursion grammar must compress into a replay-bearing lift seed.
[P5276] D.19 Closing statement
[P5277] Appendix D defines the recursive lift and block-substitution grammar of the 256 Crystal branch. It begins from the exact canonical seed and proves that the visible branch[4\to16\to64\to256]is generated by one lawful base-4 substitution rule. It then shows that every value is digitwise, every block is a prefix-defined region, every boundary is both geometric and transform-state, every local object inherits the whole seed law, and every subblock is replayable from its prefix and the seed alone. In this appendix the crystal becomes generative in a mathematically exact sense. Without Appendix D, the seed would remain a lawful local kernel but not a lawful branch engine. With Appendix D, the seed unfolds.
[P5278] Appendix D — Recursive Lift and Block Substitution
[P5279] Appendix E — Base-4 Address and Location Calculus
[P5280] E.0 Appendix Function
[P5281] In the current live branch of The 256 Crystal Extraction, Appendix E is explicitly stabilized as “Base-4 Address and Location Calculus.” Its 16 macro-cells are fixed as:
[P5282] Cell address law
[P5283] 4-block address law
[P5284] 16-block address law
[P5285] 64-block address law
[P5286] Board identity law
[P5287] Prefix retrieval
[P5288] Suffix reconstruction
[P5289] Block locality
[P5290] Neighborhood metrics
[P5291] Update transport
[P5292] Address normalization
[P5293] Address hashes
[P5294] Route hooks
[P5295] Location proofs
[P5296] Replay pathing
[P5297] Address seed.
[P5298] Appendix E is therefore the first appendix of the 256 Crystal branch in which the crystal ceases to be only a recursively generated board and becomes a fully navigable address manifold. The live chapter spine already established the core ingredients that AppE now formalizes: Chapter 4 proved the recursive lift law and the digitwise value theorem; Chapter 5 fixed the chapter-level “Crystal Address, Location, and Block Geometry” program with cell address, 4/16/64-block addresses, board identity, prefix retrieval, suffix reconstruction, locality, normalization, route hooks, location proofs, and replay pathing. Appendix E is the full support-layer extraction of that law.
[P5299] A deeper support branch sharpens the same role through the doctrine of Addressed Holography and DLS Memory. It explicitly names:
[P5300] HoloAddress grammar,
[P5301] prefix stability,
[P5302] streamed decode,
[P5303] address-preserving rewrites,
[P5304] random access under incomplete materialization,
[P5305] replayable reconstruction proofs,
[P5306] generator-plus-residual storage law,
[P5307] and deterministic carrier reconstruction. This means AppE is not merely about notation for coordinates. It is the place where the crystal’s address law becomes a lawful storage, retrieval, and routing substrate.
[P5308] The root canonical data remain:
[P5309] [
[P5310] L_4=
[P5311] \begin{bmatrix}
[P5312] 1&2&3&4\
[P5313] 3&4&1&2\
[P5314] 4&3&2&1\
[P5315] 2&1&4&3
[P5316] \end{bmatrix},
[P5317] ]
[P5318] together with the recursive substitution law
[P5319] [
[P5320] L_{4^m}\bigl(4^{m-1}i+r,\ 4^{m-1}j+s\bigr)
[P5321] 4^{m-1}\bigl(L_4(i,j)-1\bigr)+L_{4^{m-1}}(r,s),]and the exact location dual:a block of side (4^k) inside a (4^m)-board is determined by the first (m-k) base-4 digits of its row and column address.
[P5322] Formally, define the Appendix E substrate by
[P5323] [
[P5324] \mathbb E_{\mathrm{addr}}
[P5325] (\mathcal A_{\mathrm{cell}},\mathcal B_{\mathrm{blk}},\mathcal P_{\mathrm{pref}},\mathcal S_{\mathrm{suf}},\mathcal L_{\mathrm{loc}},\mathcal M_{\mathrm{metric}},\mathcal N_{\mathrm{norm}},\mathcal R_{\mathrm{rep}},\mathcal S_{\mathrm{seed}}),]where:
[P5326] (\mathcal A_{\mathrm{cell}}) is the cell-address family,
[P5327] (\mathcal B_{\mathrm{blk}}) is the block-address family,
[P5328] (\mathcal P_{\mathrm{pref}}) is the prefix-retrieval family,
[P5329] (\mathcal S_{\mathrm{suf}}) is the suffix-reconstruction family,
[P5330] (\mathcal L_{\mathrm{loc}}) is the locality family,
[P5331] (\mathcal M_{\mathrm{metric}}) is the address-metric family,
[P5332] (\mathcal N_{\mathrm{norm}}) is the normalization family,
[P5333] (\mathcal R_{\mathrm{rep}}) is the replay/pathing family,
[P5334] (\mathcal S_{\mathrm{seed}}) is the address-seed family.
[P5335] The central thesis of Appendix E is:
[P5336] [\boxed{\text{The lifted crystal is lawful only when every cell, block, district, and replay trace is addressable by one canonical base-4 geometry in which prefixes determine region identity, suffixes determine local refinement, and addresses preserve both location and generative ancestry.}}]
[P5337] E.1 Cell address law
[P5338] For a board of order (4^m), every row and column index has a unique base-4 expansion:[r=(r_{m-1}\dots r_0)4,\qquadc=(c{m-1}\dots c_0)_4,\qquadr_t,c_t\in{0,1,2,3}.]The current 256 Crystal branch treats this full digit word, not the undifferentiated pair ((r,c)), as the lawful cell address. In the branch’s own exact phrasing, “a cell is the full digit string.”
[P5339] Define the canonical cell address by[\mathcal A_m(r,c)=\bigl((r_{m-1},c_{m-1});(r_{m-2},c_{m-2});\dots;(r_0,c_0)\bigr).]This is the branch-canonical location body of a visible crystal cell. It is already enough to recover:
[P5340] the cell’s place in the recursive lift chain,
[P5341] the full block ancestry of the cell,
[P5342] the digitwise kernel evaluations that will determine its value.
[P5343] A deeper support branch gives a more implementation-facing statement through HoloAddress grammar: addresses must be deterministic, self-delimiting, prefix-stable, and reconstructive. While that support branch is broader than the 256 Crystal manuscript, it confirms the same underlying requirement: a lawful crystal address is not an arbitrary label but a reproducible coordinate object.
[P5344] The governing laws are:
[P5345] Cell Address Law.Every visible crystal cell is canonically identified by its full base-4 row/column digit word.
[P5346] Deterministic Address Law.The same crystal point may not admit several unrelated canonical address forms.
[P5347] Kernel pseudocode
[P5348] record CellAddress:
[P5349] row_digits
[P5350] col_digits
[P5351] scale
[P5352] truth_stage
[P5353] function BuildCellAddress(r, c, m):
[P5354] row_digits = Base4Digits(r, m)
[P5355] col_digits = Base4Digits(c, m)
[P5356] return CellAddress(row_digits, col_digits, m, "OK")
[P5357] E.2 4-block address law
[P5358] A block of side (4) inside a (4^m)-board is determined by the first (m-1) row digits and the first (m-1) column digits. The current extraction corpus gives this explicitly as part of the exact location hierarchy: “a 4×4 block is determined by the first ((m-1)) digits.”
[P5359] Define the 4-block address by
[P5360] [
[P5361] \mathrm{Blk}_{m,1}(r,c)
[P5362] (r_{m-1}\dots r_1,\ c_{m-1}\dots c_1).]The final suffix digits ((r_0,c_0)) then range over (\mathbb Z_4^2) and enumerate the sixteen cells inside that seed-sized chamber.
[P5363] This law is significant because it makes every visible (4\times4) descendant block an addressed seed chamber rather than only a local patch. The root kernel survives at every scale not only in values but in address structure.
[P5364] The governing law is:
[P5365] 4-Block Address Law.Every (4\times4) descendant block is determined by one prefix level shorter than a full cell address.
[P5366] E.3 16-block address law
[P5367] A block of side (16) inside a (4^m)-board is determined by the first (m-2) row and column digits. The current extraction corpus states this explicitly: “a 16×16 block [is determined] by the first ((m-2)) digits.”
[P5368] Define the 16-block address by
[P5369] [
[P5370] \mathrm{Blk}_{m,2}(r,c)
[P5371] (r_{m-1}\dots r_2,\ c_{m-1}\dots c_2).]The suffix[(r_1,r_0;\ c_1,c_0)]then indexes the (16\times16) local subcrystal.
[P5372] This is the first truly mesoscopic address unit of the visible crystal. It is large enough to carry two full levels of recursive bloom, but still small enough to remain entirely governed by only two suffix digit-pairs. The support branch’s language of prefix stability and streamed decode applies directly here: a 16-block is what is fixed when the first two digit layers are known and the final two are left unresolved.
[P5373] The governing law is:
[P5374] 16-Block Address Law.Every (16\times16) block is identified by fixing all but the last two row/column digit pairs.
[P5375] E.4 64-block address law
[P5376] At the (256\times256) scale, the current branch gives the 64-block law in exact form:[\text{64-block}:(r_3,c_3).]More generally, a (64\times64) block inside a (4^m)-board is determined by the first (m-3) row and column digits. For the visible (256)-board where (m=4), this reduces to one outer digit-pair.
[P5377] Define the 64-block address by
[P5378] [
[P5379] \mathrm{Blk}_{m,3}(r,c)
[P5380] (r_{m-1}\dots r_3,\ c_{m-1}\dots c_3).]For (m=4):[\mathrm{Blk}_{4,3}(r,c)=(r_3,c_3).]
[P5381] This law is the first visible “district map” of the 256 board. The board splits into 16 macro-districts, each governed by the high-order seed digit (L_4(r_3,c_3)-1). This is the first place where address geometry becomes obviously metro-like.
[P5382] The governing law is:
[P5383] 64-Block Address Law.At (L_{256}), the outermost district partition is indexed by the first row/column base-4 digit pair.
[P5384] E.5 Board identity law
[P5385] The current branch explicitly states that the board identity is the empty prefix:[\mathrm{BoardAddr}=\varnothing.]This means the whole crystal is the zero-prefix object of the same address grammar. There is no separate “whole-board naming law” added from outside. The full board is simply the unique region in which no prefix constraint has yet been imposed.
[P5386] Define the board identity by[\mathrm{Blk}_{m,m}(r,c)=\varnothing.]This is the canonical address of the whole (4^m\times4^m) board.
[P5387] The support branch on addressed holography reinforces the same logic at a more abstract level: the atlas page is finite, but infinite depth is realized by prefix-closed addressing and incremental refinement. The empty prefix is therefore the exact lawful top of the hierarchy.
[P5388] The governing laws are:
[P5389] Board Identity Law.The whole crystal is the unique empty-prefix region of the base-4 address grammar.
[P5390] No Extra-Whole Law.The whole board is not an external object above the address system; it is the top node of that system itself.
[P5391] E.6 Prefix retrieval
[P5392] The current live appendix role explicitly names prefix retrieval, and the support corpus on addressed holography sharpens it as prefix stability and random access under incomplete materialization. Prefix retrieval is therefore the operation that maps a full address to a coarser region by truncating suffix digits while preserving lawful block identity.
[P5393] Define the prefix-retrieval operator by[\mathcal P_{\mathrm{pref}}:\mathcal A_m(r,c)\mapsto \mathrm{Blk}_{m,k}(r,c),\qquad 0\le k\le m.]Operationally, this means:
[P5394] to retrieve a 64-block from a cell in (L_{256}), keep only ((r_3,c_3)),
[P5395] to retrieve a 16-block, keep ((r_3,c_3;r_2,c_2)),
[P5396] to retrieve a 4-block, keep ((r_3,c_3;r_2,c_2;r_1,c_1)).
[P5397] Because the live branch’s location law and value law are dual, prefix retrieval also retrieves the high-order transform-state digits implicitly fixed by that prefix. Thus a prefix is not merely a spatial query. It is also a partial semantic state.
[P5398] The governing laws are:
[P5399] Prefix Retrieval Law.Every lawful coarse retrieval in the crystal is performed by address truncation to a prefix.
[P5400] Prefix Stability Law.A lawful refinement may add suffix structure but may not invalidate a fixed prefix.
[P5401] E.7 Suffix reconstruction
[P5402] Dual to prefix retrieval is suffix reconstruction, explicitly named in the live Appendix E skeleton. Given a fixed prefix block, suffix reconstruction fills in the remaining local detail by varying the unresolved tail digits. This is the exact mechanism by which a lawful block can regrow its interior.
[P5403] Define the suffix-reconstruction operator by[\mathcal S_{\mathrm{suf}}:(\mathrm{Blk}_{m,k},u,v)\mapsto \mathcal A_m(r,c),]where (u,v\in\mathbb Z_4^k) are the suffix words completing the row and column.
[P5404] This is the same operational law as the support branch’s “tail refinement and depth control”: a prefix fixes the coherent partial structure, and additional tail digits refine it without rewriting the already-fixed prefix.
[P5405] The governing laws are:
[P5406] Suffix Reconstruction Law.Every lawful refinement of a crystal region occurs by appending suffix digits to a fixed prefix.
[P5407] No Prefix Rewrite Law.Suffix refinement may not alter the structure already fixed by the prefix.
[P5408] E.8 Block locality
[P5409] The current branch explicitly names block locality. Because the crystal is recursively generated, locality is not merely Euclidean closeness in the visible square. It is common ancestral prefix depth. Two points are locally close when they remain together until late in the recursive decomposition.
[P5410] Define the common-prefix depth of two addresses (\alpha,\beta) by[\lambda(\alpha,\beta)=\max{k:\mathrm{Pref}_k(\alpha)=\mathrm{Pref}k(\beta)}.]Then define block-locality class by[\mathcal L{\mathrm{blk}}(\alpha,\beta)=\lambda(\alpha,\beta).]
[P5411] This locality law is the direct exact version of the support corpus’s addressed-memory doctrine: locality lives in the address structure, and sparse residuals remain local because they occupy few locality blocks.
[P5412] The governing law is:
[P5413] Block Locality Law.The crystal’s native locality is prefix locality, not merely coordinate distance.
[P5414] E.9 Neighborhood metrics
[P5415] The live skeleton explicitly names neighborhood metrics. Since locality is prefix-based, the native address metric is naturally defined from common-prefix depth. Let (\alpha,\beta) be canonical crystal addresses. Then define[d_{\mathrm{pref}}(\alpha,\beta)=4^{-\lambda(\alpha,\beta)},]where (\lambda(\alpha,\beta)) is their common-prefix depth.
[P5416] This metric has the desired properties:
[P5417] equal addresses give distance (0) in the induced identification,
[P5418] deeper shared prefixes imply smaller distance,
[P5419] coarse district separation gives large distance.
[P5420] A second lawful metric is the visible coordinate metric[d_{\mathrm{vis}}((r,c),(r',c'))=|r-r'|+|c-c'|,]but the branch’s support documents imply that prefix locality is the more native metric because it is the one preserved under reconstruction, compression, and random access.
[P5421] The governing laws are:
[P5422] Neighborhood Metric Law.A lawful crystal metric must respect the recursive prefix hierarchy.
[P5423] Dual Metric Law.Visible metric and prefix metric may coexist, but prefix metric is the native reconstruction metric of the branch.
[P5424] E.10 Update transport
[P5425] The live skeleton explicitly names update transport. This means AppE must formalize how an address-bearing crystal object can be updated without losing its lawful location identity. The support corpus on addressed carriers and diffs states this sharply: updates should primarily modify sparse residuals, while the generator and address body remain stable; diffs are versioned; audit trails preserve exact change history.
[P5426] Define the update transport by[\mathcal U_{\mathrm{addr}}:(\mathcal A,\Delta r)\mapsto (\mathcal A,r\oplus \Delta r),]where:
[P5427] (\mathcal A) is the canonical address body,
[P5428] (r) is the current residual shell,
[P5429] (\Delta r) is the sparse update,
[P5430] (\oplus) is the deterministic merge law.
[P5431] In exceptional cases, the generator itself may change:[(g_{t+1},r_{t+1})=(g_t\oplus\Delta g_t,\ r_t\oplus\Delta r_t),]but the support corpus explicitly says generator rewrites should be rare relative to residual updates.
[P5432] The governing laws are:
[P5433] Update Transport Law.Lawful update preserves the address body and modifies residual or generator state through typed diff transport.
[P5434] Sparse Update Law.Updates should localize in residual shells whenever possible.
[P5435] E.11 Address normalization
[P5436] The live skeleton names address normalization, and the broader address-support corpus treats canonical self-delimiting representation, deterministic naming, and reproducible reconstruction as essential. Therefore AppE defines the address normalizer[\mathcal N_{\mathrm{addr}}:\mathcal A_{\mathrm{raw}}\to \mathcal A_{\mathrm{canon}}.]
[P5437] For the 256 Crystal branch, the canonical address form is:[\Xi_m(r,c)=\Bigl[(r_{m-1},c_{m-1})\mid\dots\mid(r_0,c_0)\Bigr].]Any shorthand, local alias, block-relative description, or compressed route notation must normalize to that full base-4 coordinate packet or to a typed prefix block derived from it.
[P5438] The normalizer must satisfy[\mathcal N_{\mathrm{addr}}(\mathcal N_{\mathrm{addr}}(x))=\mathcal N_{\mathrm{addr}}(x).]
[P5439] The laws are:
[P5440] Address Normalization Law.Every lawful address representation must reduce to one canonical coordinate packet.
[P5441] Idempotence Law.Normalizing twice may not change the result.
[P5442] E.12 Address hashes
[P5443] The live skeleton explicitly names address hashes. Since the crystal is replayable and audit-bearing, every strong address object must admit a digest that ties:
[P5444] its canonical coordinate body,
[P5445] its scale,
[P5446] its optional generator/residual shell,
[P5447] and its reconstruction regimeinto one stable fingerprint.
[P5448] Define the address hash by
[P5449] [
[P5450] H_E
[P5451] \mathrm{Hash}\bigl(\mathcal N_{\mathrm{addr}}(\mathcal A),g,r,\mathcal R_{\mathrm{regime}}\bigr).]
[P5452] This hash is not only for storage. It is used to:
[P5453] verify that an address has not drifted,
[P5454] connect replay artifacts to exact locations,
[P5455] bind update diffs to precise locality,
[P5456] support route auditing.
[P5457] The support corpus’s insistence on deterministic addressing, hash derivation, audit trails, and proof-carrying storage directly justifies this object.
[P5458] The law is:
[P5459] Address Hash Law.Every strong crystal address must admit a stable hash tied to its canonical form and reconstruction regime.
[P5460] E.13 Route hooks
[P5461] The live skeleton next names route hooks. This is where address law becomes routing law. The support metro corpus states that the manuscript is navigable by deterministic routing, that addresses are route anchors, and that custom path reading and replay reading are legitimate regimes. In the 256 Crystal branch, route hooks are the points where an address enters:
[P5462] a block-retrieval route,
[P5463] a transform route,
[P5464] a hyperlift route,
[P5465] a metro route,
[P5466] a replay route.
[P5467] Define the route-hook object by
[P5468] [
[P5469] h
[P5470] (\mathrm{HID},\mathcal A,\mathrm{RouteClass},\mathrm{EntryConditions},\mathrm{ExitConditions},\Theta_h),]where:
[P5471] (\mathcal A) is the address or block prefix,
[P5472] (\mathrm{RouteClass}) specifies the route type,
[P5473] entry and exit conditions state when this address can be used as a route anchor.
[P5474] Thus an address is no longer only a location key. It is a lawful launch point into the crystal’s own traversal grammar.
[P5475] The law is:
[P5476] Route Hook Law.A lawful crystal address may serve as a typed route anchor into retrieval, transform, metro, or replay flow.
[P5477] E.14 Location proofs
[P5478] The live skeleton requires location proofs. A location proof is the exact object showing that:
[P5479] a visible point belongs to a specific block lineage,
[P5480] its prefix hierarchy is correct,
[P5481] its digitwise coordinate law is lawful,
[P5482] its location is compatible with the seed generation law.
[P5483] Define the location-proof object by
[P5484] [
[P5485] \pi_E
[P5486] (\mathrm{PID},\mathrm{TargetRef},\mathcal A,\mathrm{PrefixLineage},\mathrm{ValueConsistency},\Theta_\pi),]where:
[P5487] (\mathcal A) is the canonical address,
[P5488] (\mathrm{PrefixLineage}) is the block ancestry,
[P5489] (\mathrm{ValueConsistency}) checks compatibility with the digitwise value theorem.
[P5490] This is the exact local proof surface of Chapter 5’s address theorem.
[P5491] The law is:
[P5492] Location Proof Law.Every strong claim about where a crystal object lives must be supported by a prefix-lineage and value-consistency proof.
[P5493] E.15 Replay pathing
[P5494] The live skeleton explicitly names replay pathing. This is the route by which an address-bearing object is reconstructed. The support corpus on replayable reconstruction, generator-plus-residual storage, and versioned diffs makes the replay law explicit:
[P5495] an address plus generator must reconstruct the lawful carrier,
[P5496] residuals refine it without invalidating the prefix,
[P5497] replay traces must show how the object was recovered.
[P5498] Define the replay-path object by
[P5499] [
[P5500] \rho_E
[P5501] (\mathrm{AddressRef},\mathrm{GeneratorRef},\mathrm{ResidualRef},\mathrm{DecodeTrace},\mathrm{ExpectedObject},\Theta_\rho).]
[P5502] A lawful replay path therefore performs:
[P5503] normalize address,
[P5504] retrieve or instantiate generator,
[P5505] apply suffix reconstruction,
[P5506] apply sparse residuals,
[P5507] certify resulting object.
[P5508] The law is:
[P5509] Replay Pathing Law.Every lawful crystal address must support a replay path from canonical coordinates to reconstructed object.
[P5510] E.16 Address seed
[P5511] The final macro-cell is the address seed. Appendix E must compress its whole law into a replay-bearing seed:
[P5512] [
[P5513] \zeta_E
[P5514] (g_E,r_E,\eta_E,\rho_E,\Theta_E),]where:
[P5515] (g_E) is the generator core of the address grammar,
[P5516] (r_E) is the residual shell of variant or bounded location regimes,
[P5517] (\eta_E) is the address-identity digest,
[P5518] (\rho_E) is the replay/regrowth bundle.
[P5519] This address seed can regenerate:
[P5520] the cell-address law,
[P5521] the 4/16/64-block hierarchy,
[P5522] board identity,
[P5523] prefix and suffix operators,
[P5524] locality metrics,
[P5525] normalization,
[P5526] route hooks,
[P5527] location proofs,
[P5528] replay pathing.
[P5529] The final theorem of Appendix E is therefore:
[P5530] [\boxed{\text{The base-4 address and location calculus is fully lawful only when cell addresses, block prefixes, locality metrics, normalization, hashes, route hooks, location proofs, replay paths, and address seeds form one coherent replayable geometry of location.}}]
[P5531] E.17 Canonical algorithmic form
[P5532] from dataclasses import dataclass
[P5533] from typing import List, Tuple, Dict, Any
[P5534] def base4_digits(x: int, m: int) -> List[int]:
[P5535] out = [0] * m
[P5536] for i in range(m):
[P5537] out[i] = x % 4
[P5538] x //= 4
[P5539] return list(reversed(out))
[P5540] @dataclass
[P5541] class CellAddress:
[P5542] row_digits: List[int]
[P5543] col_digits: List[int]
[P5544] scale: int
[P5545] truth_stage: str
[P5546] @dataclass
[P5547] class ReplayPath:
[P5548] address_ref: Any
[P5549] generator_ref: Any
[P5550] residual_ref: Any
[P5551] decode_trace: List[Dict[str, Any]]
[P5552] expected_object: Any
[P5553] truth_stage: str
[P5554] def build_cell_address(r: int, c: int, m: int) -> CellAddress:
[P5555] return CellAddress(
[P5556] row_digits=base4_digits(r, m),
[P5557] col_digits=base4_digits(c, m),
[P5558] scale=m,
[P5559] truth_stage="OK"
[P5560] )
[P5561] def block_prefix(r: int, c: int, m: int, k: int) -> Tuple[List[int], List[int]]:
[P5562] # block side = 4**k
[P5563] row_digits = base4_digits(r, m)
[P5564] col_digits = base4_digits(c, m)
[P5565] return row_digits[:m-k], col_digits[:m-k]
[P5566] def replay_path(address: CellAddress, generator_ref: str, residual_ref: str) -> ReplayPath:
[P5567] trace = [
[P5568] {"step": "normalize", "row_digits": address.row_digits, "col_digits": address.col_digits},
[P5569] {"step": "load_generator", "generator_ref": generator_ref},
[P5570] {"step": "apply_suffix_refinement", "residual_ref": residual_ref}
[P5571] ]
[P5572] return ReplayPath(
[P5573] address_ref=address,
[P5574] generator_ref=generator_ref,
[P5575] residual_ref=residual_ref,
[P5576] decode_trace=trace,
[P5577] expected_object="crystal_region_or_cell",
[P5578] truth_stage="OK"
[P5579] )
[P5580] This canonical form compresses the appendix’s true law: every crystal object is reached through a canonical base-4 address, every block is a prefix, and every lawful replay path reconstructs the object from address, generator, and residual shell.
[P5581] E.18 Appendix-level laws
[P5582] Cell Address Law — every crystal cell is canonically identified by its full base-4 row/column word.
[P5583] 4-Block Address Law — every (4\times4) descendant block is identified by one shorter prefix level.
[P5584] 16-Block Address Law — every (16\times16) block is identified by two unresolved suffix levels.
[P5585] 64-Block Address Law — in (L_{256}), the outer district split is indexed by the first digit pair.
[P5586] Board Identity Law — the whole board is the empty-prefix object of the same grammar.
[P5587] Prefix Retrieval Law — lawful coarse access occurs by address truncation.
[P5588] Suffix Reconstruction Law — lawful refinement occurs by appending suffix digits.
[P5589] Block Locality Law — the native locality of the crystal is common-prefix depth.
[P5590] Neighborhood Metric Law — lawful crystal metrics must respect recursive prefix structure.
[P5591] Update Transport Law — lawful updates preserve the address body and change residual or generator shells explicitly.
[P5592] Address Normalization Law — all address forms must reduce to one canonical packet.
[P5593] Address Hash Law — strong address objects require stable digest forms.
[P5594] Route Hook Law — addresses serve as lawful anchors for route entry.
[P5595] Location Proof Law — location claims require prefix-lineage and value-consistency proof.
[P5596] Address Seed Law — the full address calculus must compress into a replay-bearing seed.
[P5597] E.19 Closing statement
[P5598] Appendix E defines the address grammar of the 256 Crystal branch. It turns the recursive lift law into an exact location calculus in which every cell is a base-4 address, every block is a prefix-defined region, every board is the empty-prefix whole, every refinement is suffix reconstruction, every locality relation is prefix depth, every update is a lawful transport over stable coordinates, and every replay path reconstructs the object from its address, generator, and sparse residual shell. This appendix is the exact support-layer counterpart to Chapter 5’s address geometry. Without Appendix E, the crystal would be generative but not navigable. With Appendix E, the crystal acquires its lawful map of place.
[P5599] Appendix E — Base-4 Address and Location Calculus
[P5600] Appendix F — Hyperaddress and Tensor Engine
[P5601] F.0 Appendix Function
[P5602] In the current live branch of The 256 Crystal Extraction, Appendix F is explicitly stabilized as “Hyperaddress and Tensor Engine.” Its 16 macro-cells are fixed as:
[P5603] 16-digit quaternary address law
[P5604] ((X,Y,Z,W)) decomposition
[P5605] Pairing schemes
[P5606] Eight-kernel tensorization
[P5607] ((L_4^{\otimes 8})) state law
[P5608] Hypercell state tuples
[P5609] Slice families
[P5610] Fiber laws
[P5611] Tensor channels
[P5612] Hyperstate metrics
[P5613] Tensor proofs
[P5614] Tensor defect bounds
[P5615] Replay bundles
[P5616] Runtime encoding
[P5617] Certificates
[P5618] Hyperseed.
[P5619] Appendix F is therefore the first appendix in the 256 Crystal branch where the visible (256\times256) board is no longer treated as the terminal crystal object. It becomes the gateway into the full (256^4) hypercrystal, whose exact coordinate law, tensor decomposition, and replay-bearing engine were already fixed in the branch’s deeper extraction pass. The core branch statements are explicit:[256^4=(4^4)^4=4^{16},\qquad\mathcal C_{256^4}=L_4^{\otimes 8},]and the full 4D coordinate law is given by the lifted quaternary embedding[(X,Y,Z,W)\in{0,\dots,255}^4,]with (X,Y) the visible coordinates and (Z,W) the lifted hidden coordinates. Appendix F is where those claims are made exact as appendix-level support law.
[P5620] The support corpus also sharpens why this appendix is necessary. The 256 Crystal branch’s own true-holographic encoding states that the whole treatise is seeded by a (4\times4) local–global kernel, lifted by exact base-4 substitution, then promoted into a 16-digit quaternary hyperaddress space in which every point carries:
[P5621] a location address,
[P5622] a transform state given by kernel application on digit-pairs.That is precisely the role of Appendix F: to formalize the higher-dimensional address engine beneath Chapters 6–9.
[P5623] Formally, define the Appendix F substrate by
[P5624] [
[P5625] \mathbb F_{\mathrm{hyper}}
[P5626] (\mathcal A_{16},\mathcal X_{4D},\mathcal P_{\mathrm{pair}},\mathcal T_{\otimes},\mathcal S_{\mathrm{state}},\mathcal F_{\mathrm{slice}},\mathcal C_{\mathrm{chan}},\mathcal R_{\mathrm{rep}},\mathcal S_{\mathrm{seed}}),]where:
[P5627] (\mathcal A_{16}) is the 16-digit quaternary address family,
[P5628] (\mathcal X_{4D}) is the hypercell family,
[P5629] (\mathcal P_{\mathrm{pair}}) is the kernel-pairing family,
[P5630] (\mathcal T_{\otimes}) is the tensorization family,
[P5631] (\mathcal S_{\mathrm{state}}) is the hyperstate family,
[P5632] (\mathcal F_{\mathrm{slice}}) is the slice/fiber family,
[P5633] (\mathcal C_{\mathrm{chan}}) is the tensor-channel family,
[P5634] (\mathcal R_{\mathrm{rep}}) is the replay and runtime family,
[P5635] (\mathcal S_{\mathrm{seed}}) is the hyperseed family.
[P5636] The central thesis of Appendix F is:
[P5637] [\boxed{\text{The full crystal is a lawful }16\text{-digit quaternary hyperaddress space whose hypercells are generated by eight applications of the canonical }4\times4\text{ seed kernel, and whose geometry, runtime, and replay law are all inherited from that tensor factorization.}}]
[P5638] F.1 16-digit quaternary address law
[P5639] The first macro-cell of Appendix F is the exact 16-digit quaternary address law. The current extraction branch already states the decisive identity[256^4=(4^4)^4=4^{16},]and explicitly interprets the full crystal as a 16-digit quaternary address space. This means that a point of the full hypercrystal is not “one large opaque coordinate.” It is a finite word in a 16-symbol quaternary tensor grammar.
[P5640] Define a hyperaddress by
[P5641] [
[P5642] \mathcal A_{16}(\chi)
[P5643] (x_3x_2x_1x_0;\ y_3y_2y_1y_0;\ z_3z_2z_1z_0;\ w_3w_2w_1w_0)4,]where[\chi=(X,Y,Z,W)\in{0,\dots,255}^4,]and[X=\sum{t=0}^{3}4^t x_t,\quadY=\sum_{t=0}^{3}4^t y_t,\quadZ=\sum_{t=0}^{3}4^t z_t,\quadW=\sum_{t=0}^{3}4^t w_t.]This is the canonical address body of the hypercrystal point.
[P5644] A lawful hyperaddress must therefore satisfy:
[P5645] each coordinate is a 4-digit base-4 word,
[P5646] the full point is exactly a 16-digit word,
[P5647] address decomposition is deterministic,
[P5648] normalization is replay-stable.
[P5649] The governing laws are:
[P5650] 16-Digit Address Law.Every hypercell of the full crystal is canonically identified by one 16-digit quaternary address word.
[P5651] No Opaque Hyperpoint Law.A lawful 4D crystal point must be decomposable into its full quaternary digit structure.
[P5652] Kernel pseudocode
[P5653] record HyperAddress16:
[P5654] x_digits
[P5655] y_digits
[P5656] z_digits
[P5657] w_digits
[P5658] truth_stage
[P5659] function BuildHyperAddress16(X, Y, Z, W):
[P5660] return HyperAddress16(
[P5661] Base4Digits(X, 4),
[P5662] Base4Digits(Y, 4),
[P5663] Base4Digits(Z, 4),
[P5664] Base4Digits(W, 4),
[P5665] "OK"
[P5666] )
[P5667] F.2 ((X,Y,Z,W)) decomposition
[P5668] The second macro-cell is the exact coordinate decomposition of the 4D crystal. The current branch’s preferred lifted quaternary coordinate law is:[X=r,\qquad Y=c,][Z=\sum_{t=0}^{3}4^t((r_t+c_t)\bmod 4),\qquadW=\sum_{t=0}^{3}4^t((r_t-c_t)\bmod 4),]where[r=(r_3r_2r_1r_0)_4,\qquad c=(c_3c_2c_1c_0)_4.]Thus:
[P5669] (X) is the visible row axis,
[P5670] (Y) is the visible column axis,
[P5671] (Z) is the lifted phase-sum / orbit axis,
[P5672] (W) is the lifted directional / difference / tunneling axis.
[P5673] This is not merely a coordinate change. It is the appendix-level support law for Chapter 6’s higher-dimensional projection. The visible (256\times256) board already determines two hidden coordinates. Therefore every visible cell of the board may be lifted canonically into a 4D hyperpoint.
[P5674] Define the decomposition object by
[P5675] [
[P5676] d
[P5677] (\mathrm{DID},X,Y,Z,W,\mathcal I_d,\Theta_d),]where (\mathcal I_d) is the invariant shell of the coordinate decomposition.
[P5678] The governing laws are:
[P5679] Axis Decomposition Law.A lawful 4D crystal point must decompose into two visible and two hidden quaternary coordinates.
[P5680] Lifted Hidden-Axis Law.The hidden coordinates (Z) and (W) are exact lifted descendants of the seed’s diagonal-class coordinates.
[P5681] F.3 Pairing schemes
[P5682] The third macro-cell is the pairing scheme family. The current extraction branch explicitly says that the 16 digits of the hyperaddress are grouped into eight kernel pairs, and gives a natural pairing:[(x_t,y_t),\qquad (z_t,w_t),\qquad t=0,1,2,3.]It also remarks that other lawful pairings exist, but that the visible/hidden split above is the cleanest canonical pairing.
[P5683] Define the canonical pairing family by[\mathcal P_{\mathrm{pair}}=\Bigl{(x_t,y_t),\ (z_t,w_t)\ :\ t=0,1,2,3\Bigr}.]
[P5684] This family is canonical for the current branch because:
[P5685] it respects the visible ((X,Y)) pair,
[P5686] it respects the hidden ((Z,W)) pair,
[P5687] it preserves the scale index (t),
[P5688] it gives the exact eightfold factorization required by (L_4^{\otimes 8}).
[P5689] Derived pairing schemes may permute these pairings or regroup the 16 digits differently, but only if:
[P5690] they preserve total cardinality,
[P5691] preserve replay equivalence,
[P5692] and admit a conjugacy back to the canonical pairing.
[P5693] The law is:
[P5694] Pairing Scheme Law.Every lawful hyperstate factorization must specify how the 16 quaternary digits are grouped into eight kernel pairs.
[P5695] Canonical Pairing Law.The preferred pairing of the current branch is the visible/hidden-by-scale pairing ((x_t,y_t),(z_t,w_t)).
[P5696] F.4 Eight-kernel tensorization
[P5697] The fourth macro-cell is the exact eight-kernel tensorization law. The current branch states this explicitly:[\mathcal C_{256^4}=L_4^{\otimes 8}.]This is not just a slogan. It is the closed-form generation law of the full hypercrystal.
[P5698] Given the pairing family (\mathcal P_{\mathrm{pair}}), define the tensorized crystal state by
[P5699] [
[P5700] \mathcal T_{\otimes}(\chi)
[P5701] \bigotimes_{t=0}^{3}L_4(x_t,y_t)\ \otimes\ \bigotimes_{t=0}^{3}L_4(z_t,w_t).]The order of tensor factors may be written canonically as[L_4(x_3,y_3)\otimes L_4(z_3,w_3)\otimes \cdots \otimes L_4(x_0,y_0)\otimes L_4(z_0,w_0),]or in another fixed order, provided the ordering convention is replay-stable.
[P5702] This law means the full crystal is not a new gigantic primitive. It is the exact tensor-lift of one small canonical seed.
[P5703] The governing laws are:
[P5704] Eight-Kernel Tensorization Law.The full (256^4) crystal is generated by eight lawful applications of the root kernel composed tensorially.
[P5705] No Untyped Hyperstate Law.A hyperstate may not be treated as lawful unless its tensor factorization is explicit.
[P5706] F.5 ((L_4^{\otimes 8})) state law
[P5707] The fifth macro-cell is the exact state law induced by the tensorization. The extraction branch states that, after grouping the digits into eight legal kernel pairs, the global transformed state is the eight-digit quaternary tuple
[P5708] [
[P5709] (v_7,\dots,v_0)4
[P5710] ]
[P5711] with each
[P5712] [
[P5713] v_t=L_4(r_t,c_t)-1
[P5714] ]
[P5715] under the relevant pairing. For the visible/hidden split this becomes
[P5716] [
[P5717] u_t=L_4(x_t,y_t)-1,\qquad
[P5718] v_t=L_4(z_t,w_t)-1,
[P5719] \qquad t=0,1,2,3.
[P5720] ]
[P5721] The full hyperstate is therefore
[P5722] [
[P5723] \Xi{\mathrm{state}}(\chi)
[P5724] (u_3,u_2,u_1,u_0;\ v_3,v_2,v_1,v_0)_4.]This is the appendix-level exact state tuple of the hypercell.
[P5725] The state law is what makes the higher crystal computationally tractable. One never needs to brute-force all (256^4) cells. One evaluates eight seed states and assembles the result.
[P5726] The law is:
[P5727] Hyperstate Law.The state of a hypercell is the eight-digit quaternary tuple produced by digitwise kernel evaluation on the canonical pairing family.
[P5728] F.6 Hypercell state tuples
[P5729] The sixth macro-cell formalizes the full hypercell state tuple. A lawful hypercell must carry:
[P5730] its 16-digit address,
[P5731] its 4D coordinate decomposition,
[P5732] its 8-factor tensor state,
[P5733] its invariant shell,
[P5734] its replay bundle.
[P5735] Define the hypercell tuple by
[P5736] [
[P5737] \chi
[P5738] (\mathcal A_{16},\Theta_{4D},\Xi_{\mathrm{state}},\mathcal I_\chi,\rho_\chi,\Theta_\chi),]where:
[P5739] (\mathcal A_{16}) is the 16-digit hyperaddress,
[P5740] (\Theta_{4D}=(X,Y,Z,W)),
[P5741] (\Xi_{\mathrm{state}}) is the tensor state tuple,
[P5742] (\mathcal I_\chi) is the hypercell invariant shell,
[P5743] (\rho_\chi) is the replay object,
[P5744] (\Theta_\chi) is the hypercell truth stage.
[P5745] This object is the first fully operational state carrier of the complete 4D crystal.
[P5746] The governing law is:
[P5747] Hypercell State Tuple Law.A lawful hypercell must be represented by an address–coordinate–state triple, not by a coordinate alone.
[P5748] F.7 Slice families
[P5749] The seventh macro-cell is the family of slices in the hypercrystal. The chapter skeleton for the 256 Crystal branch already names “fibers, slices, and 3D visible shadows,” and Appendix F now formalizes the slice layer.
[P5750] A slice is obtained by fixing one or more coordinates:[X=X_0,\qquadY=Y_0,\qquadZ=Z_0,\qquadW=W_0,]or any conjunction thereof.
[P5751] Canonical slice classes include:
[P5752] (X)-slices,
[P5753] (Y)-slices,
[P5754] (Z)-slices,
[P5755] (W)-slices,
[P5756] bi-slices such as ((X,Y))-slices,
[P5757] hidden-sector slices such as ((Z,W))-slices.
[P5758] Define the slice family by
[P5759] [
[P5760] \mathcal F_{\mathrm{slice}}
[P5761] {\chi\in \mathcal X_{256^4}: \mathcal C_{\mathrm{fix}}(\chi)=\text{const}}.]
[P5762] The law is:
[P5763] Slice Law.A lawful slice of the hypercrystal is a coordinate-restricted submanifold determined by explicit fixed-coordinate constraints.
[P5764] F.8 Fiber laws
[P5765] Dual to slices are fibers. A fiber fixes all but one free coordinate. For example:[(X,Y,Z)=(X_0,Y_0,Z_0)]with (W) free yields a 1-dimensional fiber of length (256). Similarly, fixing ((Y,Z,W)) gives an (X)-fiber, and so on.
[P5766] Define the fiber family by
[P5767] [
[P5768] \mathcal F_{\mathrm{fib}}
[P5769] {\chi\in\mathcal X_{256^4}: \mathcal C_{\mathrm{fix}}(\chi)=\text{const},\ \mathcal C_{\mathrm{free}}(\chi)\ \text{varies}}.]
[P5770] Fibers are the canonical one-dimensional lanes of the hypercrystal. In the later metro and tunneling chapters, these become the simplest route carriers.
[P5771] The law is:
[P5772] Fiber Law.A lawful fiber of the hypercrystal is a coordinate lane with one free axis and all others pinned.
[P5773] F.9 Tensor channels
[P5774] The ninth macro-cell is the family of tensor channels. Once the hyperstate is recognized as (L_4^{\otimes 8}), movement in the crystal may act on one tensor factor, several tensor factors, or all of them in coordinated transport. The current branch’s chapter skeleton already names “tensor channels and state transport,” and the support extraction describes this as the higher-dimensional continuation of the seed’s transform algebra.
[P5775] Define the tensor-channel family by
[P5776] [
[P5777] \mathcal C_{\mathrm{chan}}
[P5778] {\Gamma_1,\dots,\Gamma_8},]with each (\Gamma_i) acting on one kernel factor, and with compound channels defined by tensor products or ordered compositions of the (\Gamma_i).
[P5779] This is the support-layer formalization of later “inference lanes” and “hidden-axis transport” in the body chapters.
[P5780] The law is:
[P5781] Tensor Channel Law.A lawful hypercrystal transport must declare which tensor factors are active and how their actions compose.
[P5782] F.10 Hyperstate metrics
[P5783] The tenth macro-cell is the family of hyperstate metrics. The current support branch already distinguishes visible metrics, orbit metrics, directional metrics, nexus metrics, and later tensor metrics. Appendix F gathers the exact higher-dimensional state metric layer.
[P5784] Canonical metrics include:
[P5785] address metric[d_{\mathrm{addr}}(\chi,\chi')=4^{-\lambda(\chi,\chi')},]where (\lambda) is common-prefix depth on the 16-digit word;
[P5786] coordinate metric[d_{4D}(\chi,\chi')=| (X,Y,Z,W)-(X',Y',Z',W') |_1]or another declared norm;
[P5787] tensor-state metric[d_{\otimes}(\chi,\chi')=\sum_{i=1}^{8} \delta_i,]where (\delta_i) measures factor mismatch;
[P5788] hidden-sector metricon the ((Z,W))-plane or its toroidal quotient.
[P5789] The law is:
[P5790] Hyperstate Metric Law.A lawful hypercrystal comparison must specify whether it is measuring address distance, coordinate distance, tensor-state distance, or hidden-sector distance.
[P5791] F.11 Tensor proofs
[P5792] The eleventh macro-cell is tensor proofs. Strong claims about the hypercrystal require proof objects showing:
[P5793] address legality,
[P5794] decomposition legality,
[P5795] pairing legality,
[P5796] tensor-state correctness,
[P5797] consistency with the branch’s recursive lift.
[P5798] Define the tensor-proof object by
[P5799] [
[P5800] \pi_F
[P5801] (\mathrm{PID},\mathrm{Claim},\Gamma,\mathrm{AddressRef},\mathrm{PairingRef},\mathrm{TensorStateRef},\Theta_\pi),]where:
[P5802] (\Gamma) is the assumption and operator set,
[P5803] the references identify the exact hypercell and factorization used.
[P5804] Typical proof classes include:
[P5805] exact hyperstate reconstruction,
[P5806] pairing-equivalence proof,
[P5807] slice/fiber law proof,
[P5808] tensor-channel legality proof,
[P5809] hyperaddress normalization proof.
[P5810] The law is:
[P5811] Tensor Proof Law.No strong hypercrystal claim is lawful without a typed tensor proof or proof-bearing certificate chain.
[P5812] F.12 Tensor defect bounds
[P5813] The twelfth macro-cell is the family of tensor defect bounds. Not every higher-dimensional comparison or transport is exact. The current branch already distinguishes exact and bounded transforms, and Appendix F extends that distinction to tensorized hyperstates.
[P5814] Define the tensor defect object by
[P5815] [
[P5816] \delta_F
[P5817] (\delta_1,\dots,\delta_8),]where (\delta_i) is the mismatch in factor (i). Aggregate defect may then be measured by[\Delta_F = \sum_{i=1}^{8}\delta_i]or another declared norm.
[P5818] Exact tensor equality requires[\Delta_F=0.]Bounded hyperstate equivalence requires[0<\Delta_F\le \tau_F.]
[P5819] The law is:
[P5820] Tensor Defect Law.A lawful nonexact hypercrystal relation must carry an explicit tensor defect bound.
[P5821] No Hidden Hyperdrift Law.Hyperstate mismatch may not be absorbed silently into the comparison.
[P5822] F.13 Replay bundles
[P5823] The thirteenth macro-cell is replay bundles. The branch repeatedly insists that no strong claim survives without replay, and this is especially critical in the higher-dimensional setting. A lawful hyperstate claim must emit:
[P5824] [
[P5825] \rho_F
[P5826] (\mathrm{AddressRef},\mathrm{DecompositionRef},\mathrm{PairingRef},\mathrm{TensorTrace},\mathrm{ExpectedState},\Theta_\rho).]
[P5827] A replay bundle for a hypercell must reconstruct:
[P5828] the 16-digit address,
[P5829] the ((X,Y,Z,W)) coordinates,
[P5830] the canonical pairing scheme,
[P5831] the eight kernel evaluations,
[P5832] the final hyperstate tuple.
[P5833] The law is:
[P5834] Hyperstate Replay Law.A strong hyperstate claim is incomplete until the full address-to-state path can be replayed deterministically.
[P5835] F.14 Runtime encoding
[P5836] The fourteenth macro-cell is runtime encoding. Appendix F is not only a static mathematical appendix; it supports the engine runtime used later by the extraction and metro systems.
[P5837] Define the runtime encoding object by
[P5838] [
[P5839] \mathcal R_{\mathrm{enc}}
[P5840] (\mathrm{InputMode},\mathrm{AddressMode},\mathrm{PairingMode},\mathrm{StateMode},\mathrm{OutputMode},\Theta_R).]
[P5841] Canonical runtime modes include:
[P5842] visible-board point mode,
[P5843] lifted ((X,Y,Z,W)) coordinate mode,
[P5844] canonical pairing mode,
[P5845] derived pairing mode,
[P5846] exact state mode,
[P5847] bounded comparison mode.
[P5848] This object ensures that runtime evaluation remains typed and reproducible.
[P5849] The law is:
[P5850] Runtime Encoding Law.Every lawful hypercrystal computation must declare its input, pairing, and output encoding modes explicitly.
[P5851] F.15 Certificates
[P5852] The fifteenth macro-cell is the general certificate family of Appendix F. A hyperstate certificate takes the form
[P5853] [
[P5854] C_F
[P5855] (\mathrm{CID},\mathrm{TargetRef},\mathrm{AddressProof},\mathrm{PairingProof},\mathrm{TensorProof},\delta_F,\rho_F,\Theta_F),]where:
[P5856] (\mathrm{AddressProof}) certifies the 16-digit address and 4D decomposition,
[P5857] (\mathrm{PairingProof}) certifies the tensor factorization,
[P5858] (\mathrm{TensorProof}) certifies the resulting state,
[P5859] (\delta_F) records defect,
[P5860] (\rho_F) is the replay bundle.
[P5861] This certificate is the support-layer closure object of the whole hyperaddress/tensor system.
[P5862] The law is:
[P5863] Hypercertificate Law.No strong hyperaddress or hyperstate claim is lawful without a certificate-bearing object.
[P5864] F.16 Hyperseed
[P5865] The final macro-cell is the hyperseed. Appendix F must compress its whole higher-dimensional grammar into a single seed:
[P5866] [
[P5867] \zeta_F
[P5868] (g_F,r_F,\eta_F,\rho_F,\Theta_F),]where:
[P5869] (g_F) is the generator core of the 16-digit address law and (L_4^{\otimes 8}) factorization,
[P5870] (r_F) is the residual shell of bounded or alternative pairing variants,
[P5871] (\eta_F) is the hyperaddress identity digest,
[P5872] (\rho_F) is the replay/regrowth bundle.
[P5873] This hyperseed can regenerate:
[P5874] the 16-digit quaternary address law,
[P5875] the ((X,Y,Z,W)) decomposition,
[P5876] the canonical and derived pairing families,
[P5877] the eight-kernel tensorization,
[P5878] hypercell state tuples,
[P5879] slice/fiber/tensor-channel logic,
[P5880] certificates and replay bundles.
[P5881] The final theorem of Appendix F is therefore:
[P5882] [\boxed{\text{The full hyperaddress and tensor engine is fully lawful only when its 16-digit address law, 4D coordinate decomposition, pairing schemes, }L_4^{\otimes 8}\text{ state law, hypercell tuples, slices, fibers, tensor channels, metrics, proofs, defect bounds, replay bundles, runtime encodings, certificates, and hyperseed form one coherent replayable higher-dimensional grammar.}}]
[P5883] F.17 Canonical algorithmic form
[P5884] from dataclasses import dataclass
[P5885] from typing import List, Tuple, Dict, Any
[P5886] L4 = [
[P5887] [1, 2, 3, 4],
[P5888] [3, 4, 1, 2],
[P5889] [4, 3, 2, 1],
[P5890] [2, 1, 4, 3],
[P5891] ]
[P5892] def base4_digits(x: int, m: int = 4) -> List[int]:
[P5893] out = [0] * m
[P5894] for i in range(m):
[P5895] out[i] = x % 4
[P5896] x //= 4
[P5897] return list(reversed(out))
[P5898] def l4_eval(a: int, b: int) -> int:
[P5899] return L4[a][b] - 1
[P5900] @dataclass
[P5901] class HyperCell:
[P5902] X: int
[P5903] Y: int
[P5904] Z: int
[P5905] W: int
[P5906] x_digits: List[int]
[P5907] y_digits: List[int]
[P5908] z_digits: List[int]
[P5909] w_digits: List[int]
[P5910] tensor_state: List[int]
[P5911] def hyper_decompose(r: int, c: int) -> Tuple[int, int, int, int]:
[P5912] r_digits = base4_digits(r, 4)
[P5913] c_digits = base4_digits(c, 4)
[P5914] z = sum((4 ** (3 - t)) * ((r_digits[t] + c_digits[t]) % 4) for t in range(4))
[P5915] w = sum((4 ** (3 - t)) * ((r_digits[t] - c_digits[t]) % 4) for t in range(4))
[P5916] return r, c, z, w
[P5917] def hyper_tensor_state(X: int, Y: int, Z: int, W: int) -> List[int]:
[P5918] x_digits = base4_digits(X, 4)
[P5919] y_digits = base4_digits(Y, 4)
[P5920] z_digits = base4_digits(Z, 4)
[P5921] w_digits = base4_digits(W, 4)
[P5922] state = []
[P5923] for t in range(4):
[P5924] state.append(l4_eval(x_digits[t], y_digits[t]))
[P5925] state.append(l4_eval(z_digits[t], w_digits[t]))
[P5926] return state
[P5927] def build_hypercell(r: int, c: int) -> HyperCell:
[P5928] X, Y, Z, W = hyper_decompose(r, c)
[P5929] return HyperCell(
[P5930] X=X,
[P5931] Y=Y,
[P5932] Z=Z,
[P5933] W=W,
[P5934] x_digits=base4_digits(X, 4),
[P5935] y_digits=base4_digits(Y, 4),
[P5936] z_digits=base4_digits(Z, 4),
[P5937] w_digits=base4_digits(W, 4),
[P5938] tensor_state=hyper_tensor_state(X, Y, Z, W),
[P5939] )
[P5940] This canonical form compresses the appendix’s exact law: the visible board coordinates are lifted into 4D hypercoordinates, the full hypercell becomes a 16-digit quaternary address, and its state is generated by eight lawful seed-kernel applications.
[P5941] F.18 Appendix-level laws
[P5942] 16-Digit Address Law — every hypercell is canonically a 16-digit quaternary word.
[P5943] Axis Decomposition Law — ((X,Y,Z,W)) is the exact 4D coordinate law of the lifted crystal.
[P5944] Pairing Scheme Law — hyperstate factorization requires explicit kernel pairing.
[P5945] Canonical Pairing Law — the visible/hidden-by-scale pairing is the preferred branch-canonical factorization.
[P5946] Eight-Kernel Tensorization Law — the full crystal is (L_4^{\otimes 8}).
[P5947] Hyperstate Law — every hypercell has an exact tensor state tuple.
[P5948] Hypercell State Tuple Law — a lawful hypercell includes address, coordinates, state, and replay bundle.
[P5949] Slice Law — lawful slices are coordinate-restricted submanifolds.
[P5950] Fiber Law — lawful fibers fix all but one axis.
[P5951] Tensor Channel Law — higher-dimensional movement acts through typed factor channels.
[P5952] Hyperstate Metric Law — address, coordinate, tensor, and hidden-sector metrics must be distinguished explicitly.
[P5953] Tensor Proof Law — strong hypercrystal claims require proof objects.
[P5954] Tensor Defect Law — bounded hyperstate mismatch must be explicit.
[P5955] Hyperstate Replay Law — strong hyperstate claims must replay from address to tensor state.
[P5956] Hyperseed Law — the full hyperaddress/tensor engine must compress into a replay-bearing seed.
[P5957] F.19 Closing statement
[P5958] Appendix F defines the full hyperaddress and tensor engine of the 256 Crystal branch. It is the appendix where the visible 256-board is rigorously recognized as the shadow of a 4D quaternary crystal, where every point is a 16-digit address, where hidden coordinates ((Z,W)) are made explicit, where the canonical pairing of those digits yields eight lawful applications of the root kernel, and where the entire higher-dimensional crystal is formalized as (L_4^{\otimes 8}). In its later macro-cells it equips that higher crystal with slices, fibers, tensor channels, metrics, proofs, defect bounds, replay bundles, runtime encodings, certificates, and a hyperseed. This appendix is therefore the exact support-layer realization of Chapter 6. Without Appendix F, the (256^4) hypercrystal would remain a branch-level theorem. With Appendix F, it becomes an explicit engine.
[P5959] Appendix F — Hyperaddress and Tensor Engine
[P5960] Appendix G — Symmetry Catalog and Automorphism Groups
[P5961] G.0 Appendix Function
[P5962] In the current live branch of The 256 Crystal Extraction, Appendix G is explicitly stabilized as “Symmetry Catalog and Automorphism Groups.” Its 16 macro-cells are fixed as:
[P5963] Row symmetry catalog
[P5964] Column symmetry catalog
[P5965] Diagonal duals
[P5966] Quadrant rotations
[P5967] Complement sectors
[P5968] Reversal sectors
