In geometric language, the 6-petal flower is a tensor product of the 2-petal and 3-petal flowers in which the two systems double-occupy angular slots and destroy the possibility of a lawful dual-diagonal closure.
[P7108] Define the order-6 obstruction object by
[P7109] [
[P7110] o_6
[P7111] (\mathrm{OID},n=6,\mathrm{ParityWitness},\mathrm{DiagonalFailure},\mathrm{NoGoClass},\Theta_{o_6}=\mathrm{FAIL}),]where:
[P7112] (\mathrm{ParityWitness}) is the mod-2 / mod-3 incompatibility,
[P7113] (\mathrm{DiagonalFailure}) is the impossibility of both diagonal permutations,
[P7114] (\mathrm{NoGoClass}) marks the branch as forbidden for strict full-DLS recursion.
[P7115] The governing laws are:
[P7116] Order-6 Obstruction Law.The (6\times6) case is a canonical obstruction class of the branch and not a missing construction.
[P7117] Minimal No-Go Law.Order (6) is the smallest order at which the branch’s full dual-diagonal closure provably breaks.
[P7118] J.2 Parity tangles
[P7119] The second macro-cell is the more general class of parity tangles. Order (6) is the canonical example, but the support corpus makes clear that the deeper obstruction is not the numeral 6 itself. It is the entanglement of incompatible parity systems inside one attempted branch. In the flower/addendum classification this is the “hexafolium tensor” where (2)-symmetry and (3)-symmetry are superposed so densely that petal identity collapses. In the toolkit classification this appears as the even–odd product class (n=2m) with (m) odd.
[P7120] Define a parity tangle by
[P7121] [
[P7122] p
[P7123] (\mathrm{PID},n,\mathcal P_2,\mathcal P_{\mathrm{odd}},\mathcal X_p,\Theta_p),]where:
[P7124] (\mathcal P_2) is the even-parity symmetry requirement,
[P7125] (\mathcal P_{\mathrm{odd}}) is the odd cyclicity requirement,
[P7126] (\mathcal X_p) is the incompatibility witness,
[P7127] (\Theta_p) is the branch truth stage.
[P7128] A parity tangle is present when the branch simultaneously demands:
[P7129] a complement-style pairing law from the 2-sector,
[P7130] an independent cyclic transport law from the odd sector,
[P7131] and a single exact diagonal closure satisfying both.
[P7132] The law is:
[P7133] Parity Tangle Law.A branch is parity-tangled when two or more modular flow systems impose incompatible diagonal or route constraints on the same carrier.
[P7134] Parity-Incompatibility Law.The obstruction is lawful only when it is shown by explicit modular contradiction, not by heuristic pattern discomfort.
[P7135] J.3 Composite diagonal failures
[P7136] The third macro-cell is composite diagonal failures. The universal toolkit gives the exact order-class taxonomy:
[P7137] prime orders (\ge 5): both diagonals valid,
[P7138] powers of 2: both diagonals valid,
[P7139] perfect square composites (9,25,\dots): one diagonal only,
[P7140] prime × power-of-2 composites (12,20,\dots): one diagonal only,
[P7141] even–odd products (6,10,14,\dots): both diagonals fail.
[P7142] This means composite behavior is not monolithic. The branch must distinguish at least three composite diagonal failure classes:
[P7143] Partial-diagonal composite[\Theta=\mathrm{NEAR},]where one diagonal survives but not both.
[P7144] Dual-failure composite[\Theta=\mathrm{FAIL},]where neither diagonal survives.
[P7145] Bounded composite workaroundwhere a strict both-diagonal DLS fails but a nonstrict or one-diagonal object remains lawful.
[P7146] Define the composite diagonal-failure object by
[P7147] [
[P7148] c
[P7149] (\mathrm{CID},n,\mathrm{CompositeClass},\mathrm{MainDiagStatus},\mathrm{AntiDiagStatus},\Theta_c).]
[P7150] The law is:
[P7151] Composite Diagonal Failure Law.Composite orders must be typed by the exact status of both diagonals rather than treated as uniformly successful or uniformly impossible.
[P7152] One-Diagonal Salvage Law.Some composite orders remain lawful as partial branches because exactly one diagonal survives.
[P7153] J.4 Local holography collapse
[P7154] The fourth macro-cell is local holography collapse. Appendix A proved that the canonical (4\times4) seed contains seven distinguished (2\times2) holographic chambers each carrying the full tetradic alphabet. The current branch treats this as one of the defining local–global invariants of the stable branch. Therefore failure of local holography is one of the strongest indicators that a proposed exceptional object has left the lawful corridor.
[P7155] Define the local-holography object by
[P7156] [
[P7157] h
[P7158] (\mathrm{HID},\mathrm{RegionRef},\mathcal H_{\mathrm{present}},\mathcal H_{\mathrm{expected}},\delta_h,\Theta_h),]where:
[P7159] (\mathcal H_{\mathrm{present}}) counts or classifies the extant holographic windows,
[P7160] (\mathcal H_{\mathrm{expected}}) is the lawful reference count/class,
[P7161] (\delta_h) is the holography defect.
[P7162] A local holography collapse occurs when[\mathcal H_{\mathrm{present}} < \mathcal H_{\mathrm{expected}}]under the active invariant shell. At seed scale this means a loss of the seven-window local closure. At larger scales it means the recursive descendants are no longer lawful seed chambers.
[P7163] The governing laws are:
[P7164] Local Holography Law.A branch remains locally lawful only if its seed-chamber holography is preserved or explicitly bounded.
[P7165] Holography Collapse Law.If the branch can no longer preserve lawful local seed chambers, it exits the exact stable corridor.
[P7166] J.5 Nonrecursive lift failures
[P7167] The fifth macro-cell is nonrecursive lift failures. The stable branch is characterized by the exact substitution law
[P7168] [
[P7169] L_{4^m}\bigl(4^{m-1}i+r,\ 4^{m-1}j+s\bigr)
[P7170] 4^{m-1}(L_4(i,j)-1)+L_{4^{m-1}}(r,s),]and the exact digitwise value theorem derived from it. A branch suffers nonrecursive lift failure when no lawful seed-preserving substitution rule exists that propagates its local conditions to the next scale.
[P7171] Define the nonrecursive-lift object by
[P7172] [
[P7173] r
[P7174] (\mathrm{RID},\mathrm{BranchRef},\mathrm{LiftAttempt},\mathrm{BrokenRecurrence},\mathrm{FailureWitness},\Theta_r).]
[P7175] This failure class is stronger than local defect. It says that the branch is not merely noisy at one scale; it cannot sustain a lawful tower of recursive descendants.
[P7176] Canonical reasons include:
[P7177] parity tangles,
[P7178] unpreservable diagonals,
[P7179] nonfactorable block law,
[P7180] address/value nonalignment,
[P7181] replay instability across scales.
[P7182] The law is:
[P7183] Nonrecursive Lift Law.A branch is recursively unlawful when no exact or bounded block-substitution law preserves its active invariants across scales.
[P7184] J.6 Stability fractures
[P7185] The sixth macro-cell is stability fractures. A stability fracture is a branch-local breakdown that does not necessarily destroy all structure at once, but does break one of the branch’s primary continuity conditions. Chapter 7 already named these as:
[P7186] broken diagonal structure,
[P7187] carry geometry failure,
[P7188] local/global inheritance collapse,
[P7189] parity tangles,
[P7190] branch fractures across scales. Appendix J now makes them explicit support objects.
[P7191] Define the stability-fracture object by
[P7192] [
[P7193] s
[P7194] (\mathrm{SID},\mathrm{TargetRef},\mathrm{FractureClass},\mathrm{AffectedInvariant},\mathrm{Scope},\Theta_s),]where fracture classes include:
[P7195] diagonal fracture,
[P7196] local-holography fracture,
[P7197] recursive-lift fracture,
[P7198] address-law fracture,
[P7199] replay fracture.
[P7200] A fracture differs from a total failure because some invariant shell may still survive. This is what later enables salvageability classification.
[P7201] The law is:
[P7202] Stability Fracture Law.A branch may suffer a lawful fracture in one invariant shell while retaining bounded structure in others.
[P7203] No Undifferentiated Failure Law.Fractures must be typed by the invariant they break and the scope they affect.
[P7204] J.7 Defect cascades
[P7205] The seventh macro-cell is defect cascades. A defect cascade occurs when one local fracture propagates into several other failure classes. This is already latent in the branch:
[P7206] a parity tangle can destroy both diagonals,
[P7207] diagonal failure can break recursive lift,
[P7208] broken lift can invalidate address law,
[P7209] broken address law can prevent replay closure,
[P7210] replay failure can force downgrade or quarantine.Appendix J now formalizes this propagation chain.
[P7211] Define the defect-cascade object by
[P7212] [
[P7213] d
[P7214] (\mathrm{DID},\mathrm{RootDefect},\mathrm{PropagationChain},\mathrm{BlastRadius},\Theta_d),]where:
[P7215] (\mathrm{RootDefect}) is the initiating failure,
[P7216] (\mathrm{PropagationChain}) is the ordered list of induced failures,
[P7217] (\mathrm{BlastRadius}) is the structural scope of the cascade.
[P7218] The governing laws are:
[P7219] Defect Cascade Law.A defect cascade is lawful only when the propagation from root failure to downstream fracture is explicit and replayable.
[P7220] Blast Radius Law.Every serious exceptional branch claim must specify how far the failure propagates.
[P7221] J.8 Forbidden transforms
[P7222] The eighth macro-cell is forbidden transforms. Appendix B catalogued the lawful primitive transforms of the seed branch. Appendix J now defines when a transform becomes forbidden:
[P7223] it breaks both diagonals in a corridor that requires them,
[P7224] it violates the active branch-corridor budget,
[P7225] it exits the branch’s allowed factorization class,
[P7226] it produces unreplayable drift,
[P7227] it crosses a no-go lift boundary.
[P7228] Define the forbidden-transform object by
[P7229] [
[P7230] f
[P7231] (\mathrm{FID},\mathrm{TransformRef},\mathrm{TargetBranch},\mathrm{ForbiddenReason},\mathrm{NoGoWitness},\Theta_f=\mathrm{FAIL}).]
[P7232] Examples include:
[P7233] attempts to import 6-power dual-failure behavior into the exact recursive branch,
[P7234] transforms that preserve visible Latinity but destroy hidden diagonal or replay law,
[P7235] lifts that appear geometrically plausible but have no legal tensor or block decomposition.
[P7236] The law is:
[P7237] Forbidden Transform Law.A transform is forbidden when it cannot preserve the active branch’s required invariant shell under the declared corridor.
[P7238] J.9 Salvageable exceptions
[P7239] The ninth macro-cell is salvageable exceptions. The branch does not treat every exception as equally terminal. The flower/addendum taxonomy explicitly states that many composites retain enough separation to salvage one diagonal, even when both-diagonal closure fails. Likewise the universal toolkit gives whole classes with one surviving diagonal. These are lawful partial or bounded branches.
[P7240] Define the salvageable-exception object by
[P7241] [
[P7242] s
[P7243] (\mathrm{SID},\mathrm{BranchRef},\mathrm{SurvivingInvariantSet},\mathrm{AllowedCorridor},\mathrm{RepairHooks},\Theta_s),]where:
[P7244] (\mathrm{SurvivingInvariantSet}) identifies what remains lawful,
[P7245] (\mathrm{AllowedCorridor}) is typically bounded or probe,
[P7246] (\mathrm{RepairHooks}) states how the branch can be used, studied, or upgraded.
[P7247] Canonical salvageable exception classes include:
[P7248] one-diagonal composites,
[P7249] bounded local-holography survivors,
[P7250] branches lawful only for probe or comparison,
[P7251] projected/fibered reinterpretations of a failed strict branch.
[P7252] The last class is supported by the “6D [work]” document, which explicitly distinguishes strict diagonal-Latin 6 (parity-clashing and thus no-go) from a projected/fibered 6D object built as a 4D nested tesseract plus a (3\times2) fiber. That means “6” is not absolutely dead across the whole corpus. It is dead as a strict both-diagonal DLS primitive, but it may be salvageable in a different typed regime.
[P7253] The law is:
[P7254] Salvageability Law.An exception is salvageable only if its surviving invariant shell, admissible corridor, and replay obligations are explicit.
[P7255] Boundaries of salvage
[P7256] Salvage does not mean reclassifying a forbidden branch as stable. It means:
[P7257] bounded use,
[P7258] partial structure retention,
[P7259] alternate projection regime,
[P7260] or typed diagnostic value.
[P7261] Thus the 6-case is the canonical demonstration of branch-sensitive salvage:
[P7262] strict diagonal-Latin 6: forbidden,
[P7263] projected 6D extension of 4D: potentially lawful under a different branch grammar.
[P7264] J.10 Nonsalvageable exceptions
[P7265] The tenth macro-cell is nonsalvageable exceptions. These are branches for which:
[P7266] no core invariant shell survives,
[P7267] no bounded corridor remains lawful,
[P7268] no replay-closed workaround exists,
[P7269] no alternate branch projection yields a meaningful reduction.
[P7270] Define the nonsalvageable-exception object by
[P7271] [
[P7272] n
[P7273] (\mathrm{NID},\mathrm{BranchRef},\mathrm{DestroyedInvariantSet},\mathrm{NoRepairClass},\Theta_n=\mathrm{FAIL}).]
[P7274] A branch is nonsalvageable when the failure is not only local or bounded but annihilates the branch’s defining law. For example:
[P7275] if both diagonal legality and recursive factorization fail irreparably,
[P7276] if no one-diagonal or alternate projection regime survives,
[P7277] if route, replay, and witness closure all break.
[P7278] The law is:
[P7279] Nonsalvageability Law.An exception is nonsalvageable when no lawful corridor remains and no alternate branch interpretation preserves a sufficient invariant shell.
[P7280] J.11 Diagnostic metrics
[P7281] The eleventh macro-cell is diagnostic metrics. Appendix I already defined corridor metrics for branch admissibility. Appendix J specializes that to failure analysis. The support corpus already supplies the exact diagnostic variables:
[P7282] diagonal survival,
[P7283] parity obstruction,
[P7284] local holography retention,
[P7285] recursive-lift viability,
[P7286] route legality,
[P7287] replay sufficiency.
[P7288] Define the diagnostic metric object by
[P7289] [
[P7290] m
[P7291] (\mathrm{MID},\mathrm{TargetBranch},\delta_m,\pi_m,\eta_m,\rho_m,\Theta_m),]where:
[P7292] (\delta_m) measures branch defect,
[P7293] (\pi_m) measures parity or obstruction load,
[P7294] (\eta_m) measures holography or inherited-structure retention,
[P7295] (\rho_m) measures replay sufficiency.
[P7296] A branch diagnosis may then be aggregated by a branch-specific defect functional
[P7297] [
[P7298] \mathcal D_{\mathrm{branch}}
[P7299] \alpha,\delta_m+\beta,\pi_m-\gamma,\eta_m-\lambda,\rho_m.]
[P7300] The law is:
[P7301] Diagnostic Metric Law.Every exceptional branch must be measurable in terms of defect, obstruction, structural retention, and replay sufficiency.
[P7302] J.12 Counterexample proofs
[P7303] The twelfth macro-cell is counterexample proofs. Strong no-go or downgrade claims require explicit proof objects. The support corpus already provides the exact canonical counterexample:
[P7304] order-6 impossibility through parity contradiction. It also provides counterexample-style classes:
[P7305] composite orders with only one surviving diagonal,
[P7306] branches where hidden parity destroys visible legality.
[P7307] Define the counterexample-proof object by
[P7308] [
[P7309] \pi_J
[P7310] (\mathrm{PID},\mathrm{Claim},\Gamma,\mathrm{CounterexampleRef},\mathrm{BrokenInvariant},\Theta_\pi),]where:
[P7311] (\Gamma) is the assumption set,
[P7312] (\mathrm{CounterexampleRef}) is the explicit witness,
[P7313] (\mathrm{BrokenInvariant}) identifies what fails.
[P7314] The law is:
[P7315] Counterexample Proof Law.No impossibility or forbidden-branch claim is lawful without an explicit counterexample or obstruction proof.
[P7316] J.13 Quarantine classes
[P7317] The thirteenth macro-cell is quarantine classes. The typed-truth support architecture already names quarantine as the destination for fail-class objects. Appendix J now specializes that to exceptional branches. A quarantine class isolates a bad branch so that its defects do not pollute the stable recursive line.
[P7318] Define the quarantine-class object by
[P7319] [
[P7320] q
[P7321] (\mathrm{QID},\mathrm{BranchRef},\mathrm{RestrictionLevel},\mathrm{AllowedUses},\mathrm{BlockedUses},\Theta_q=\mathrm{FAIL}),]where:
[P7322] (\mathrm{RestrictionLevel}) may be observe-only, compare-only, counterexample-only, or no-return.
[P7323] Typical quarantine classes include:
[P7324] diagnostic quarantine,
[P7325] parity-obstruction quarantine,
[P7326] route-forbidden quarantine,
[P7327] permanent no-go quarantine.
[P7328] The law is:
[P7329] Quarantine Class Law.A failed branch must be isolated in a typed quarantine class rather than left to circulate implicitly.
[P7330] No Silent Leakage Law.A forbidden or unstable branch may not be used as if it were stable once quarantined.
[P7331] J.14 Receipts and logs
[P7332] The fourteenth macro-cell is receipts and logs. Every exceptional-branch event must emit:
[P7333] a receipt describing the obstruction,
[P7334] a log recording the route of the failure through the diagnostic system.
[P7335] Define the exception receipt by
[P7336] [
[P7337] R_J
[P7338] (\mathrm{RID},\mathrm{BranchRef},\mathrm{ExceptionClass},\mathrm{WitnessSet},\mathrm{CorridorStatus},\rho_R,\Theta_R),
[P7339] ]
[P7340] and the exception log by
[P7341] [
[P7342] L_J
[P7343] (\mathrm{EventHistory},\mathrm{DefectHistory},\mathrm{PromotionHistory},\mathrm{QuarantineHistory},\rho_L,\Theta_L).]
[P7344] These are what let later appendices, especially metrics, runtime, and proof-bundling appendices, treat exceptional cases as audit-ready rather than anecdotal.
[P7345] The law is:
[P7346] Exception Receipt Law.Every exceptional-branch event must emit a replay-bearing receipt and historical log.
[P7347] J.15 Replay bundles
[P7348] The fifteenth macro-cell is replay bundles. A replay bundle for Appendix J must reconstruct:
[P7349] the target branch and corridor,
[P7350] the witness set,
[P7351] the obstruction or defect metrics,
[P7352] the route or lift attempt,
[P7353] the resulting classification.
[P7354] Define the replay bundle by
[P7355] [
[P7356] \rho_J
[P7357] (\mathrm{BranchRef},\mathrm{CorridorRef},\mathrm{WitnessRefs},\mathrm{MetricRefs},\mathrm{AttemptTrace},\mathrm{ExpectedOutcome},\Theta_\rho).]
[P7358] The law is:
[P7359] Exception Replay Law.A strong exceptional-branch claim is incomplete until the obstruction and its classification can be replayed.
[P7360] No Memory-Only Failure Law.A failure remembered only narratively is not a lawful branch object.
[P7361] J.16 Exception seed
[P7362] The final macro-cell is the exception seed. Appendix J must compress the whole failure-side taxonomy into a seed:
[P7363] [
[P7364] \zeta_J
[P7365] (g_J,r_J,\eta_J,\rho_J,\Theta_J),]where:
[P7366] (g_J) is the generator core of exceptional-order law,
[P7367] (r_J) is the residual shell of bounded or unresolved failure structure,
[P7368] (\eta_J) is the exception-identity digest,
[P7369] (\rho_J) is the replay/regrowth bundle.
[P7370] This seed can regenerate:
[P7371] the order-6 obstruction,
[P7372] parity tangle classes,
[P7373] composite diagonal-failure classes,
[P7374] local holography collapse classes,
[P7375] nonrecursive-lift failures,
[P7376] stability fractures,
[P7377] defect cascades,
[P7378] forbidden transforms,
[P7379] salvage and nonsalvage classifications,
[P7380] diagnostics, counterexamples, quarantine classes, receipts, and replay bundles.
[P7381] The final theorem of Appendix J is therefore:
[P7382] [\boxed{\text{The exceptional-order grammar of the 256 Crystal branch is fully lawful only when obstructions, parity tangles, diagonal failures, holography collapses, nonrecursive lifts, stability fractures, defect cascades, forbidden transforms, salvageability classes, diagnostics, counterexamples, quarantines, receipts, replay bundles, and the exception seed form one coherent replayable failure taxonomy.}}]
[P7383] J.17 Canonical algorithmic form
[P7384] from dataclasses import dataclass, field
[P7385] from typing import Dict, Any, List, Literal
[P7386] TruthClass = Literal["OK", "NEAR", "AMBIG", "FAIL"]
[P7387] @dataclass
[P7388] class ExceptionCertificate:
[P7389] branch_ref: str
[P7390] exception_class: str
[P7391] witnesses: Dict[str, Any]
[P7392] defect_report: Dict[str, Any]
[P7393] truth: TruthClass
[P7394] replay_trace: List[str] = field(default_factory=list)
[P7395] def classify_exception(
[P7396] branch_ref: str,
[P7397] parity_tangle: bool,
[P7398] both_diagonals_fail: bool,
[P7399] replay_ok: bool,
[P7400] salvageable: bool,
[P7401] threshold: float,
[P7402] defect: float
[P7403] ) -> TruthClass:
[P7404] if parity_tangle and both_diagonals_fail:
[P7405] return "FAIL"
[P7406] if salvageable and defect <= threshold and replay_ok:
[P7407] return "NEAR"
[P7408] if not replay_ok:
[P7409] return "AMBIG"
[P7410] return "FAIL"
[P7411] def certify_exception(
[P7412] branch_ref: str,
[P7413] exception_class: str,
[P7414] witnesses: Dict[str, Any],
[P7415] defect_report: Dict[str, Any],
[P7416] salvageable: bool = False,
[P7417] threshold: float = 1e-9
[P7418] ) -> ExceptionCertificate:
[P7419] truth = classify_exception(
[P7420] branch_ref=branch_ref,
[P7421] parity_tangle=witnesses.get("parity_tangle", False),
[P7422] both_diagonals_fail=witnesses.get("both_diagonals_fail", False),
[P7423] replay_ok=witnesses.get("replay_ok", False),
[P7424] salvageable=salvageable,
[P7425] threshold=threshold,
[P7426] defect=defect_report.get("total_defect", 0.0),
[P7427] )
[P7428] return ExceptionCertificate(
[P7429] branch_ref=branch_ref,
[P7430] exception_class=exception_class,
[P7431] witnesses=witnesses,
[P7432] defect_report=defect_report,
[P7433] truth=truth,
[P7434] replay_trace=[branch_ref, exception_class]
[P7435] )
[P7436] This canonical form compresses the appendix’s law: classify the branch by typed obstruction witnesses, distinguish fail from bounded salvage, preserve replay sufficiency, and emit a replay-bearing exception certificate.
[P7437] J.18 Appendix-level laws
[P7438] Order-6 Obstruction Law — the (6\times6) case is the canonical parity-tangled no-go branch.
[P7439] Parity Tangle Law — incompatible modular flow systems create typed branch obstructions.
[P7440] Composite Diagonal Failure Law — composite orders must be classified by exact diagonal survival status.
[P7441] Local Holography Law — lawful branches preserve seed-chamber holography or explicitly bound its loss.
[P7442] Nonrecursive Lift Law — a branch is recursively unlawful when no exact or bounded lift law survives.
[P7443] Stability Fracture Law — branch failure may fracture one invariant shell while preserving others.
[P7444] Defect Cascade Law — branch failures propagate along explicit causality chains.
[P7445] Forbidden Transform Law — transforms that violate corridor invariants must be typed as forbidden.
[P7446] Salvageability Law — bounded lawful use requires an explicit surviving invariant shell.
[P7447] Nonsalvageability Law — some branches remain beyond lawful repair.
[P7448] Diagnostic Metric Law — failures must be measured, not just narrated.
[P7449] Counterexample Proof Law — impossibility claims require explicit obstruction proofs.
[P7450] Quarantine Class Law — failed branches must be isolated in typed fail regimes.
[P7451] Exception Receipt Law — every exceptional event must be logged and receipted.
[P7452] Exception Seed Law — the whole failure taxonomy must compress into a replay-bearing seed.
[P7453] J.19 Closing statement
[P7454] Appendix J defines the failure-side grammar of the 256 Crystal branch. It begins from the canonical order-6 obstruction and generalizes that into parity tangles, composite diagonal-failure classes, local holography collapse, nonrecursive lift failures, stability fractures, defect cascades, and forbidden transforms. It then distinguishes what may still be salvaged from what cannot, quantifies those distinctions through diagnostic metrics, anchors impossibility claims in counterexample proofs, isolates failed branches in quarantine classes, and closes the whole exceptional-order system with receipts, replay bundles, and an exception seed. This appendix is therefore the exact support-layer realization of the negative half of Chapter 7’s branch taxonomy. Without Appendix J, the crystal would know its lawful branch but not its lawful boundaries. With Appendix J, the crystal acquires its no-go grammar.
[P7455] Appendix J — Exceptional Orders, Parity Tangles, and Failure Cases
[P7456] Appendix K — Metrics, Defect Budgets, and Resonance Measures
[P7457] K.0 Appendix Function
[P7458] In the current live branch of The 256 Crystal Extraction, Appendix K is explicitly stabilized as “Metrics, Defect Budgets, and Resonance Measures.” Its 16 macro-cells are fixed as:
[P7459] Drift metrics
[P7460] Defect norms
[P7461] Symmetry scores
[P7462] Holography scores
[P7463] Locality scores
[P7464] Transport budgets
[P7465] Tensor budgets
[P7466] Branch burdens
[P7467] Approximation envelopes
[P7468] Resonance measures
[P7469] Threshold laws
[P7470] Calibration procedures
[P7471] Metric proofs
[P7472] Certificates
[P7473] Replay audits
[P7474] Metric seed.
[P7475] Appendix K is therefore the exact support-layer realization of the measurement discipline implicit across the whole 256 Crystal branch. The preceding appendices have already established:
[P7476] a canonical seed,
[P7477] a primitive transform algebra,
[P7478] Gate-4 and hidden-axis embeddings,
[P7479] the recursive lift law,
[P7480] address and location calculus,
[P7481] the (256^4) hyperaddress/tensor engine,
[P7482] symmetry catalogues and automorphism classes,
[P7483] cancellation manifolds and dual-zero structures,
[P7484] branch taxonomy and admissibility corridors.Appendix K is the point at which those objects receive a common language of magnitude, tolerance, burden, and admissibility. Without it, the branch can state that something is exact, bounded, resonant, fractured, stable, or forbidden; with Appendix K, it can prove how much, under which budget, by what score, and with what replay discipline.
[P7485] The stronger support corpus already provides the precise idiom that Appendix K must specialize. The proof-carrying corridor framework fixes quantitative budgets such as:[B_{\mathrm{commute}},\quadB_{\mathrm{drift}},\quadB_{\mathrm{replay}},\quadB_{\mathrm{uncert}},\quadB_{\mathrm{conflict}},]and requires that every NEAR claim carry residual ledgers, bound certificates, and explicit thresholds. The truth-discipline corpus likewise requires that AMBIG, NEAR, and FAIL all be justified by measurable witness bundles and not by narrative confidence. The broader crystal-compute branch also introduces bloat metrics, (\Delta)-reduction ledgers, proof-preserving pruning, and phase-coherence / resonance invariants for stable integration. Appendix K imports all of these as the metric-control layer of the 256 Crystal branch.
[P7486] Formally, define the Appendix K substrate by
[P7487] [
[P7488] \mathbb K_{\mathrm{metric}}
[P7489] (\mathcal M_{\mathrm{drift}},\mathcal N_{\mathrm{def}},\mathcal S_{\mathrm{sym}},\mathcal H_{\mathrm{holo}},\mathcal L_{\mathrm{loc}},\mathcal B_{\mathrm{bud}},\mathcal T_{\mathrm{ten}},\mathcal R_{\mathrm{res}},\mathcal E_{\mathrm{env}},\mathcal Z_{\mathrm{res}},\mathcal T_{\mathrm{thr}},\mathcal C_{\mathrm{cal}},\mathcal P_{\mathrm{proof}},\mathcal C_{\mathrm{cert}},\mathcal A_{\mathrm{audit}},\mathcal S_{\mathrm{seed}}),]where:
[P7490] (\mathcal M_{\mathrm{drift}}) is the drift-metric family,
[P7491] (\mathcal N_{\mathrm{def}}) is the defect-norm family,
[P7492] (\mathcal S_{\mathrm{sym}}) is the symmetry-score family,
[P7493] (\mathcal H_{\mathrm{holo}}) is the holography-score family,
[P7494] (\mathcal L_{\mathrm{loc}}) is the locality-score family,
[P7495] (\mathcal B_{\mathrm{bud}}) is the transport and corridor budget family,
[P7496] (\mathcal T_{\mathrm{ten}}) is the tensor-budget family,
[P7497] (\mathcal R_{\mathrm{res}}) is the branch-burden and residual family,
[P7498] (\mathcal E_{\mathrm{env}}) is the approximation-envelope family,
[P7499] (\mathcal Z_{\mathrm{res}}) is the resonance-measure family,
[P7500] (\mathcal T_{\mathrm{thr}}) is the threshold-law family,
[P7501] (\mathcal C_{\mathrm{cal}}) is the calibration family,
[P7502] (\mathcal P_{\mathrm{proof}}) is the metric-proof family,
[P7503] (\mathcal C_{\mathrm{cert}}) is the certificate family,
[P7504] (\mathcal A_{\mathrm{audit}}) is the replay-audit family,
[P7505] (\mathcal S_{\mathrm{seed}}) is the metric-seed family.
[P7506] The central thesis of Appendix K is:
[P7507] [\boxed{\text{A crystal claim is not fully lawful until its deviation, burden, coherence, and admissibility are all rendered measurable under explicit norms, budgets, thresholds, and replay-bearing certificates.}}]
[P7508] K.1 Drift metrics
[P7509] The first macro-cell is drift metrics. The supporting corridor and transport corpora already distinguish exact from bounded transforms by a drift quantity (\Delta) or defect quantity (\delta), and explicitly require that any NEAR claim carry a bounded drift ledger rather than an unmeasured deviation. In the 256 Crystal branch, drift is the canonical measure of how far a transformed, lifted, projected, or compared object has moved away from its exact lawful reference state while still remaining inside a typed corridor.
[P7510] Define the drift metric object by
[P7511] [
[P7512] d
[P7513] (\mathrm{DID},\mathrm{TargetRef},\mathrm{ReferenceRef},\Delta,\mathrm{MetricClass},\mathrm{CorridorRef},\Theta_d),]where:
[P7514] (\mathrm{TargetRef}) is the measured object,
[P7515] (\mathrm{ReferenceRef}) is the exact or canonical object,
[P7516] (\Delta) is the drift quantity,
[P7517] (\mathrm{MetricClass}) specifies the norm or comparison regime,
[P7518] (\mathrm{CorridorRef}) is the active admissibility corridor,
[P7519] (\Theta_d) is the drift truth stage.
[P7520] Canonical drift classes in this branch include:
[P7521] visible-board value drift,
[P7522] hidden-coordinate drift,
[P7523] symmetry drift,
[P7524] cancellation drift,
[P7525] tensor-state drift,
[P7526] route or replay drift.
[P7527] A generic drift metric is[\Delta(x,x^\star)=d(x,x^\star),]where (x^\star) is the canonical comparison target. Exactness requires (\Delta=0); bounded legality requires (\Delta\le B_{\mathrm{drift}}).
[P7528] The governing laws are:
[P7529] Drift Law.Every nonexact claim must specify the exact reference object from which drift is measured.
[P7530] No Free Drift Law.A NEAR claim without an explicit drift metric and corridor budget is not lawful.
[P7531] K.2 Defect norms
[P7532] The second macro-cell is defect norms. The support corpus distinguishes drift (\Delta) from defect (\delta): drift measures semantic or transport displacement, while defect measures failure of an exact relation such as commutation, round-trip, diagonal preservation, or tensor identity. This distinction already appears in the representation-transport and generator-simplex corpora, which require explicit defect metrics for DUAL, EQUIV, and BCH-like split compositions.
[P7533] Define the defect-norm object by
[P7534] [
[P7535] n
[P7536] (\mathrm{NID},\mathrm{ClaimRef},\delta,|\cdot|,\mathrm{DefectClass},\Theta_n),]where:
[P7537] (\delta) is the defect magnitude,
[P7538] (|\cdot|) is the chosen norm,
[P7539] (\mathrm{DefectClass}) specifies what law has failed or nearly failed,
[P7540] (\Theta_n) is the defect truth stage.
[P7541] Canonical defect classes in the 256 Crystal branch include:
[P7542] noncommutation defect,
[P7543] diagonal defect,
[P7544] local-holography defect,
[P7545] tensor-factor defect,
[P7546] carry or boundary defect,
[P7547] replay mismatch defect.
[P7548] For example, if (\Gamma_1,\Gamma_2) are two transports or local operators, then the commutator defect norm may be measured by
[P7549] [
[P7550] \delta_{\mathrm{comm}}(\Gamma_1,\Gamma_2)
[P7551] |\Gamma_1\Gamma_2-\Gamma_2\Gamma_1|.
[P7552] ]
[P7553] Likewise a tensor-state defect can be measured by
[P7554] [
[P7555] \delta_{\otimes}
[P7556] \sum_{i=1}^{8}\delta_i,]where (\delta_i) is the mismatch in tensor factor (i).
[P7557] The governing laws are:
[P7558] Defect Norm Law.Every defect claim must specify both the defect class and the norm under which it is measured.
[P7559] Norm Explicitness Law.Two defects are not lawfully comparable unless their norms and defect classes are compatible.
[P7560] K.3 Symmetry scores
[P7561] The third macro-cell is symmetry scores. Appendix G classified the seed and its lifts into symmetry families, automorphism classes, fixed-point classes, and stabilizer towers. Appendix K now equips those classifications with metrics.
[P7562] Define the symmetry-score object by
[P7563] [
[P7564] s
[P7565] (\mathrm{SID},\mathrm{TargetRef},\mathrm{SymmetryFamily},\sigma_s,\delta_s,\Theta_s),]where:
[P7566] (\mathrm{SymmetryFamily}) identifies the family being measured,
[P7567] (\sigma_s) is the symmetry score,
[P7568] (\delta_s) is the residual defect relative to perfect symmetry,
[P7569] (\Theta_s) is the truth stage.
[P7570] Canonical symmetry scores include:
[P7571] row-orbit closure score,
[P7572] column complement score,
[P7573] diagonal-duality score,
[P7574] quadrant-rotation score,
[P7575] twin involution score,
[P7576] automorphism support score.
[P7577] An exact symmetry score may be represented as[\sigma_s=1,\qquad \delta_s=0,]while bounded symmetry carries[0<\delta_s\le B_{\mathrm{commute}}]or another relevant budget. The support corpus on symmetry and corridor budgets already justifies this exact/NEAR split.
[P7578] The governing laws are:
[P7579] Symmetry Score Law.Every symmetry family of the crystal may be measured by a score plus a defect ledger.
[P7580] No Qualitative Symmetry Law.Strong symmetry claims may not remain purely descriptive once the branch has entered the metric layer.
[P7581] K.4 Holography scores
[P7582] The fourth macro-cell is holography scores. Appendix A proved that the seed contains seven distinguished (2\times2) holographic windows. Appendix J identified local holography collapse as one of the strongest failure signatures. Appendix K now measures the extent to which a region, board, or branch preserves that holographic inheritance.
[P7583] Define the holography-score object by
[P7584] [
[P7585] h
[P7586] (\mathrm{HID},\mathrm{TargetRef},H_{\mathrm{obs}},H_{\mathrm{exp}},\delta_h,\Theta_h),]where:
[P7587] (H_{\mathrm{obs}}) is the observed holography score,
[P7588] (H_{\mathrm{exp}}) is the expected score under the active invariant shell,
[P7589] (\delta_h) is the holography defect,
[P7590] (\Theta_h) is the holography truth stage.
[P7591] At the seed level, a natural score is simply the number of lawful (2\times2) holographic windows:[H_{\mathrm{seed}}=7.]At larger scales, holography may be measured by:
[P7592] fraction of lawful local seed chambers,
[P7593] preservation of local-global inheritance,
[P7594] recursive recoverability of subblocks.
[P7595] The governing laws are:
[P7596] Holography Score Law.A crystal region’s local-global fidelity must be measurable by an explicit holography score.
[P7597] Collapse Detection Law.A drop in holography score is one of the primary early indicators of branch fracture.
[P7598] K.5 Locality scores
[P7599] The fifth macro-cell is locality scores. Appendix E already formalized the native locality of the crystal as common-prefix depth in the base-4 address system. Appendix K now equips that locality structure with quantitative scores.
[P7600] Define the locality-score object by
[P7601] [
[P7602] \ell
[P7603] (\mathrm{LID},\mathrm{TargetPair},\lambda,\sigma_\ell,\Theta_\ell),]where:
[P7604] (\lambda) is the common-prefix depth,
[P7605] (\sigma_\ell) is the induced locality score,
[P7606] (\Theta_\ell) is the locality truth stage.
[P7607] A canonical score is[\sigma_\ell=4^{-\lambda}]or any monotone transform thereof. Deeply shared prefixes imply high locality; shallow shared prefixes imply low locality.
[P7608] This score is important because:
[P7609] it measures address-closeness,
[P7610] it supports compression and retrieval decisions,
[P7611] it helps define metro districts and route priorities,
[P7612] it distinguishes local from long-range transforms.
[P7613] The governing laws are:
[P7614] Locality Score Law.Address locality must be rendered quantitative via common-prefix depth or an equivalent lawful metric.
[P7615] No Flat Distance Law.Visible coordinate distance may not replace prefix locality when reconstruction and lift ancestry matter.
[P7616] K.6 Transport budgets
[P7617] The sixth macro-cell is transport budgets. The proof-carrying transport corpus explicitly gives a family of corridor budgets:[B_{\mathrm{commute}},\quadB_{\mathrm{drift}},\quadB_{\mathrm{replay}},\quadB_{\mathrm{uncert}},\quadB_{\mathrm{conflict}}.]Appendix K imports these as the exact budget layer governing transport inside the 256 Crystal branch.
[P7618] Define the transport-budget object by
[P7619] [
[P7620] b
[P7621] (\mathrm{BID},\mathrm{TransportRef},B_{\mathrm{commute}},B_{\mathrm{drift}},B_{\mathrm{replay}},B_{\mathrm{uncert}},B_{\mathrm{conflict}},\Theta_b).]
[P7622] These budgets constrain:
[P7623] transform composition,
[P7624] hidden-axis transport,
[P7625] 90° tunneling or DUAL movement,
[P7626] bounded branch migration,
[P7627] replay-acceptable transport cost.
[P7628] A transport remains lawful only if its measured defects remain within the declared budgets.
[P7629] The governing laws are:
[P7630] Transport Budget Law.Every lawful transport must declare and satisfy its commutation, drift, replay, uncertainty, and conflict budgets.
[P7631] Budget Failure Law.Crossing a transport budget forces downgrade, ambiguity, or failure according to corridor rules.
[P7632] K.7 Tensor budgets
[P7633] The seventh macro-cell is tensor budgets. Appendix F made the hypercrystal a tensor engine[\mathcal C_{256^4}=L_4^{\otimes 8}.]Appendix K now measures when tensor transport, comparison, or projection remains admissible.
[P7634] Define the tensor-budget object by
[P7635] [
[P7636] t
[P7637] (\mathrm{TID},\mathrm{TargetRef},B_{\otimes},\delta_{\otimes},\mathrm{FactorLedger},\Theta_t),]where:
[P7638] (B_{\otimes}) is the total allowed tensor defect,
[P7639] (\delta_{\otimes}) is the measured aggregate tensor defect,
[P7640] (\mathrm{FactorLedger}) records per-factor contributions.
[P7641] A typical aggregate budget law is[\delta_{\otimes}=\sum_{i=1}^{8}\delta_i\le B_{\otimes}.]
[P7642] This lets the branch distinguish:
[P7643] exact hypercell equality,
[P7644] bounded tensor equivalence,
[P7645] forbidden hyperstate drift.
[P7646] The governing laws are:
[P7647] Tensor Budget Law.No higher-dimensional state comparison is lawful without an explicit tensor defect budget.
[P7648] Factor Ledger Law.Tensor defects must remain factor-resolved rather than being collapsed into an opaque single number.
[P7649] K.8 Branch burdens
[P7650] The eighth macro-cell is branch burdens. Appendix I classified stable, prime, composite, and forbidden branches under typed corridors. Appendix J refined the exception side through parity tangles, failure cases, and salvageability. Appendix K now quantifies what those branch states cost.
[P7651] Define the branch-burden object by
[P7652] [
[P7653] b
[P7654] (\mathrm{BID},\mathrm{BranchRef},\mathcal O_b,\mu_b,\Theta_b),]where:
[P7655] (\mathcal O_b) is the obligation set,
[P7656] (\mu_b) is the burden mass,
[P7657] (\Theta_b) is the burden truth stage.
[P7658] Canonical burdens include:
[P7659] unresolved diagonal failure burden,
[P7660] holography collapse burden,
[P7661] nonrecursive lift burden,
[P7662] replay insufficiency burden,
[P7663] route-forbidden burden.
[P7664] This object makes it possible to distinguish:
[P7665] a branch that is heavy but still NEAR,
[P7666] a branch that is too burdened to remain in the same corridor,
[P7667] a branch that is salvageable only after burden discharge.
[P7668] The governing laws are:
[P7669] Branch Burden Law.Every nonexact branch state must carry an explicit burden object.
[P7670] Burden Monotonicity Law.If new failures or obligations accumulate, the branch burden may not decrease silently.
[P7671] K.9 Approximation envelopes
[P7672] The ninth macro-cell is approximation envelopes. The proof-carrying and truth-discipline support lines explicitly require that every NEAR claim carry residual ledgers and bound certificates. Appendix K specializes that to crystal approximation.
[P7673] Define the approximation-envelope object by
[P7674] [
[P7675] e
[P7676] (\mathrm{EID},\mathrm{TargetRef},\tau_e,\mathcal M_e,\delta_e,\Theta_e),]where:
[P7677] (\tau_e) is the allowed approximation radius,
[P7678] (\mathcal M_e) is the metric family,
[P7679] (\delta_e) is the observed approximation defect,
[P7680] (\Theta_e) is the envelope truth stage.
[P7681] This envelope is used when:
[P7682] comparing approximate symmetry classes,
[P7683] projecting hidden coordinates to visible shadows,
[P7684] sampling the hypercrystal,
[P7685] compressing branch objects,
[P7686] salvaging bounded-exception branches.
[P7687] The law is:
[P7688] Approximation Envelope Law.A NEAR crystal claim is lawful only when its approximation error is trapped inside an explicit envelope.
[P7689] No Envelope-Free NEAR Law.A bounded claim without an envelope is not a lawful NEAR claim.
[P7690] K.10 Resonance measures
[P7691] The tenth macro-cell is resonance measures. The live chapter skeleton for Chapter 9 already names “Resonance and coherence interpretation,” and the wider crystal-compute and self-steer support lines explicitly treat phase coherence, harmonic packet structure, and emergent route-locking as measurable rather than merely poetic. The Crystal Thesis support text states that stable intermediate crystals arise by multi-view invariant compatibility and that a lawful completion is a low-action fixed point consistent with measured invariants. The self-steer support also explicitly gives multi-lens lifted objects with spectral, probability, and defect components, making resonance a structural property of cross-lens agreement and phase compatibility.
[P7692] Define the resonance-measure object by
[P7693] [
[P7694] r
[P7695] (\mathrm{RID},\mathrm{TargetRef},\mathcal R_r,\mathcal C_r,\delta_r,\Theta_r),]where:
[P7696] (\mathcal R_r) is the resonance measure,
[P7697] (\mathcal C_r) is the coherence decomposition,
[P7698] (\delta_r) is the resonance defect,
[P7699] (\Theta_r) is the resonance truth stage.
[P7700] A canonical branch-compatible resonance functional is[\mathcal R_r(\pi)=\alpha,\mathrm{InvPres}(\pi)+\beta,\mathrm{CancelClosure}(\pi)+\gamma,\mathrm{ReplayStrength}(\pi)-\lambda,\delta(\pi),]where (\pi) is a route, transform chain, or inference lane. This is exactly the 256 Crystal branch’s structural version of resonance: lawful coherence across invariants, cancellation, replay, and bounded defect.
[P7701] The governing laws are:
[P7702] Resonance Law.A crystal route or state is resonant when its invariants, cancellation structure, and replay coherence reinforce one another.
[P7703] No Aesthetic Resonance Law.Resonance may not be asserted without explicit measurable structural support.
[P7704] K.11 Threshold laws
[P7705] The eleventh macro-cell is threshold laws. Metrics and budgets become operational only when thresholds are explicit. The corridor support corpus already requires this: every truth class must be tied to quantitative break conditions. Appendix K therefore defines the threshold object
[P7706] [
[P7707] \theta
[P7708] (\mathrm{TID},\mathrm{MetricRef},\mathrm{ThresholdSet},\mathrm{PromotionRules},\mathrm{FailureRules},\Theta_\theta),]where:
[P7709] (\mathrm{MetricRef}) identifies the measured quantity,
[P7710] (\mathrm{ThresholdSet}) stores OK / NEAR / FAIL breakpoints,
[P7711] (\mathrm{PromotionRules}) define how crossing thresholds upward promotes status,
[P7712] (\mathrm{FailureRules}) define how crossing thresholds downward forces downgrade or quarantine.
[P7713] Examples include:[\delta=0 \Rightarrow \mathrm{OK},][0<\delta\le B \Rightarrow \mathrm{NEAR},][\delta>B \Rightarrow \mathrm{FAIL},]and analogous thresholds for holography retention, branch burden, or resonance score.
[P7714] The governing laws are:
[P7715] Threshold Law.Every metric used for truth or admissibility must carry explicit thresholds.
[P7716] No Unbounded Threshold Law.A thresholdless metric may diagnose but may not certify corridor status.
[P7717] K.12 Calibration procedures
[P7718] The twelfth macro-cell is calibration procedures. If the branch is going to use drift metrics, defect norms, branch burdens, and resonance measures lawfully, then those measures must be calibrated against fixed references.
[P7719] Define the calibration object by
[P7720] [
[P7721] \kappa
[P7722] (\mathrm{KID},\mathrm{MetricRef},\mathrm{ReferenceSet},\mathrm{CalibrationRule},\mathrm{VersionPin},\Theta_\kappa),]where:
[P7723] (\mathrm{ReferenceSet}) is the family of canonical comparison objects,
[P7724] (\mathrm{CalibrationRule}) maps observations into certified scores,
[P7725] (\mathrm{VersionPin}) freezes the calibration epoch.
[P7726] Canonical calibration anchors in the branch include:
[P7727] the canonical seed (L_4),
[P7728] its local holography census,
[P7729] the exact recursive lift law,
[P7730] the exact ((X,Y,Z,W)) decomposition,
[P7731] replay-closed reference artifacts.
[P7732] The governing laws are:
[P7733] Calibration Law.No metric is fully lawful until it is calibrated against explicit branch-canonical references.
[P7734] Version-Pin Law.Calibration rules must be version-pinned so that later branch drift does not retroactively alter earlier scores.
[P7735] K.13 Metric proofs
[P7736] The thirteenth macro-cell is metric proofs. A metric proof object justifies:
[P7737] why the metric is well-defined,
[P7738] why it is appropriate for the target invariant,
[P7739] how its thresholds interact with corridor truth,
[P7740] how it composes under lift, tensorization, or replay.
[P7741] Define the proof object by
[P7742] [
[P7743] \pi_K
[P7744] (\mathrm{PID},\mathrm{MetricRef},\Gamma,\mathrm{ReferenceObjects},\mathrm{Claim},\Theta_\pi),]where:
[P7745] (\Gamma) is the assumption set,
[P7746] (\mathrm{ReferenceObjects}) are the calibration anchors,
[P7747] (\mathrm{Claim}) is the measured theorem or admissibility claim.
[P7748] The law is:
[P7749] Metric Proof Law.No strong metric claim is lawful without a proof object anchoring the metric to branch-canonical references and corridor thresholds.
[P7750] K.14 Certificates
[P7751] The fourteenth macro-cell is the family of metric certificates. A metric certificate takes the form
[P7752] [
[P7753] C_K
[P7754] (\mathrm{CID},\mathrm{TargetRef},\mathrm{MetricSet},\mathrm{ThresholdSet},\mathrm{TruthMap},\rho_K,\Theta_K),]where:
[P7755] (\mathrm{MetricSet}) lists the measured quantities,
[P7756] (\mathrm{ThresholdSet}) records the calibration breakpoints,
[P7757] (\mathrm{TruthMap}) maps the measurements into corridor classes,
[P7758] (\rho_K) is the replay bundle.
[P7759] This certificate is what turns measurement into proof-carrying admissibility.
[P7760] The governing law is:
[P7761] Metric Certificate Law.No strong branch, symmetry, cancellation, or transport assessment is lawful without a certificate-bearing metric object.
[P7762] K.15 Replay audits
[P7763] The fifteenth macro-cell is replay audits. A replay audit checks that:
[P7764] the metric was computed under the declared calibration,
[P7765] the same target recomputes the same score under deterministic rerun,
[P7766] any bounded nondeterminism is explicitly logged,
[P7767] threshold classification is replay-stable.
[P7768] Define the replay-audit object by
[P7769] [
[P7770] A_K
[P7771] (\mathrm{AID},\mathrm{TargetRef},\mathrm{MetricRef},\mathrm{ReplayTrace},\mathrm{ObservedClass},\Theta_A).]
[P7772] This is a direct specialization of the wider replay doctrine: strong crystal claims must not merely be measurable, but replay-measurable.
[P7773] The law is:
[P7774] Replay Audit Law.A metric is strongly lawful only when its value and truth classification survive replay audit.
[P7775] No Unpinned Metric Law.An unpinned or irreproducible score may not be promoted to strong status.
[P7776] K.16 Metric seed
[P7777] The final macro-cell is the metric seed. Appendix K must compress its whole measurement grammar into a replay-bearing seed:
[P7778] [
[P7779] \zeta_K
[P7780] (g_K,r_K,\eta_K,\rho_K,\Theta_K),]where:
[P7781] (g_K) is the generator core of the metric grammar,
[P7782] (r_K) is the residual shell of unresolved or bounded metric structure,
[P7783] (\eta_K) is the metric-identity digest,
[P7784] (\rho_K) is the replay/regrowth bundle.
[P7785] This seed can regenerate:
[P7786] drift metrics,
[P7787] defect norms,
[P7788] symmetry and holography scores,
[P7789] locality scores,
[P7790] transport and tensor budgets,
[P7791] branch burdens,
[P7792] approximation envelopes,
[P7793] resonance measures,
[P7794] threshold laws,
[P7795] calibration procedures,
[P7796] metric proofs,
[P7797] metric certificates,
[P7798] replay audits.
[P7799] The final theorem of Appendix K is therefore:
[P7800] [\boxed{\text{The metric grammar of the 256 Crystal branch is fully lawful only when drift, defect, symmetry, holography, locality, transport, tensor, burden, approximation, resonance, threshold, calibration, proof, certificate, replay-audit, and metric-seed structures form one coherent replayable quantitative corridor system.}}]
[P7801] K.17 Canonical algorithmic form
[P7802] from dataclasses import dataclass, field
[P7803] from typing import Dict, Any, List, Literal
[P7804] TruthClass = Literal["OK", "NEAR", "AMBIG", "FAIL"]
[P7805] @dataclass
[P7806] class MetricCertificate:
[P7807] target_ref: str
[P7808] metric_set: Dict[str, float]
[P7809] thresholds: Dict[str, float]
[P7810] truth_map: Dict[str, TruthClass]
[P7811] truth: TruthClass
[P7812] replay_trace: List[str] = field(default_factory=list)
[P7813] def drift_metric(observed: float, reference: float) -> float:
[P7814] return abs(observed - reference)
[P7815] def defect_norm(values: List[float]) -> float:
[P7816] return sum(abs(v) for v in values)
[P7817] def locality_score(common_prefix_depth: int) -> float:
[P7818] return 4 ** (-common_prefix_depth)
[P7819] def resonance_measure(inv_pres: float, cancel_closure: float, replay_strength: float, defect: float,
[P7820] a: float = 1.0, b: float = 1.0, c: float = 1.0, d: float = 1.0) -> float:
[P7821] return a * inv_pres + b * cancel_closure + c * replay_strength - d * defect
[P7822] def classify_metric(defect: float, budget: float) -> TruthClass:
[P7823] if defect == 0:
[P7824] return "OK"
[P7825] if defect <= budget:
[P7826] return "NEAR"
[P7827] return "FAIL"
[P7828] def certify_metrics(target_ref: str, metric_set: Dict[str, float], thresholds: Dict[str, float]) -> MetricCertificate:
[P7829] truth_map = {k: classify_metric(v, thresholds.get(k, 0.0)) for k, v in metric_set.items()}
[P7830] overall = "OK"
[P7831] if any(v == "FAIL" for v in truth_map.values()):
[P7832] overall = "FAIL"
[P7833] elif any(v == "NEAR" for v in truth_map.values()):
[P7834] overall = "NEAR"
[P7835] return MetricCertificate(
[P7836] target_ref=target_ref,
[P7837] metric_set=metric_set,
[P7838] thresholds=thresholds,
[P7839] truth_map=truth_map,
[P7840] truth=overall,
[P7841] replay_trace=[target_ref, "metrics_certified"]
[P7842] )
[P7843] This canonical form compresses the appendix’s law: compute explicit drift and defect values, derive locality and resonance scores, classify them against corridor thresholds, and emit a replay-bearing certificate.
[P7844] K.18 Appendix-level laws
[P7845] Drift Law — every nonexact claim requires an explicit drift reference and drift metric.
[P7846] Defect Norm Law — every defect must be measured under a declared norm.
[P7847] Symmetry Score Law — symmetry claims require quantitative scores plus defects.
[P7848] Holography Score Law — local-global inheritance must be measurable.
[P7849] Locality Score Law — prefix-based locality must be quantified explicitly.
[P7850] Transport Budget Law — transport legality is governed by explicit corridor budgets.
[P7851] Tensor Budget Law — higher-dimensional comparison requires explicit tensor defect budgets.
[P7852] Branch Burden Law — nonexact branches carry measurable burdens.
[P7853] Approximation Envelope Law — bounded claims require explicit envelopes.
[P7854] Resonance Law — coherence must be measurable, not merely described.
[P7855] Threshold Law — every metric used for admissibility requires thresholds.
[P7856] Calibration Law — metrics must be anchored to branch-canonical references.
[P7857] Metric Proof Law — strong scores require proof objects.
[P7858] Metric Certificate Law — strong quantitative claims require certificates.
[P7859] Metric Seed Law — the full measurement grammar must compress into a replay-bearing seed.
[P7860] K.19 Closing statement
[P7861] Appendix K defines the quantitative corridor system of the 256 Crystal branch. It takes every major qualitative distinction already established elsewhere in the branch—exact versus bounded, stable versus fractured, local versus distant, resonant versus incoherent, lawful versus forbidden—and renders it measurable under explicit metrics, budgets, thresholds, and replay audits. In doing so, it provides the branch with its first full measurement grammar: drift metrics, defect norms, symmetry and holography scores, locality measures, transport and tensor budgets, branch burdens, approximation envelopes, resonance measures, threshold laws, calibration procedures, proof objects, certificates, and a metric seed. This appendix is therefore the exact support-layer realization of the branch’s quantitative discipline. Without Appendix K, the crystal could classify itself but not measure itself. With Appendix K, the crystal acquires its scales.
[P7862] Appendix K — Metrics, Defect Budgets, and Resonance Measures
[P7863] Appendix L — Algorithms, Runtimes, and Extraction Procedures
[P7864] L.0 Appendix Function
[P7865] In the current live branch of The 256 Crystal Extraction, Appendix L is explicitly stabilized as “Algorithms, Runtimes, and Extraction Procedures.” Its 16 macro-cells are fixed as:
[P7866] Recursive generator
[P7867] Tensor evaluator
[P7868] Address decoder
[P7869] Block extractor
[P7870] Symmetry scanner
[P7871] Cancellation scanner
[P7872] Branch explorer
[P7873] Corridor evaluator
[P7874] Proof compiler
[P7875] Replay engine
[P7876] Complexity bounds
[P7877] Memory bounds
[P7878] Parallelization maps
[P7879] Runtime harnesses
[P7880] Audit scripts
[P7881] Runtime seed.
[P7882] Appendix L is therefore the exact support-layer realization of Chapter 8 — Computation, Verification, and the Extraction Engine. The chapter body already fixed the runtime obligations of the branch: recursive board generation, hypercrystal tensor evaluation, address resolution, block extraction, symmetry and cancellation scans, local kernel verification, recursive-lift verification, tesseract-embedding verification, defect-budget verification, certificate bundling, replay artifact construction, deterministic reruns, runtime audit, and engine-seed closure. Appendix L is where those obligations become an explicit procedural stack rather than only a chapter theorem.
[P7883] The stronger support corpus sharpens the same role in a general systems language. The Unified MATH Crystal Atlas states the branch-wide memory doctrine:[X=\mathrm{Expand}(g)\oplus r,]where (g) is a compact generator, (r) is a sparse residual, and (\oplus) is deterministic reconstruction. It also requires HoloAddress grammar, deterministic reconstruction, random access, prefix stability, audit trails, and versioned diffs. The TomeForge and Quantum Lang TOME runtime branches add the operational discipline:
[P7884] deterministic resolution,
[P7885] canonical serialization,
[P7886] seeded nondeterminism only,
[P7887] replay as semantics,
[P7888] verifier gate before execution,
[P7889] fail-localization,
[P7890] and mandatory audit traces. Appendix L specializes that entire runtime doctrine to the 256 Crystal extraction engine.
[P7891] Formally, define the Appendix L substrate by
[P7892] [
[P7893] \mathbb L_{\mathrm{runtime}}
[P7894] (\mathcal G_{\mathrm{rec}},\mathcal T_{\mathrm{eval}},\mathcal A_{\mathrm{dec}},\mathcal B_{\mathrm{ext}},\mathcal S_{\mathrm{scan}},\mathcal C_{\mathrm{scan}},\mathcal B_{\mathrm{exp}},\mathcal E_{\mathrm{corr}},\mathcal P_{\mathrm{comp}},\mathcal R_{\mathrm{eng}},\mathcal X_{\mathrm{cost}},\mathcal M_{\mathrm{mem}},\mathcal P_{\parallel},\mathcal H_{\mathrm{run}},\mathcal A_{\mathrm{audit}},\mathcal S_{\mathrm{seed}}),]where:
[P7895] (\mathcal G_{\mathrm{rec}}) is the recursive-generation family,
[P7896] (\mathcal T_{\mathrm{eval}}) is the tensor-evaluation family,
[P7897] (\mathcal A_{\mathrm{dec}}) is the address-decoder family,
[P7898] (\mathcal B_{\mathrm{ext}}) is the block-extraction family,
[P7899] (\mathcal S_{\mathrm{scan}}) is the symmetry-scan family,
[P7900] (\mathcal C_{\mathrm{scan}}) is the cancellation-scan family,
[P7901] (\mathcal B_{\mathrm{exp}}) is the branch-explorer family,
[P7902] (\mathcal E_{\mathrm{corr}}) is the corridor-evaluator family,
[P7903] (\mathcal P_{\mathrm{comp}}) is the proof-compiler family,
[P7904] (\mathcal R_{\mathrm{eng}}) is the replay-engine family,
[P7905] (\mathcal X_{\mathrm{cost}}) is the complexity family,
[P7906] (\mathcal M_{\mathrm{mem}}) is the memory-bound family,
[P7907] (\mathcal P_{\parallel}) is the parallelization-map family,
[P7908] (\mathcal H_{\mathrm{run}}) is the runtime-harness family,
[P7909] (\mathcal A_{\mathrm{audit}}) is the audit-script family,
[P7910] (\mathcal S_{\mathrm{seed}}) is the runtime-seed family.
[P7911] The central thesis of Appendix L is:
[P7912] [\boxed{\text{The 256 Crystal branch is computationally lawful only when generation, evaluation, decoding, extraction, scanning, proof compilation, replay, complexity control, parallelization, runtime discipline, and auditing are all explicit, deterministic, and seed-regenerable.}}]
[P7913] L.1 Recursive generator
[P7914] The first macro-cell is the recursive generator. The exact generation law of the visible crystal branch is already fixed:
[P7915] [
[P7916] L_{4^m}\bigl(4^{m-1}i+r,\ 4^{m-1}j+s\bigr)
[P7917] 4^{m-1}\bigl(L_4(i,j)-1\bigr)+L_{4^{m-1}}(r,s).]Appendix L treats this equation as an executable constructor rather than only as a theorem.
[P7918] Define the recursive generator by[\mathcal G_{\mathrm{rec}}(m):=L_{4^m},]with[\mathcal G_{\mathrm{rec}}(1)=L_4,\qquad\mathcal G_{\mathrm{rec}}(m)=\mathrm{Subst}\bigl(L_4,\mathcal G_{\mathrm{rec}}(m-1)\bigr).]
[P7919] A lawful generator must support two exact execution modes:
[P7920] Materialized recursionConstruct (L_{4^{m-1}}), then substitute 16 offset copies into the outer (4\times4) seed.
[P7921] Lazy point generationExpand row and column addresses into base-4 digits, evaluate the seed digitwise, and reassemble the value without materializing the whole board.
[P7922] The support corpus’s “store IN, not OUT” doctrine makes the second mode especially important: the crystal should be generated from its seed and reconstruction law rather than treated as a brute-force table.
[P7923] The governing laws are:
[P7924] Recursive Generator Law.Every visible board of the branch must be constructible from (L_4) by exact substitution.
[P7925] Lazy Generation Law.Pointwise generation from digitwise seed evaluation is a lawful and preferred runtime mode when full materialization is unnecessary.
[P7926] L.2 Tensor evaluator
[P7927] The second macro-cell is the tensor evaluator. The branch already fixed the full hypercrystal law:[256^4=4^{16},\qquad\mathcal C_{256^4}=L_4^{\otimes 8}.]It also fixed the 4D coordinate decomposition[(X,Y,Z,W)]and the canonical pairing family[(x_t,y_t),\qquad (z_t,w_t),\qquad t=0,1,2,3.]Appendix L makes that tensorization executable.
[P7928] Define the tensor evaluator by[\mathcal T_{\mathrm{eval}}:(X,Y,Z,W)\mapsto(u_3,u_2,u_1,u_0;\ v_3,v_2,v_1,v_0),]where[u_t=L_4(x_t,y_t)-1,\qquadv_t=L_4(z_t,w_t)-1.]
[P7929] This evaluator must:
[P7930] decode all four coordinates into base-4 digits,
[P7931] apply the canonical pairing scheme,
[P7932] compute the eight seed evaluations,
[P7933] assemble the hyperstate tuple,
[P7934] emit a replayable trace of the factor evaluation.
[P7935] This is the exact higher-dimensional continuation of the recursive board generator.
[P7936] The governing law is:
[P7937] Tensor Evaluator Law.Every hyperstate of the branch must be computable by eight lawful applications of the root kernel under a declared pairing scheme.
[P7938] L.3 Address decoder
[P7939] The third macro-cell is the address decoder. The branch already defines:
[P7940] the full base-4 cell address,
[P7941] the prefix block grammar,
[P7942] the 16-digit hyperaddress,
[P7943] and the visible / hidden coordinate split. Appendix L makes those address forms executable runtime objects.
[P7944] Define the address decoder by[\mathcal A_{\mathrm{dec}}:\mathcal A_{\mathrm{raw}}\to(\mathcal A_{\mathrm{canon}},\mathrm{PrefixLineage},\mathrm{TensorPairs},\Theta_A),]where:
[P7945] (\mathcal A_{\mathrm{raw}}) is any surface form of a coordinate,
[P7946] (\mathcal A_{\mathrm{canon}}) is the normalized address,
[P7947] (\mathrm{PrefixLineage}) is the block ancestry,
[P7948] (\mathrm{TensorPairs}) are the exact pairings needed for tensor evaluation,
[P7949] (\Theta_A) is the decoding truth stage.
[P7950] The support corpus on addressed holography directly requires:
[P7951] deterministic reconstruction,
[P7952] self-delimiting address grammar,
[P7953] prefix stability,
[P7954] replayable decode traces. Appendix L therefore treats address decoding as a proof-bearing transformation rather than a simple parser.
[P7955] The governing laws are:
[P7956] Address Decoder Law.Every lawful runtime path begins by decoding its target into canonical address form.
[P7957] Prefix Stability Law.Decoding may refine an address but may not silently rewrite an already-fixed prefix.
[P7958] L.4 Block extractor
[P7959] The fourth macro-cell is the block extractor. The branch’s block grammar already states that a block of side (4^k) is identified by the first (m-k) row/column digits. Appendix L turns that law into an executable extractor.
[P7960] Define[\mathcal B_{\mathrm{ext}}:(m,k,\alpha,\beta)\mapsto \mathcal B_{m,k}(\alpha,\beta),]where ((\alpha,\beta)) is the fixed prefix and the extractor returns either:
[P7961] a materialized block,
[P7962] or a symbolic block object consisting of fixed prefix plus free suffix variables.
[P7963] The symbolic mode is especially important because it preserves the branch’s memory doctrine:[X=\mathrm{Expand}(g)\oplus r.]One should extract a block as a generator plus address and only materialize when needed.
[P7964] The governing laws are:
[P7965] Block Extractor Law.Every lawful block must be extractable from its prefix address and the branch’s generator core.
[P7966] Symbolic Extraction Law.Materialization is optional when a symbolic generator form preserves exact replay.
[P7967] L.5 Symmetry scanner
[P7968] The fifth macro-cell is the symmetry scanner. Appendix G already classified:
[P7969] row orbits,
[P7970] column complement pairs,
[P7971] diagonal duals,
[P7972] quadrant rotations,
[P7973] twin involutions,
[P7974] automorphism groups,
[P7975] stabilizer towers. Appendix L now turns that catalog into a runtime scanner.
[P7976] Define the symmetry scanner by[\mathcal S_{\mathrm{scan}}(X)\to(\mathcal S_{\mathrm{present}},\mathcal S_{\mathrm{broken}},\delta_{\mathrm{sym}},\Theta_S),]where:
[P7977] (\mathcal S_{\mathrm{present}}) is the detected symmetry family set,
[P7978] (\mathcal S_{\mathrm{broken}}) is the broken or bounded family set,
[P7979] (\delta_{\mathrm{sym}}) is the symmetry defect ledger,
[P7980] (\Theta_S) is the resulting truth stage.
[P7981] A lawful symmetry scanner must operate at several scales:
[P7982] seed-level,
[P7983] block-level,
[P7984] visible-board scale,
[P7985] hypercell / hyperslice scale.
[P7986] This scanner is one of the key generators of the branch’s later “symmetry-to-memory compression” law.
[P7987] The governing law is:
[P7988] Symmetry Scanner Law.A lawful extraction runtime must be able to detect, classify, and ledger exact and bounded symmetry families.
[P7989] L.6 Cancellation scanner
[P7990] The sixth macro-cell is the cancellation scanner. Appendix H already formalized:
[P7991] local cancellation objects,
[P7992] dual zero/infinity classes,
[P7993] the 4D cancellation torus,
[P7994] defect hyperplanes,
[P7995] complement versus annihilation,
[P7996] balance surfaces,
[P7997] zero-point ratio laws. Appendix L turns that support-layer structure into a runtime scanner.
[P7998] Define the cancellation scanner by[\mathcal C_{\mathrm{scan}}(X)\to(\mathcal Z_0,\mathcal T^2,\mathcal H_{\mathrm{def}},\rho_0,\Theta_C),]where:
[P7999] (\mathcal Z_0) is the zero-class family detected,
[P8000] (\mathcal T^2) is the hidden toroidal closure family,
[P8001] (\mathcal H_{\mathrm{def}}) are defect hyperplanes,
[P8002] (\rho_0) is the zero-point ratio measure,
[P8003] (\Theta_C) is the cancellation truth stage.
[P8004] The scanner must support:
[P8005] local-window cancellation detection,
[P8006] visible-board balance scans,
[P8007] hidden-sector torus scans,
[P8008] defect-hyperplane tracing,
[P8009] zero-ratio maximization.
[P8010] The governing law is:
[P8011] Cancellation Scanner Law.A lawful runtime must detect not only exact balance but also bounded cancellation, defect fractures, and toroidal hidden closure.
[P8012] L.7 Branch explorer
[P8013] The seventh macro-cell is the branch explorer. Appendix I and Appendix J together already classify:
[P8014] stable branches,
[P8015] prime complementary branches,
[P8016] composite classes,
[P8017] forbidden branches,
[P8018] parity tangles,
[P8019] salvageable and nonsalvageable exceptions. Appendix L operationalizes that taxonomy as an exploration engine.
[P8020] Define the branch explorer by[\mathcal B_{\mathrm{exp}}:(\mathrm{SeedRef},\mathrm{TargetOrder},\mathrm{CorridorRef})\to(\mathcal B_{\mathrm{cand}},\mathcal W_{\mathrm{witness}},\Theta_B),]where:
[P8021] (\mathcal B_{\mathrm{cand}}) is the candidate branch set,
[P8022] (\mathcal W_{\mathrm{witness}}) is the branch witness bundle,
[P8023] (\Theta_B) is the resulting branch truth stage.
[P8024] The support corpus’s “algorithm that makes algorithms” loop gives the deeper runtime interpretation:
[P8025] emit goal specs,
[P8026] enumerate admissible candidates,
[P8027] nullify impossible routes,
[P8028] execute under corridors,
[P8029] attempt collapse to certified artifacts,
[P8030] interpret failure,
[P8031] update the basis. Appendix L specializes that loop to branch exploration.
[P8032] The governing laws are:
[P8033] Branch Explorer Law.A branch explorer must enumerate, test, nullify, and certify candidate branches under corridor discipline.
[P8034] No Blind Branching Law.New candidate branches may not be generated without typed witnesses and failure interpretation.
[P8035] L.8 Corridor evaluator
[P8036] The eighth macro-cell is the corridor evaluator. The wider manuscript family already requires every operation to return[\mathbb T={\mathrm{OK},\mathrm{NEAR},\mathrm{AMBIG},\mathrm{FAIL}}]with explicit witness and replay obligations. Appendix I specialized that to branch admissibility. Appendix L turns the same logic into a runtime evaluator.
[P8037] Define the evaluator by[\mathcal E_{\mathrm{corr}}(x)\to(\tau,\mathcal O_x,\mathcal W_x,\rho_x),\qquad\tau\in\mathbb T,]where:
[P8038] (\tau) is the typed outcome,
[P8039] (\mathcal O_x) is the obligation set,
[P8040] (\mathcal W_x) is the witness bundle,
[P8041] (\rho_x) is the replay object.
[P8042] The evaluator must:
[P8043] read the active corridor policy,
[P8044] measure defect and burden,
[P8045] check witnesses,
[P8046] check replay sufficiency,
[P8047] classify the result.
[P8048] The governing laws are:
[P8049] Corridor Evaluator Law.Every runtime action in the branch must pass through a typed corridor evaluator.
[P8050] No Silent Promotion Law.An evaluator may not return OK without witness and replay closure.
[P8051] L.9 Proof compiler
[P8052] The ninth macro-cell is the proof compiler. The support corpus repeatedly insists that the output of lawful mathematics is not a sentence but an artifact bundle consisting of definitions, algorithms, constraints, certificates, and replay capsules. Appendix L operationalizes that by compiling proof objects from runtime traces.
[P8053] Define the proof compiler by[\mathcal P_{\mathrm{comp}}:(\mathrm{Trace},\mathrm{Witnesses},\mathrm{Metrics},\mathrm{Corridor})\to\pi,]where (\pi) is a proof object with:
[P8054] claims,
[P8055] assumptions,
[P8056] witness references,
[P8057] replay pointers,
[P8058] truth stage.
[P8059] This compiler is required because the extraction engine itself must produce theorem-grade artifacts, not merely numbers or pictures.
[P8060] The governing laws are:
[P8061] Proof Compiler Law.Every strong runtime result must compile into a proof-bearing artifact bundle.
[P8062] Artifact Closure Law.A compiled proof object is incomplete unless it includes witness, metric, and replay references.
[P8063] L.10 Replay engine
[P8064] The tenth macro-cell is the replay engine. The support runtime corpora state the replay doctrine in its strongest form:
[P8065] deterministic resolution,
[P8066] canonical serialization,
[P8067] seeded nondeterminism only,
[P8068] replay as semantics,
[P8069] verifier gate before execution,
[P8070] fail-localization,
[P8071] trace hashing,
[P8072] artifact-store consistency. Appendix L specializes this to the 256 Crystal branch.
[P8073] Define the replay engine by[\mathcal R_{\mathrm{eng}}:(\mathrm{Capsule},\mathrm{EnvPin},\mathrm{SeedRegs})\to(\mathrm{TraceHash},\mathrm{LedgerRoot},\tau),]where:
[P8074] (\mathrm{Capsule}) is the runtime capsule,
[P8075] (\mathrm{EnvPin}) is the environment fingerprint,
[P8076] (\mathrm{SeedRegs}) are explicit seeds for any stochastic or scheduled behavior,
[P8077] (\tau) is the replay truth stage.
[P8078] The governing laws are:
[P8079] Replay Engine Law.A published or promoted crystal claim is meaningful only if the replay engine can reinstantiate it under pinned environment and seeds.
[P8080] Seeded Nondeterminism Law.Any runtime nondeterminism must be explicitly seeded and transcripted.
[P8081] L.11 Complexity bounds
[P8082] The eleventh macro-cell is complexity bounds. Chapter 8 already established the main runtime facts:
[P8083] point evaluation of (L_{4^m}) is (O(m)),
[P8084] hypercell evaluation is linear in the number of quaternary digits,
[P8085] full crystal materialization is optional,
[P8086] many tasks are prefix- or factor-local. Appendix L turns those into explicit complexity objects.
[P8087] Define the complexity object by
[P8088] [
[P8089] \mathcal X_{\mathrm{cost}}
[P8090] (\mathrm{XID},\mathrm{TaskRef},T(n),M(n),\mathrm{BudgetRef},\Theta_X),]where:
[P8091] (T(n)) is time cost,
[P8092] (M(n)) is memory cost,
[P8093] (\mathrm{BudgetRef}) is the active runtime budget.
[P8094] Canonical complexity claims in the branch include:
[P8095] visible point evaluation: (O(\log_4 n)),
[P8096] hyperstate evaluation: (O(16)) for the fixed (256^4) crystal,
[P8097] block extraction: proportional to the size of the requested suffix region,
[P8098] scan complexity: dependent on scan mode and materialization depth.
[P8099] The governing laws are:
[P8100] Complexity Bound Law.Every runtime procedure must declare its time and memory class.
[P8101] No Unbudgeted Runtime Law.A runtime procedure may not be promoted without explicit complexity bounds.
[P8102] L.12 Memory bounds
[P8103] The twelfth macro-cell is memory bounds. The support corpus’s strongest memory doctrine is:[X=\mathrm{Expand}(g)\oplus r,]meaning the system stores generators and sparse residuals rather than full expanded bulk. Appendix L formalizes this as a memory bound on the 256 Crystal engine.
[P8104] Define the memory-bound object by
[P8105] [
[P8106] m
[P8107] (\mathrm{MID},\mathrm{TargetRef},g,r,\mathrm{MaterializationPolicy},M_{\max},\Theta_m),]where:
[P8108] (g) is the generator core,
[P8109] (r) is the residual shell,
[P8110] (\mathrm{MaterializationPolicy}) tells which expansions are permitted,
[P8111] (M_{\max}) is the allowed memory bound.
[P8112] This object governs:
[P8113] full-board caching,
[P8114] prefix-block caching,
[P8115] hypercell-on-demand evaluation,
[P8116] replay artifact retention,
[P8117] audit-log retention.
[P8118] The governing laws are:
[P8119] Memory Bound Law.The runtime must prefer generator-plus-residual storage to brute-force full expansion.
[P8120] Materialization Policy Law.Large crystal regions may be materialized only under explicit policy and budget.
[P8121] L.13 Parallelization maps
[P8122] The thirteenth macro-cell is parallelization maps. The branch is naturally shardable because its geometry is prefix-structured. The support skeleton already names parallelization maps explicitly. A prefix block can therefore be treated as a lawful shard.
[P8123] Define the parallelization map by[\mathcal P_{\parallel}:\mathcal B_{m,k}\to {\mathrm{Shard}_1,\dots,\mathrm{Shard}_N},]where each shard is a fixed-prefix subregion and can be evaluated independently.
[P8124] Canonical shard classes include:
[P8125] macro-district shards ((64\times64)),
[P8126] meso-block shards ((16\times16)),
[P8127] seed-block shards ((4\times4)),
[P8128] hidden-sector slice shards in the hypercrystal.
[P8129] The governing laws are:
[P8130] Shard Law.Any fixed-prefix crystal region is a lawful shard for independent computation.
[P8131] Merge Law.Parallel shards may be recombined lawfully only if they share the same generator, address normalization, and replay regime.
[P8132] L.14 Runtime harnesses
[P8133] The fourteenth macro-cell is runtime harnesses. The support runtime corpora already provide the exact harness idiom:
[P8134] deterministic resolver,
[P8135] stable topo order,
[P8136] verification gate before execution,
[P8137] runtime config, store, trace log, task scheduler, effect handlers, budget monitors, and CI replay harnesses.
[P8138] Define the runtime harness by
[P8139] [
[P8140] \mathcal H_{\mathrm{run}}
[P8141] (\Gamma,\mathrm{Store},\mathrm{Scheduler},\mathrm{Verifier},\mathrm{BudgetMon},\mathrm{TraceEmit},\Theta_H),]where:
[P8142] (\Gamma) is the runtime configuration,
[P8143] (\mathrm{Store}) is the artifact store,
[P8144] (\mathrm{Scheduler}) is the deterministic scheduler,
[P8145] (\mathrm{Verifier}) is the gate before use,
[P8146] (\mathrm{BudgetMon}) enforces resource and defect budgets,
[P8147] (\mathrm{TraceEmit}) emits audit and replay records.
[P8148] The governing laws are:
[P8149] Runtime Harness Law.Every major extraction action must run inside a typed harness with deterministic scheduling and verifier gate.
[P8150] Failure Localization Law.If a harnessed run fails, the failure must localize to the minimal scope that cannot proceed.
[P8151] L.15 Audit scripts
[P8152] The fifteenth macro-cell is audit scripts. The support corpus repeatedly states that lawful operations must emit:
[P8153] trace logs,
[P8154] hash receipts,
[P8155] corridor checks,
[P8156] MetaObserver traces,
[P8157] refusal artifacts when needed,
[P8158] and append-only audit logs.
[P8159] Define the audit-script family by
[P8160] [
[P8161] \mathcal A_{\mathrm{audit}}
[P8162] {\mathrm{TraceHashCheck},\mathrm{CorridorAudit},\mathrm{ReplayAudit},\mathrm{WitnessAudit},\mathrm{RefusalAudit},\mathrm{DeltaAudit}}.]
[P8163] An audit script must:
[P8164] read canonical artifacts,
[P8165] rerun or verify declared procedures,
[P8166] compare digests and truth classes,
[P8167] emit a new audit artifact,
[P8168] never silently upgrade ambiguous or failing states.
[P8169] The governing laws are:
[P8170] Audit Script Law.Every major runtime artifact must be consumable by an explicit audit script family.
[P8171] MetaObserver Law.Meaning-bearing runtime output requires a self-steering trace that enforces corridor budgets, replay closure, and abstain-over-guess discipline.
[P8172] L.16 Runtime seed
[P8173] The final macro-cell is the runtime seed. Appendix L must compress the whole operational stack into a replay-bearing seed:
[P8174] [
[P8175] \zeta_L
[P8176] (g_L,r_L,\eta_L,\rho_L,\Theta_L),]where:
[P8177] (g_L) is the generator core of the runtime stack,
[P8178] (r_L) is the residual shell of bounded or unresolved runtime states,
[P8179] (\eta_L) is the runtime identity digest,
[P8180] (\rho_L) is the replay/regrowth bundle.
[P8181] This runtime seed can regenerate:
[P8182] the recursive generator,
[P8183] the tensor evaluator,
[P8184] the address decoder,
[P8185] the block extractor,
[P8186] the symmetry and cancellation scanners,
[P8187] the branch explorer,
[P8188] the corridor evaluator,
[P8189] the proof compiler,
[P8190] the replay engine,
[P8191] the complexity and memory bounds,
[P8192] the parallelization map,
[P8193] the runtime harnesses,
[P8194] the audit scripts.
[P8195] The final theorem of Appendix L is therefore:
[P8196] [\boxed{\text{The extraction runtime of the 256 Crystal branch is fully lawful only when recursive generation, tensor evaluation, address decoding, block extraction, scans, branch exploration, corridor evaluation, proof compilation, replay, complexity control, memory discipline, shard maps, runtime harnesses, audit scripts, and the runtime seed form one coherent replayable computational grammar.}}]
[P8197] L.17 Canonical algorithmic form
[P8198] from dataclasses import dataclass, field
[P8199] from typing import Dict, Any, List, Literal
[P8200] TruthClass = Literal["OK", "NEAR", "AMBIG", "FAIL"]
[P8201] @dataclass
[P8202] class RuntimeArtifact:
[P8203] input_ref: Any
[P8204] mode: str
[P8205] output_state: Any
[P8206] truth: TruthClass
[P8207] metrics: Dict[str, float]
[P8208] trace: List[Dict[str, Any]] = field(default_factory=list)
[P8209] def recursive_generator(seed_ref: str, r: int, c: int, m: int) -> int:
[P8210] digits_r = base4_digits(r, m)
[P8211] digits_c = base4_digits(c, m)
[P8212] value = 0
[P8213] for rd, cd in zip(digits_r, digits_c):
[P8214] value = 4 * value + l4_eval(rd, cd)
[P8215] return value + 1
[P8216] def tensor_evaluator(X: int, Y: int, Z: int, W: int) -> List[int]:
[P8217] return hyper_tensor_state(X, Y, Z, W)
[P8218] def corridor_evaluator(defect: float, budget: float, replay_ok: bool) -> TruthClass:
[P8219] if defect == 0 and replay_ok:
[P8220] return "OK"
[P8221] if defect <= budget:
[P8222] return "NEAR"
[P8223] if not replay_ok:
[P8224] return "AMBIG"
[P8225] return "FAIL"
[P8226] def replay_engine(capsule: Dict[str, Any]) -> Dict[str, Any]:
[P8227] return {
[P8228] "trace_hash": HashTrace(capsule),
[P8229] "ledger_root": HashLedger(capsule),
[P8230] "replay_ok": True,
[P8231] }
[P8232] def build_runtime_artifact(input_ref: Any, mode: str, output_state: Any, defect: float, budget: float, replay_ok: bool) -> RuntimeArtifact:
[P8233] truth = corridor_evaluator(defect, budget, replay_ok)
[P8234] return RuntimeArtifact(
[P8235] input_ref=input_ref,
[P8236] mode=mode,
[P8237] output_state=output_state,
[P8238] truth=truth,
[P8239] metrics={"defect": defect, "budget": budget},
[P8240] trace=[{"step": "compute"}, {"step": "verify"}, {"step": "replay"}]
[P8241] )
[P8242] This canonical form compresses the appendix’s law: generate the crystal recursively, evaluate tensor states, classify under typed corridors, replay the result under deterministic capsules, and emit a trace-bearing runtime artifact.
[P8243] L.18 Appendix-level laws
[P8244] Recursive Generator Law — all visible boards must be generated exactly from the root seed.
