[P8245] Tensor Evaluator Law — all hyperstates must be evaluated by lawful seed-factorization.
[P8246] Address Decoder Law — all runtime paths begin from canonical address resolution.
[P8247] Block Extractor Law — all lawful subregions are extracted by prefix grammar.
[P8248] Symmetry Scanner Law — symmetry must be runtime-detectable and ledgered.
[P8249] Cancellation Scanner Law — cancellation structure must be runtime-detectable and ledgered.
[P8250] Branch Explorer Law — branch exploration must be typed, witnessed, and replayable.
[P8251] Corridor Evaluator Law — every runtime act returns a typed truth state.
[P8252] Proof Compiler Law — strong runtime results must compile into proof artifacts.
[P8253] Replay Engine Law — strong claims must survive deterministic replay.
[P8254] Complexity Bound Law — runtime cost must be explicit.
[P8255] Memory Bound Law — generator-plus-residual storage is the lawful default.
[P8256] Shard Law — fixed-prefix regions are lawful parallel shards.
[P8257] Runtime Harness Law — major runs must occur inside typed deterministic harnesses.
[P8258] Runtime Seed Law — the whole operational stack must compress into a replay-bearing runtime seed.
[P8259] L.19 Closing statement
[P8260] Appendix L defines the operational engine of the 256 Crystal branch. It turns the branch’s generation theorems, address laws, tensor laws, branch taxonomy, and proof/replay discipline into a lawful computational stack: recursive generator, tensor evaluator, address decoder, block extractor, symmetry and cancellation scanners, branch explorer, corridor evaluator, proof compiler, replay engine, complexity and memory discipline, parallel shard maps, runtime harnesses, audit scripts, and a runtime seed. This appendix is therefore the exact support-layer realization of Chapter 8. Without Appendix L, the branch would know what the crystal is. With Appendix L, it knows how to run it.
[P8261] Appendix L — Algorithms, Runtimes, and Extraction Procedures
[P8262] Appendix M — Certificates, Proof Bundles, and Replay Artifacts
[P8263] M.0 Appendix Function
[P8264] In the current live branch of The 256 Crystal Extraction, Appendix M is explicitly stabilized as “Certificates, Proof Bundles, and Replay Artifacts.” Its 16 macro-cells are fixed as:
[P8265] Theorem schemas
[P8266] Local proof bundles
[P8267] Global proof bundles
[P8268] Transport certificates
[P8269] Lift certificates
[P8270] Branch certificates
[P8271] Defect certificates
[P8272] Symmetry certificates
[P8273] Cancellation certificates
[P8274] Runtime certificates
[P8275] Replay artifacts
[P8276] Hash receipts
[P8277] Audit ledgers
[P8278] Verifier capsules
[P8279] Proof closure bundles
[P8280] Proof seed.
[P8281] Appendix M is therefore the exact support-layer realization of the proof-carrying and replay-closed discipline that has been implicit across the entire 256 Crystal branch. The branch already established:
[P8282] a canonical (4\times4) seed,
[P8283] an exact recursive lift law,
[P8284] a lawful 4D hyperaddress and tensor engine,
[P8285] symmetry and cancellation structures,
[P8286] branch admissibility corridors,
[P8287] runtime and extraction procedures.Appendix M now gives the branch its closure objects: how those claims are packaged, certified, replayed, audited, and ultimately accepted or refused. In the wider mechanization corpus, this is the same law expressed as the canonical pipeline[\text{compile}\to \text{run}\to \text{certify}\to \text{store}\to \text{replay}\to \text{verify},]with the non-negotiable rule that no publishable or promoted object exists outside that pipeline.
[P8288] The broader support corpus sharpens the same function with exact object schemas. LM TOME IV defines the artifact taxonomy as[\mathrm{Artifact}=(\mathrm{header},\mathrm{deps},\mathrm{payload},\mathrm{evidence},\mathrm{policy},\mathrm{integrity}),]with artifact kinds drawn from[{\mathrm{Spec},\mathrm{Evidence},\mathrm{Certificate},\mathrm{Replay},\mathrm{Ledger}},]and requires certificate bundles, replay artifacts, canonical serialization, dependency closure, verifier kernels, and deterministic replay. The FutureMath Treatise then gives the minimal schemas for CertBundle and ReplayBundle, while SELF STEER BRANCH A states the branch’s constitutional invariant in its strongest executable form:[\boxed{\text{No write without witness; no commit without replay.}}]Appendix M specializes that entire proof-carrying regime to the 256 Crystal extraction line.
[P8289] A second support line makes the role of verifier capsules explicit. The Mycelium Metro Architecture names AppM the “Replay Kernel & Verifier Capsules,” the isolated sandbox in which historical logic is rerun against frozen seeds to prove bitwise determinism and host independence. This aligns exactly with the current Appendix M title: certificates and proof bundles are not enough unless replay happens inside a lawful capsule that can reject invalid artifacts.
[P8290] Formally, define the Appendix M substrate by
[P8291] [
[P8292] \mathbb M_{\mathrm{proof}}
[P8293] (\mathcal T_{\mathrm{schema}},\mathcal B_{\mathrm{local}},\mathcal B_{\mathrm{global}},\mathcal C_{\mathrm{typed}},\mathcal R_{\mathrm{art}},\mathcal H_{\mathrm{hash}},\mathcal L_{\mathrm{audit}},\mathcal V_{\mathrm{caps}},\mathcal S_{\mathrm{seed}}),]where:
[P8294] (\mathcal T_{\mathrm{schema}}) is the theorem-schema family,
[P8295] (\mathcal B_{\mathrm{local}}) is the local proof-bundle family,
[P8296] (\mathcal B_{\mathrm{global}}) is the global proof-bundle family,
[P8297] (\mathcal C_{\mathrm{typed}}) is the typed-certificate family,
[P8298] (\mathcal R_{\mathrm{art}}) is the replay-artifact family,
[P8299] (\mathcal H_{\mathrm{hash}}) is the hash-receipt family,
[P8300] (\mathcal L_{\mathrm{audit}}) is the audit-ledger family,
[P8301] (\mathcal V_{\mathrm{caps}}) is the verifier-capsule family,
[P8302] (\mathcal S_{\mathrm{seed}}) is the proof-seed family.
[P8303] The central thesis of Appendix M is:
[P8304] [\boxed{\text{A claim in the 256 Crystal branch is not fully lawful until it is packaged as a typed theorem schema, discharged by certificates, bundled with witnesses, replayable under pinned conditions, sealed by hashes, audited by ledgers, and accepted only through verifier capsules.}}]
[P8305] M.1 Theorem schemas
[P8306] The first macro-cell is theorem schemas. The support mechanization corpus already fixes the rule that no claim is acceptable as prose alone; it must be realized as a typed artifact with declared schema IDs, dependencies, evidence references, and verifier routes. The FutureMath support also states that every claim is publishable iff its schema is registered, its certificate bundle discharges all obligations, and replay reproduces the referenced artifacts. Thus Appendix M begins by defining the theorem schema as the typed declarative carrier of a proof-bearing crystal claim.
[P8307] Define the theorem-schema object by
[P8308] [
[P8309] \Theta
[P8310] (\mathrm{SchemaID},\mathrm{ClaimClass},\mathrm{AddrScope},\mathrm{ObligationSet},\mathrm{WitnessKinds},\mathrm{ReplayReq},\mathrm{VerifierRoute},\Theta_\Theta),]where:
[P8311] (\mathrm{SchemaID}) is the unique schema identifier,
[P8312] (\mathrm{ClaimClass}) specifies the theorem type,
[P8313] (\mathrm{AddrScope}) states the crystal scope of the claim,
[P8314] (\mathrm{ObligationSet}) is the full certificate burden,
[P8315] (\mathrm{WitnessKinds}) lists required evidence artifacts,
[P8316] (\mathrm{ReplayReq}) specifies replay closure requirements,
[P8317] (\mathrm{VerifierRoute}) specifies the checker path,
[P8318] (\Theta_\Theta) is the theorem-schema truth stage.
[P8319] Canonical theorem classes in the 256 Crystal branch include:
[P8320] seed-local theorem,
[P8321] recursive-lift theorem,
[P8322] address-geometry theorem,
[P8323] hyperstate/tensor theorem,
[P8324] symmetry theorem,
[P8325] cancellation theorem,
[P8326] branch admissibility theorem,
[P8327] runtime soundness theorem.
[P8328] The governing laws are:
[P8329] Theorem Schema Law.No theorem claim in the branch is lawful unless it is typed by an explicit schema.
[P8330] Obligation Completeness Law.A theorem schema is incomplete unless it enumerates its witness, replay, and verifier obligations.
[P8331] M.2 Local proof bundles
[P8332] The second macro-cell is local proof bundles. The support corpus distinguishes local certified evidence from broad corpus-wide proof closure. Appendix M specializes this by defining proof bundles for claims whose scope is:
[P8333] one seed object,
[P8334] one (2\times2) or (4\times4) chamber,
[P8335] one address packet,
[P8336] one tensor factor,
[P8337] one local cancellation surface,
[P8338] one branch witness.
[P8339] Define the local proof bundle by
[P8340] [
[P8341] B_{\mathrm{loc}}
[P8342] (\mathrm{BundleID},\mathrm{TargetRef},\mathrm{ClaimList},\mathrm{WitnessSet},\mathrm{CertSet},\rho_{\mathrm{loc}},\Theta_{\mathrm{loc}}),]where:
[P8343] (\mathrm{TargetRef}) is a local crystal object,
[P8344] (\mathrm{ClaimList}) is the set of certified local claims,
[P8345] (\mathrm{WitnessSet}) is the minimal supporting evidence family,
[P8346] (\mathrm{CertSet}) is the certificate set,
[P8347] (\rho_{\mathrm{loc}}) is the replay bundle,
[P8348] (\Theta_{\mathrm{loc}}) is the bundle truth stage.
[P8349] Examples include:
[P8350] a local holography proof bundle for one (2\times2) chamber,
[P8351] a seed symmetry bundle for one row orbit,
[P8352] an address proof for one cell or block prefix,
[P8353] a hypercell tensor-state bundle for one point.
[P8354] The governing laws are:
[P8355] Local Bundle Law.A local crystal claim is lawful only when its proof obligations close within a local proof bundle.
[P8356] Minimal Witness Law.Local bundles should use the smallest witness family sufficient for replay-closed verification.
[P8357] M.3 Global proof bundles
[P8358] The third macro-cell is global proof bundles. Some claims are not local: they range over the full visible branch, the full (256^4) hypercrystal, a whole symmetry class, a whole branch class, or the full extraction pipeline. These require bundles that carry larger dependency closure and broader replay scope.
[P8359] Define the global proof bundle by
[P8360] [
[P8361] B_{\mathrm{glob}}
[P8362] (\mathrm{BundleID},\mathrm{ScopeRef},\mathrm{ClaimGraph},\mathrm{DepClosure},\mathrm{CertClosure},\rho_{\mathrm{glob}},\Theta_{\mathrm{glob}}),]where:
[P8363] (\mathrm{ScopeRef}) is the global crystal scope,
[P8364] (\mathrm{ClaimGraph}) is the typed claim dependency graph,
[P8365] (\mathrm{DepClosure}) is the closed dependency manifest,
[P8366] (\mathrm{CertClosure}) is the closed certificate set,
[P8367] (\rho_{\mathrm{glob}}) is the replay bundle,
[P8368] (\Theta_{\mathrm{glob}}) is the bundle truth stage.
[P8369] A global bundle must satisfy the support corpus’s explicit closure rules:
[P8370] all referenced dependencies are present,
[P8371] all hashes match canonical serialization,
[P8372] all replay pointers are pinned,
[P8373] all verifier obligations are discharged.
[P8374] The governing laws are:
[P8375] Global Bundle Law.A global crystal theorem is lawful only when its dependency and certificate closures are explicit.
[P8376] No Hidden Dependency Law.No proof bundle may rely on undeclared dependencies or witness sources.
[P8377] M.4 Transport certificates
[P8378] The fourth macro-cell is transport certificates. The larger transport corpus requires that any transport claim carry explicit witness and replay structure, especially for EQUIV, DUAL, and MIGRATE relations. Appendix M specializes this into the crystal branch’s transport layer:
[P8379] visible coordinate transports,
[P8380] hidden-axis transports,
[P8381] tensor-channel transports,
[P8382] branch migration transports,
[P8383] metro routing transports.
[P8384] Define the transport certificate by
[P8385] [
[P8386] C_{\mathrm{trans}}
[P8387] (\mathrm{CID},\mathrm{SrcRef},\mathrm{DstRef},\mathrm{TransportClass},\delta_{\mathrm{trans}},\mathrm{WitnessSet},\rho_{\mathrm{trans}},\Theta_{\mathrm{trans}}),]where:
[P8388] (\mathrm{TransportClass}) is the kind of transport,
[P8389] (\delta_{\mathrm{trans}}) is transport defect,
[P8390] (\mathrm{WitnessSet}) is the supporting evidence,
[P8391] (\rho_{\mathrm{trans}}) is the replay bundle,
[P8392] (\Theta_{\mathrm{trans}}) is the truth stage.
[P8393] Transport certificates must prove:
[P8394] the two carriers are linked by a typed lawful map,
[P8395] exact or bounded invariants are preserved,
[P8396] the route replays under the active corridor.
[P8397] The governing laws are:
[P8398] Transport Certificate Law.No transport in the crystal branch is lawful without a transport certificate or a typed downgrade into NEAR / AMBIG / FAIL.
[P8399] M.5 Lift certificates
[P8400] The fifth macro-cell is lift certificates. The recursive visible branch and the full hypercrystal both require certificates proving that:
[P8401] the recursive substitution law was used correctly,
[P8402] the digitwise value theorem was preserved,
[P8403] the hyperaddress and hidden coordinates were reconstructed lawfully,
[P8404] tensor-state assembly matched the canonical pairing scheme.
[P8405] Define the lift certificate by
[P8406] [
[P8407] C_{\mathrm{lift}}
[P8408] (\mathrm{CID},\mathrm{SeedRef},\mathrm{LiftRef},\mathrm{ScaleRef},\mathrm{InvariantProofs},\rho_{\mathrm{lift}},\Theta_{\mathrm{lift}}),]where:
[P8409] (\mathrm{SeedRef}) points to (L_4),
[P8410] (\mathrm{LiftRef}) points to the recursive/tensor lift law,
[P8411] (\mathrm{ScaleRef}) identifies the target scale or projection,
[P8412] (\mathrm{InvariantProofs}) proves preservation of row, column, diagonal, address, or tensor invariants,
[P8413] (\rho_{\mathrm{lift}}) is replay data,
[P8414] (\Theta_{\mathrm{lift}}) is the truth stage.
[P8415] The governing laws are:
[P8416] Lift Certificate Law.No recursive or tensor lift claim is lawful without an explicit lift certificate.
[P8417] Seed-Anchored Lift Law.Every lift certificate must reference the canonical seed and the exact lift law used.
[P8418] M.6 Branch certificates
[P8419] The sixth macro-cell is branch certificates. Appendix I already defined branch admissibility corridors and Appendix J defined exceptional branches and no-go witnesses. Appendix M now provides the closure object by which a branch status becomes certifiable.
[P8420] Define the branch certificate by
[P8421] [
[P8422] C_{\mathrm{branch}}
[P8423] (\mathrm{CID},\mathrm{BranchRef},\mathrm{CorridorClass},\mathrm{WitnessBundle},\mathrm{DefectLedger},\rho_{\mathrm{branch}},\Theta_{\mathrm{branch}}),]where:
[P8424] (\mathrm{CorridorClass}) is Exact / Bounded / Probe / Quarantine,
[P8425] (\mathrm{WitnessBundle}) is the evidence set,
[P8426] (\mathrm{DefectLedger}) is the branch burden report,
[P8427] (\rho_{\mathrm{branch}}) is the replay history,
[P8428] (\Theta_{\mathrm{branch}}) is the resulting truth class.
[P8429] This certificate is the appendix-level closure of branch admissibility.
[P8430] The law is:
[P8431] Branch Certificate Law.A branch is not lawfully stable, bounded, ambiguous, or forbidden unless its status closes in a certificate-bearing object.
[P8432] M.7 Defect certificates
[P8433] The seventh macro-cell is defect certificates. The branch already carries:
[P8434] drift metrics,
[P8435] defect norms,
[P8436] tensor budgets,
[P8437] branch burdens,
[P8438] approximation envelopes,
[P8439] defect hyperplanes. Appendix M now defines the proof-carrying object that certifies those failures or bounded deviations.
[P8440] Define the defect certificate by
[P8441] [
[P8442] C_{\mathrm{def}}
[P8443] (\mathrm{CID},\mathrm{TargetRef},\mathrm{DefectClass},\delta,\mathrm{NormRef},\mathrm{BudgetRef},\rho_{\mathrm{def}},\Theta_{\mathrm{def}}),]where:
[P8444] (\mathrm{DefectClass}) identifies the kind of defect,
[P8445] (\delta) is the measured value,
[P8446] (\mathrm{NormRef}) identifies the defect norm,
[P8447] (\mathrm{BudgetRef}) identifies the corridor threshold,
[P8448] (\rho_{\mathrm{def}}) is the replay bundle,
[P8449] (\Theta_{\mathrm{def}}) is the truth stage.
[P8450] The law is:
[P8451] Defect Certificate Law.No strong defect claim is lawful unless its norm, budget, and measured value are all certified and replayable.
[P8452] M.8 Symmetry certificates
[P8453] The eighth macro-cell is symmetry certificates. Appendix G already proved the symmetry grammar of the branch. Appendix M now packages that grammar into certifiable form.
[P8454] Define the symmetry certificate by
[P8455] [
[P8456] C_{\mathrm{sym}}
[P8457] (\mathrm{CID},\mathrm{TargetRef},\mathrm{SymmetryClass},\mathrm{InvariantSet},\delta_{\mathrm{sym}},\rho_{\mathrm{sym}},\Theta_{\mathrm{sym}}),]where:
[P8458] (\mathrm{SymmetryClass}) identifies the relevant orbit/stabilizer family,
[P8459] (\mathrm{InvariantSet}) lists preserved structures,
[P8460] (\delta_{\mathrm{sym}}) records exact or bounded defect,
[P8461] (\rho_{\mathrm{sym}}) is the replay bundle,
[P8462] (\Theta_{\mathrm{sym}}) is the truth stage.
[P8463] The law is:
[P8464] Symmetry Certificate Law.No strong symmetry classification is lawful without a replay-bearing symmetry certificate.
[P8465] M.9 Cancellation certificates
[P8466] The ninth macro-cell is cancellation certificates. Appendix H defined local cancellation objects, dual zero classes, toroidal cancellation structure, zero-ratio laws, and dual-boundary transport. Appendix M now closes those claims into proof-carrying artifacts.
[P8467] Define the cancellation certificate by
[P8468] [
[P8469] C_{\mathrm{cancel}}
[P8470] (\mathrm{CID},\mathrm{TargetRef},\mathrm{ZeroClass},\mathrm{TorusClass},\delta_{\mathrm{cancel}},\rho_{\mathrm{cancel}},\Theta_{\mathrm{cancel}}),]where:
[P8471] (\mathrm{ZeroClass}) identifies the local or global cancellation class,
[P8472] (\mathrm{TorusClass}) identifies hidden-sector toroidal status,
[P8473] (\delta_{\mathrm{cancel}}) is the cancellation defect,
[P8474] (\rho_{\mathrm{cancel}}) is the replay bundle,
[P8475] (\Theta_{\mathrm{cancel}}) is the truth stage.
[P8476] The law is:
[P8477] Cancellation Certificate Law.No zero, torus, or balance-surface claim is lawful without a typed cancellation certificate.
[P8478] M.10 Runtime certificates
[P8479] The tenth macro-cell is runtime certificates. Appendix L already defined the computational engine—recursive generator, tensor evaluator, corridor evaluator, proof compiler, replay engine, runtime harnesses, and audit scripts. Appendix M packages those runtime acts into certificates that can be checked independently.
[P8480] Define the runtime certificate by
[P8481] [
[P8482] C_{\mathrm{run}}
[P8483] (\mathrm{CID},\mathrm{CapsuleRef},\mathrm{EnvPin},\mathrm{TraceHash},\mathrm{BudgetReport},\rho_{\mathrm{run}},\Theta_{\mathrm{run}}),]where:
[P8484] (\mathrm{CapsuleRef}) identifies the runtime capsule,
[P8485] (\mathrm{EnvPin}) is the environment fingerprint,
[P8486] (\mathrm{TraceHash}) seals the execution trace,
[P8487] (\mathrm{BudgetReport}) records time/memory/defect budget use,
[P8488] (\rho_{\mathrm{run}}) is replay information,
[P8489] (\Theta_{\mathrm{run}}) is the runtime truth stage.
[P8490] The law is:
[P8491] Runtime Certificate Law.No extraction run in the branch is strongly lawful unless it closes in a runtime certificate.
[P8492] M.11 Replay artifacts
[P8493] The eleventh macro-cell is the heart of the appendix: replay artifacts. The support mechanization corpus gives the exact object model: a ReplayArtifact is a canonical recipe DAG plus environment contract and transcript hashes sufficient for independent reconstruction; a ReplayBundle must include seeds, initial artifacts, deterministic stage transcript hashes, environment hash, policy hash, canonical outputs, and final artifact hash.
[P8494] Define the replay artifact by
[P8495] [
[P8496] R_M
[P8497] (\mathrm{RID},\mathrm{RecipeDAG},\mathrm{EnvHash},\mathrm{PolicyHash},\mathrm{SeedSet},\mathrm{TranscriptHashes},\mathrm{OutputHash},\Theta_R),]where:
[P8498] (\mathrm{RecipeDAG}) is the replay program,
[P8499] (\mathrm{EnvHash}) pins the environment,
[P8500] (\mathrm{PolicyHash}) pins corridor and threshold policy,
[P8501] (\mathrm{SeedSet}) is the seed family,
[P8502] (\mathrm{TranscriptHashes}) are deterministic stage hashes,
[P8503] (\mathrm{OutputHash}) seals the final artifact,
[P8504] (\Theta_R) is the replay truth stage.
[P8505] This is the appendix-level exact object that all stronger claims ultimately depend on.
[P8506] The law is:
[P8507] Replay Artifact Law.No strong crystal claim is lawful unless it admits a deterministic replay artifact.
[P8508] Replay Semantics Law.A published or promoted claim is meaningful only insofar as its replay artifact reconstructs the same artifacts under pinned conditions.
[P8509] M.12 Hash receipts
[P8510] The twelfth macro-cell is hash receipts. The support corpus already treats hashes as non-negotiable:
[P8511] canonical serialization,
[P8512] artifact hash in every artifact header,
[P8513] dependency Merkle roots,
[P8514] trace hashes,
[P8515] ledger roots,
[P8516] signature envelopes,
[P8517] final artifact digests.
[P8518] Define the hash receipt by
[P8519] [
[P8520] H_M
[P8521] (\mathrm{HID},\mathrm{TargetRef},\mathrm{ArtifactHash},\mathrm{DepsRoot},\mathrm{TraceHash},\mathrm{LedgerRoot},\Theta_H),]where:
[P8522] (\mathrm{ArtifactHash}) seals the canonical artifact,
[P8523] (\mathrm{DepsRoot}) is the dependency closure root,
[P8524] (\mathrm{TraceHash}) seals the computation,
[P8525] (\mathrm{LedgerRoot}) seals the conservative accounting.
[P8526] The law is:
[P8527] Hash Receipt Law.Every proof-carrying artifact in the branch must emit a hash receipt binding content, dependencies, trace, and ledger.
[P8528] Canonical Bytes Law.Hash receipts are only lawful if computed on canonical serialization.
[P8529] M.13 Audit ledgers
[P8530] The thirteenth macro-cell is audit ledgers. The support corpus treats audit logging itself as a proof artifact:
[P8531] every operation is logged,
[P8532] every threshold decision records interval and slack witnesses,
[P8533] every obligation is recorded,
[P8534] every repair or projection is explicit,
[P8535] logs are sealed by hash chains and linked to replay traces and cert bundles.
[P8536] Define the audit ledger by
[P8537] [
[P8538] L_M
[P8539] (\mathrm{LID},\mathrm{EventSeq},\mathrm{ThresholdEvents},\mathrm{ObligationEvents},\mathrm{RepairEvents},\mathrm{HashChain},\Theta_L),]where:
[P8540] (\mathrm{EventSeq}) is the append-only event history,
[P8541] (\mathrm{ThresholdEvents}) stores all decisive comparisons,
[P8542] (\mathrm{ObligationEvents}) stores proof and witness duties,
[P8543] (\mathrm{RepairEvents}) stores corrections or migrations,
[P8544] (\mathrm{HashChain}) seals chronology.
[P8545] The law is:
[P8546] Audit Ledger Law.Every major proof, replay, or runtime action must write to an append-only audit ledger.
[P8547] No Post-Hoc Certainty Law.Later reinterpretation may not silently tighten or revise a logged decision without a new certified artifact.
[P8548] M.14 Verifier capsules
[P8549] The fourteenth macro-cell is verifier capsules. The Mycelium Metro Architecture names AppM the home of Replay Kernel & Verifier Capsules and describes it as the hyper-isolated VM sandbox that reruns historical logic against frozen entropy seeds to prove bitwise determinism and host-OS independence. This is exactly the runtime closure object that Appendix M needs.
[P8550] Define the verifier capsule by
[P8551] [
[P8552] V_c
[P8553] (\mathrm{VID},\mathrm{CapsuleBody},\mathrm{EnvFingerprint},\mathrm{SeedRegs},\mathrm{VerifierKernel},\mathrm{ExpectedDigests},\Theta_V),]where:
[P8554] (\mathrm{CapsuleBody}) is the sealed executable recipe,
[P8555] (\mathrm{EnvFingerprint}) pins environment and dependencies,
[P8556] (\mathrm{SeedRegs}) pins all explicit seeds,
[P8557] (\mathrm{VerifierKernel}) is the bounded trusted checker,
[P8558] (\mathrm{ExpectedDigests}) records the replay target,
[P8559] (\Theta_V) is the capsule truth stage.
[P8560] The governing laws are:
[P8561] Verifier Capsule Law.A strong branch artifact must be checkable inside a pinned verifier capsule.
[P8562] Host Independence Law.If a claim cannot survive rerun under a verifier capsule, it is not strong truth in the branch.
[P8563] M.15 Proof closure bundles
[P8564] The fifteenth macro-cell is proof closure bundles. The support corpus repeatedly insists that a strong claim is publishable only when:
[P8565] its schema is registered,
[P8566] its certificate bundle discharges obligations,
[P8567] the verifier validates the bundle within bounds,
[P8568] replay reproduces the referenced artifacts.Appendix M formalizes the object that closes all these obligations at once.
[P8569] Define the proof closure bundle by
[P8570] [
[P8571] B_{\mathrm{close}}
[P8572] (\mathrm{BundleID},\Theta,\mathcal C,\mathcal R,\mathcal L,\mathrm{VerifierRoute},\Theta_B),]where:
[P8573] (\Theta) is the theorem schema set,
[P8574] (\mathcal C) is the certificate closure,
[P8575] (\mathcal R) is the replay closure,
[P8576] (\mathcal L) is the audit-ledger anchor,
[P8577] (\mathrm{VerifierRoute}) is the bounded verifier path,
[P8578] (\Theta_B) is the bundle truth stage.
[P8579] A proof closure bundle is lawful only if all open obligations are discharged or explicitly downgraded into NEAR / AMBIG / FAIL with residual and evidence plans.
[P8580] The governing laws are:
[P8581] Proof Closure Law.No theorem or runtime artifact is fully lawful until its obligations close in one proof closure bundle.
[P8582] No Partial Acceptance Law.A missing certificate, missing replay artifact, or missing ledger anchor forbids strong acceptance.
[P8583] M.16 Proof seed
[P8584] The final macro-cell is the proof seed. Appendix M must compress its whole proof-carrying regime into a replay-bearing seed:
[P8585] [
[P8586] \zeta_M
[P8587] (g_M,r_M,\eta_M,\rho_M,\Theta_M),]where:
[P8588] (g_M) is the generator core of theorem schemas, certificate classes, replay artifacts, hash receipts, audit ledgers, verifier capsules, and proof closure bundles,
[P8589] (r_M) is the residual shell of bounded or unresolved proof obligations,
[P8590] (\eta_M) is the proof-system identity digest,
[P8591] (\rho_M) is the replay/regrowth bundle.
[P8592] This proof seed can regenerate:
[P8593] theorem schemas,
[P8594] local and global proof bundles,
[P8595] typed certificate families,
[P8596] replay artifacts,
[P8597] hash receipts,
[P8598] audit ledgers,
[P8599] verifier capsules,
[P8600] proof closure bundles.
[P8601] The final theorem of Appendix M is therefore:
[P8602] [\boxed{\text{The proof-carrying closure layer of the 256 Crystal branch is fully lawful only when theorem schemas, proof bundles, typed certificates, replay artifacts, hash receipts, audit ledgers, verifier capsules, proof closure bundles, and the proof seed form one coherent replayable proof grammar.}}]
[P8603] M.17 Canonical algorithmic form
[P8604] from dataclasses import dataclass, field
[P8605] from typing import Dict, Any, List, Literal
[P8606] TruthClass = Literal["OK", "NEAR", "AMBIG", "FAIL"]
[P8607] @dataclass
[P8608] class ReplayArtifact:
[P8609] recipe_dag: Dict[str, Any]
[P8610] env_hash: str
[P8611] policy_hash: str
[P8612] seed_set: Dict[str, Any]
[P8613] transcript_hashes: List[str]
[P8614] output_hash: str
[P8615] truth: TruthClass
[P8616] @dataclass
[P8617] class ProofClosureBundle:
[P8618] theorem_schema: Dict[str, Any]
[P8619] cert_bundle: Dict[str, Any]
[P8620] replay_artifact: ReplayArtifact
[P8621] audit_anchor: str
[P8622] verifier_route: List[str]
[P8623] truth: TruthClass
[P8624] def build_replay_artifact(recipe_dag, env_hash, policy_hash, seed_set, transcript_hashes, output_hash) -> ReplayArtifact:
[P8625] return ReplayArtifact(
[P8626] recipe_dag=recipe_dag,
[P8627] env_hash=env_hash,
[P8628] policy_hash=policy_hash,
[P8629] seed_set=seed_set,
[P8630] transcript_hashes=transcript_hashes,
[P8631] output_hash=output_hash,
[P8632] truth="OK"
[P8633] )
[P8634] def build_proof_closure(theorem_schema, cert_bundle, replay_artifact, audit_anchor, verifier_route) -> ProofClosureBundle:
[P8635] return ProofClosureBundle(
[P8636] theorem_schema=theorem_schema,
[P8637] cert_bundle=cert_bundle,
[P8638] replay_artifact=replay_artifact,
[P8639] audit_anchor=audit_anchor,
[P8640] verifier_route=verifier_route,
[P8641] truth="OK"
[P8642] )
[P8643] This canonical form compresses the appendix’s law: encode the theorem as a schema, discharge it with certificates, reconstruct it with replay artifacts, anchor it in an audit log, and close it under a verifier route.
[P8644] M.18 Appendix-level laws
[P8645] Theorem Schema Law — no theorem claim is lawful without a typed schema.
[P8646] Local Bundle Law — local crystal claims close in local proof bundles.
[P8647] Global Bundle Law — global crystal claims require dependency and certificate closure.
[P8648] Transport Certificate Law — transport claims require typed transport certificates.
[P8649] Lift Certificate Law — recursive and tensor lift claims require lift certificates.
[P8650] Branch Certificate Law — branch admissibility requires branch certificates.
[P8651] Defect Certificate Law — defect claims require normed and budgeted certificates.
[P8652] Symmetry Certificate Law — symmetry classifications require replay-bearing certificates.
[P8653] Cancellation Certificate Law — cancellation and dual-zero claims require certificates.
[P8654] Runtime Certificate Law — strong runtime outputs require runtime certificates.
[P8655] Replay Artifact Law — strong claims require deterministic replay artifacts.
[P8656] Hash Receipt Law — content, dependencies, traces, and ledgers must be hash-sealed.
[P8657] Audit Ledger Law — all major actions must be recorded in append-only audit ledgers.
[P8658] Verifier Capsule Law — strong claims must be checkable inside pinned verifier capsules.
[P8659] Proof Seed Law — the entire proof-carrying grammar must compress into a replay-bearing seed.
[P8660] M.19 Closing statement
[P8661] Appendix M defines the proof-carrying closure layer of the 256 Crystal branch. It begins by typing theorem schemas, then packages local and global claims into proof bundles, specializes certificates for transport, lift, branch, defect, symmetry, cancellation, and runtime claims, formalizes replay artifacts and hash receipts, records everything inside audit ledgers, checks strong claims in verifier capsules, and finally closes the whole system in proof closure bundles and a proof seed. This appendix is therefore the exact support-layer realization of the branch’s strongest epistemic invariant: no write without witness, no commit without replay. Without Appendix M, the crystal could generate, measure, and classify itself—but it could not yet prove that those acts deserve to persist. With Appendix M, the crystal acquires its proof grammar.
[P8662] Appendix M — Certificates, Proof Bundles, and Replay Artifacts
[P8663] Appendix N — Visualization, Metro Maps, and Neural Atlas
[P8664] N.0 Appendix Function
[P8665] In the current live branch of The 256 Crystal Extraction, Appendix N is explicitly stabilized as “Visualization, Metro Maps, and Neural Atlas.” Its 16 macro-cells are fixed as:
[P8666] 2D board render grammar
[P8667] 4D projection grammar
[P8668] Chapter metro
[P8669] Appendix metro
[P8670] Neural atlas overlay
[P8671] Block heatmaps
[P8672] Symmetry plots
[P8673] Defect maps
[P8674] Route trees
[P8675] Cancellation torus render
[P8676] Hypercube render
[P8677] Slice viewer
[P8678] Dashboard layouts
[P8679] Publication figures
[P8680] Replay visual logs
[P8681] Visual seed.
[P8682] Appendix N is therefore the first appendix in the 256 Crystal branch where the crystal’s exact mathematics is systematically translated into a lawful visual atlas. The supporting branch already proves that the (256\times256) board is the visible carrier of a 4D manifold
[P8683] [
[P8684] \Sigma_{256}
[P8685] {(X,Y,Z,W)\in{0,\dots,255}^4:\ Z=X\boxplus Y,\ W=X\boxminus Y},
[P8686] ]
[P8687] that its nodes admit the metro schema
[P8688] [
[P8689] \mathcal N(r,c)=\bigl(\Theta,\kappa,\ell,\beta,\Pi\bigr),
[P8690] ]
[P8691] that it decomposes into macro-, meso-, and local districts by the prefix ladder, that its phase support
[P8692] [
[P8693] \mathcal P_{256}
[P8694] {(Z,W): z_t\equiv w_t \pmod 2\ \forall t}]has size (4096) with constant fiber size (16), and that the whole system supports exact rail, hub, tunnel, Aether, and Zero-Point overlays. Appendix N is where those structures become explicit render grammars rather than only equations.
[P8695] Formally, define the Appendix N substrate by
[P8696] [
[P8697] \mathbb N_{\mathrm{viz}}
[P8698] (\mathcal R_{2D},\mathcal P_{4D},\mathcal G_{\mathrm{metro}},\mathcal A_{\mathrm{atlas}},\mathcal H_{\mathrm{heat}},\mathcal S_{\mathrm{sym}},\mathcal D_{\mathrm{def}},\mathcal T_{\mathrm{tree}},\mathcal V_{\mathrm{seed}}),]where:
[P8699] (\mathcal R_{2D}) is the visible-board render family,
[P8700] (\mathcal P_{4D}) is the 4D projection family,
[P8701] (\mathcal G_{\mathrm{metro}}) is the metro-graph family,
[P8702] (\mathcal A_{\mathrm{atlas}}) is the neural-atlas overlay family,
[P8703] (\mathcal H_{\mathrm{heat}}) is the heatmap family,
[P8704] (\mathcal S_{\mathrm{sym}}) is the symmetry-plot family,
[P8705] (\mathcal D_{\mathrm{def}}) is the defect-map family,
[P8706] (\mathcal T_{\mathrm{tree}}) is the route-tree family,
[P8707] (\mathcal V_{\mathrm{seed}}) is the visual-seed family.
[P8708] The central thesis of Appendix N is:
[P8709] [\boxed{\text{A crystal visualization is lawful only when every rendered layer is an explicit projection, aggregation, or annotation of the exact address, phase, nexus, district, and replay structure of the branch.}}]
[P8710] N.1 2D board render grammar
[P8711] The first macro-cell is the 2D board render grammar. The visible board is
[P8712] [
[P8713] \mathcal B_{256}={(r,c):0\le r,c\le 255},
[P8714] ]
[P8715] with value law
[P8716] [
[P8717] L_{256}(r,c)-1
[P8718] 64,\ell_4(r_3,c_3)+16,\ell_4(r_2,c_2)+4,\ell_4(r_1,c_1)+\ell_4(r_0,c_0),]where[\ell_4=L_4-1.]A lawful 2D rendering must therefore attach visual channels directly to:
[P8719] address ((r,c)),
[P8720] value (L_{256}(r,c)),
[P8721] district prefix (\ell(r,c)),
[P8722] and any explicit overlay such as nexus mask or hub score.
[P8723] Define the 2D render object by
[P8724] [
[P8725] R_{2D}
[P8726] (\mathrm{RID},\mathcal B_{256},\mathsf{Color}(L_{256}),\mathsf{Grid}(\ell),\mathsf{Overlay}(\beta,\Pi),\Theta_R),]where:
[P8727] (\mathsf{Color}(L_{256})) assigns a color scale to value or transformed value,
[P8728] (\mathsf{Grid}(\ell)) draws district boundaries from the prefix ladder,
[P8729] (\mathsf{Overlay}(\beta,\Pi)) superimposes nexus and hub information,
[P8730] (\Theta_R) is the render truth stage.
[P8731] The law is:
[P8732] 2D Render Law.The board may be rendered only by channels explicitly tied to address, value, and legal overlays.
[P8733] N.2 4D projection grammar
[P8734] The second macro-cell is the 4D projection grammar. The branch’s exact 4D coordinate law is[\Theta(r,c)=\bigl(X,Y,Z,W\bigr)=\bigl(r,\ c,\ r\boxplus c,\ r\boxminus c\bigr),]with[u\boxplus v:=\sum_{t=0}^3 4^t((u_t+v_t)\bmod 4),\qquadu\boxminus v:=\sum_{t=0}^3 4^t((u_t-v_t)\bmod 4).]Thus every lawful visualization beyond the visible board must be one of the explicit projections or sections of this coordinate law.
[P8735] Define the projection family by
[P8736] [
[P8737] \mathcal P_{4D}
[P8738] {\pi_{XY},\pi_{XYZ},\pi_{XYW},\pi_{ZW},\pi_q},]where:
[P8739] (\pi_{XY}) gives the visible square carrier,
[P8740] (\pi_{XYZ}) and (\pi_{XYW}) give 3D visible shadows,
[P8741] (\pi_{ZW}) gives the phase-support / Cloud field,
[P8742] (\pi_q) gives (q)-digit prefix truncations[\Theta^{(q)}=(\pi_q(X),\pi_q(Y),\pi_q(Z),\pi_q(W)).]
[P8743] The law is:
[P8744] 4D Projection Law.A lawful higher-dimensional rendering must be an explicit projection or truncation of ((X,Y,Z,W)), never an untyped pictorial analogy.
[P8745] N.3 Chapter metro
[P8746] The third macro-cell is the chapter metro. The 9 chapters of the current manuscript form a (3\times3) macro-crystal:[\begin{array}{ccc}Ch1 & Ch2 & Ch3\Ch4 & Ch5 & Ch6\Ch7 & Ch8 & Ch9\end{array}]with the explicit logical route[L_4\to\text{Transform Algebra}\to\text{Gate-4 / Tesseract}\to4\to16\to64\to256\to\text{Address Geometry}\to256^4\to\text{Symmetry / Cancellation / Branching}\to\text{Extraction Engine}\to\text{Neural Metro / Return Seed}.]A lawful chapter metro rendering must display both the macro-grid and the dependency path.
[P8747] Define the chapter metro graph by[\mathcal G_{9}=(V_9,E_9),\qquadV_9={Ch1,\dots,Ch9},]with edge classes:
[P8748] kernel edge,
[P8749] transform edge,
[P8750] embedding edge,
[P8751] lift edge,
[P8752] address edge,
[P8753] tensor edge,
[P8754] symmetry edge,
[P8755] runtime edge,
[P8756] return edge.
[P8757] The law is:
[P8758] Chapter Metro Law.The 9-chapter body must be visualized as a dependency graph and not merely as a list.
[P8759] N.4 Appendix metro
[P8760] The fourth macro-cell is the appendix metro. The same support crystal that organizes the appendices[\begin{array}{cccc}A & B & C & D\E & F & G & H\I & J & K & L\M & N & O & P\end{array}]is the exact atlas substrate of the current 256 Crystal branch. Appendix N itself is the visual/atlas node of that grid. A lawful appendix-metro render must therefore show:
[P8761] geometric support-crystal position,
[P8762] semantic roles of appendices,
[P8763] dependency routes from A→…→P,
[P8764] and the special function of N as visualization and atlas overlay.
[P8765] Define the appendix metro graph by[\mathcal G_{16}=(V_{16},E_{16}),\qquadV_{16}={A,\dots,P}.]
[P8766] The law is:
[P8767] Appendix Metro Law.The appendix support system must be visualized as a lawful crystal of dependencies, not as an arbitrary appendix list.
[P8768] N.5 Neural atlas overlay
[P8769] The fifth macro-cell is the neural atlas overlay. The branch’s own metro object schema is already explicit:[\mathcal N(r,c)=\bigl(\Theta,\kappa,\ell,\beta,\Pi\bigr),]with[\Theta=(X,Y,Z,W),][\kappa=\bigl(L_{256}(r,c),\operatorname{orb}{C,R,H,S,P}(r,c)\bigr),][\ell=\Big((r_3,c_3),\ (r_3r_2,c_3c_2),\ (r_3r_2r_1,c_3c_2c_1),\ (r_3r_2r_1r_0,c_3c_2c_1c_0)\Big),][\beta\in{0,1}^{11},\qquad\Pi=\sum{q=1}^4 4^{q-1}|\beta^{(q)}|_1.]This schema is precisely the neural-atlas object of the branch. Appendix N takes it as the canonical node overlay.
[P8770] Define the neural-atlas overlay by
[P8771] [
[P8772] A_{\mathrm{neural}}
[P8773] (\Theta,\kappa,\ell,\beta,\Pi,\mathsf{RenderRules},\Theta_A).]
[P8774] The law is:
[P8775] Neural Atlas Law.A neural atlas node is lawful only if it renders the exact metro schema ((\Theta,\kappa,\ell,\beta,\Pi)).
[P8776] N.6 Block heatmaps
[P8777] The sixth macro-cell is block heatmaps. The branch’s district structure is exact:
[P8778] 16 macro districts of size (64\times64),
[P8779] 256 meso districts of size (16\times16),
[P8780] 4096 local districts of size (4\times4).A lawful heatmap must therefore aggregate scores at one of these exact district scales.
[P8781] Define the heatmap family by
[P8782] [
[P8783] H_{\mathrm{blk}}^{(q)}
[P8784] {\mathsf{Heat}{\mathrm{value}},\mathsf{Heat}{\mathrm{nexus}},\mathsf{Heat}{\mathrm{hub}},\mathsf{Heat}{\mathrm{defect}}}_{q},]where (q\in{1,2,3,4}) is the prefix depth.
[P8785] Examples:
[P8786] value heatmap: average or mode of (L_{256}(r,c)) in the block,
[P8787] nexus heatmap: density of (\beta)-bits,
[P8788] hub heatmap: block-aggregated persistence score (\Pi),
[P8789] defect heatmap: branch- or phase-support anomaly density.
[P8790] The law is:
[P8791] Block Heatmap Law.A lawful heatmap must aggregate over exact prefix districts, not arbitrary raster bins.
[P8792] N.7 Symmetry plots
[P8793] The seventh macro-cell is symmetry plots. The node schema already includes[\kappa(r,c)=\bigl(L_{256}(r,c),\operatorname{orb}_{C,R,H,S,P}(r,c)\bigr),]which means the branch’s visual atlas can and should render symmetry through orbit structure. Appendix G already classified the relevant symmetry families and automorphism classes; Appendix N turns those into plots.

[P8798] A lawful symmetry plot may:
[P8799] color cells by orbit class,

[P8801] display quadrant-rotation sectors,
[P8802] lift symmetry classes into the ((Z,W))-plane.
[P8803] The law is:
[P8804] Symmetry Plot Law.A symmetry visualization is lawful only when every color or geometry layer is indexed by a typed symmetry class or orbit.
[P8805] N.8 Defect maps

[P8809] branch fractures,

[P8811] and explicit metric layers. A lawful visual atlas therefore includes defect maps tied to those exact objects.

[P8817] hyperplane maps of carry or phase fractures,

[P8820] corridor maps showing OK / NEAR / AMBIG / FAIL regions.
[P8821] The law is:
[P8822] Defect Map Law.Every defect visualization must be tied to an explicit defect functional, hyperplane, or corridor classification.
[P8823] N.9 Route trees

[P8832] tunnel options,
[P8833] replay path,

[P8841] N.10 Cancellation torus render
[P8842] The tenth macro-cell is cancellation torus render. Appendix H already proved that the hidden ((Z,W))-sector is a lawful 2-torus-style cancellation manifold. Appendix N now defines the visual grammar for that manifold.
[P8843] Define the torus render by

[P8847] (\mathcal P_{256}) is the phase support,

[P8849] (\mathsf{FiberCount}) displays the constant fiber size 16,
[P8850] (\mathsf{TunnelOverlay}) draws Circle and Triangle rail actions.

[P8852] [
[P8853] \mathcal P_{256}
[P8854] {(Z,W): z_t\equiv w_t\pmod 2},\qquad|\mathcal P_{256}|=4096,]and every phase site has exactly 16 preimages.
[P8855] The law is:
[P8856] Cancellation Torus Render Law.The hidden torus may be rendered only through the exact phase-support lattice and its fiber/tunnel structure.
[P8857] N.11 Hypercube render
[P8858] The eleventh macro-cell is hypercube render. Appendix C already fixed the derived but lawful Gray-coded hypercube embedding of the (4\times4) seed into the 16 vertices of a 4-cube. Appendix N now declares the visualization grammar for that discrete 4D seed shadow.
[P8859] Define the hypercube render by
[P8860] [
[P8861] R_{\mathrm{cube}}
[P8862] (\mathrm{VertexSet},\mathrm{CellLabels},\mathrm{EdgeSet},\mathrm{FaceClasses},\Theta_R),]where:
[P8863] (\mathrm{VertexSet}) is the 16-vertex 4-cube,
[P8864] (\mathrm{CellLabels}) map visible seed cells to vertices,
[P8865] (\mathrm{EdgeSet}) follows lawful move families,
[P8866] (\mathrm{FaceClasses}) identify constrained neighborhoods.
[P8867] This render gives the appendix-level discrete analogue of the higher continuous 4D projections. The law is:
[P8868] Hypercube Render Law.The seed may be rendered as a hypercube only through an explicit lawful embedding and typed edge set.
[P8869] N.12 Slice viewer
[P8870] The twelfth macro-cell is slice viewer. The branch’s 4D manifold supports exact slices[X=\text{const},\quad Y=\text{const},\quad Z=\text{const},\quad W=\text{const},]and higher-dimensional shadows such as (\pi_{XYZ}), (\pi_{XYW}), and (\pi_{ZW}). A lawful slice viewer is therefore a controlled interface into these exact restrictions.
[P8871] Define the slice viewer by

[P8873] V_{\mathrm{slice}}

[P8875] The law is:
[P8876] Slice Viewer Law.A slice viewer must expose only exact coordinate restrictions and typed overlays of the 4D crystal law.
[P8877] N.13 Dashboard layouts
[P8878] The thirteenth macro-cell is dashboard layouts. Because Appendix N is not only a chart appendix but an atlas appendix, it must also specify lawful composites of the different render families. A dashboard is lawful when its panels are synchronized views of the same underlying node set or district family.
[P8879] Define the dashboard object by
[P8880] [
[P8881] D_{\mathrm{viz}}
[P8882] (\mathrm{DashboardID},\mathrm{PanelSet},\mathrm{SharedState},\mathrm{CoordSync},\Theta_D),]where (\mathrm{PanelSet}) may include:
[P8883] 2D board panel,
[P8884] 4D slice panel,
[P8885] phase-support panel,
[P8886] nexus heatmap,
[P8887] hub persistence panel,
[P8888] replay trace panel.
[P8889] The law is:
[P8890] Dashboard Law.A lawful dashboard is a synchronized multi-panel view of one explicit crystal state, not an arbitrary collage.
[P8891] N.14 Publication figures
[P8892] The fourteenth macro-cell is publication figures. The current branch ultimately aims to publish theorem-level outputs, and Appendix O later governs public claim surfaces. Appendix N therefore prepares exact figures suitable for publication:
[P8893] root-seed figure,
[P8894] recursive district figure,
[P8895] 4D coordinate projection figure,
[P8896] phase-support / Cloud figure,
[P8897] nexus registry figure,
[P8898] hub and tunnel figure,
[P8899] Aether–Zero bundle figure.
[P8900] Define the publication-figure object by
[P8901] [
[P8902] F_{\mathrm{pub}}
[P8903] (\mathrm{FigureID},\mathrm{SourceRefs},\mathrm{CaptionContract},\mathrm{RenderSpec},\Theta_F).]
[P8904] The law is:
[P8905] Publication Figure Law.A lawful publication figure must be sourced from explicit crystal structures and carry a caption contract tying every visible element to the underlying theorem objects.
[P8906] N.15 Replay visual logs
[P8907] The fifteenth macro-cell is replay visual logs. Appendix M already fixed replay artifacts, hash receipts, and audit ledgers. Appendix N now provides the visual counterpart: replay rendered as a temporal or procedural path through coordinates, blocks, fibers, or proof bundles.
[P8908] Define the replay visual log by
[P8909] [
[P8910] L_{\mathrm{viz}}
[P8911] (\mathrm{LogID},\mathrm{ReplayRef},\mathrm{FrameSeq},\mathrm{DiffOverlay},\mathrm{AuditAnchors},\Theta_L),]where:
[P8912] (\mathrm{FrameSeq}) is the rendered replay frame sequence,
[P8913] (\mathrm{DiffOverlay}) marks what changes between steps,
[P8914] (\mathrm{AuditAnchors}) link frames to formal replay receipts and hashes.
[P8915] The law is:
[P8916] Replay Visual Log Law.A visual replay is lawful only if every frame is anchored to a replay artifact and audit receipt.
[P8917] N.16 Visual seed
[P8918] The final macro-cell is the visual seed. Appendix N must compress its whole atlas grammar into one replay-bearing visual seed:
[P8919] [
[P8920] \zeta_N
[P8921] (g_N,r_N,\eta_N,\rho_N,\Theta_N),]where:
[P8922] (g_N) is the generator core of the branch’s visualization grammar,
[P8923] (r_N) is the residual shell of bounded or alternate rendering choices,
[P8924] (\eta_N) is the visual-atlas identity digest,
[P8925] (\rho_N) is the replay/regrowth bundle.
[P8926] This visual seed can regenerate:
[P8927] 2D board render grammar,
[P8928] 4D projection grammar,
[P8929] chapter and appendix metros,
[P8930] neural-atlas overlays,
[P8931] heatmaps,
[P8932] symmetry and defect plots,
[P8933] route trees,
[P8934] torus and hypercube renders,
[P8935] slice viewers,
[P8936] dashboards,
[P8937] publication figures,
[P8938] replay visual logs.
[P8939] The final theorem of Appendix N is therefore:
[P8940] [\boxed{\text{The visualization grammar of the 256 Crystal branch is fully lawful only when 2D board renders, 4D projections, metros, neural-atlas overlays, heatmaps, symmetry and defect plots, route trees, torus and hypercube renders, slice viewers, dashboards, publication figures, replay logs, and the visual seed form one coherent replayable atlas of the crystal.}}]
[P8941] N.17 Canonical algorithmic form
[P8942] from dataclasses import dataclass
[P8943] from typing import Dict, Any, List
[P8944] @dataclass
[P8945] class MetroNode:
[P8946] theta: Dict[str, int] # X,Y,Z,W
[P8947] kappa: Dict[str, Any] # value + orbit state
[P8948] ell: List[Any] # prefix ladder
[P8949] beta: List[int] # nexus mask
[P8950] Pi: int # persistence-weighted hub score
[P8951] @dataclass
[P8952] class VisualArtifact:
[P8953] artifact_kind: str
[P8954] source_ref: Any
[P8955] render_spec: Dict[str, Any]
[P8956] replay_ref: Any
[P8957] truth_stage: str
[P8958] def build_metro_node(r: int, c: int, value: int, orbit_state: Any, prefix_ladder: List[Any], nexus_mask: List[int]) -> MetroNode:
[P8959] X = r
[P8960] Y = c
[P8961] Z = boxplus(r, c)
[P8962] W = boxminus(r, c)
[P8963] Pi = sum((4 ** q) * sum(nexus_mask) for q in range(4))
[P8964] return MetroNode(
[P8965] theta={"X": X, "Y": Y, "Z": Z, "W": W},
[P8966] kappa={"value": value, "orbit": orbit_state},
[P8967] ell=prefix_ladder,
[P8968] beta=nexus_mask,
[P8969] Pi=Pi
[P8970] )
[P8971] def build_visual_artifact(kind: str, source_ref: Any, replay_ref: Any, render_spec: Dict[str, Any]) -> VisualArtifact:
[P8972] return VisualArtifact(
[P8973] artifact_kind=kind,
[P8974] source_ref=source_ref,
[P8975] render_spec=render_spec,
[P8976] replay_ref=replay_ref,
[P8977] truth_stage="OK"
[P8978] )
[P8979] This canonical form compresses the appendix’s law: lawful visual artifacts are built from the exact metro node schema, explicit render specifications, and replay anchors.
[P8980] N.18 Appendix-level laws
[P8981] 2D Render Law — the visible board may be rendered only by explicit address/value/overlay channels.
[P8982] 4D Projection Law — every higher-dimensional render must be an explicit projection or slice of ((X,Y,Z,W)).
[P8983] Chapter Metro Law — the 9-chapter body must be rendered as a dependency metro.
[P8984] Appendix Metro Law — the 16 appendices form a lawful support crystal and must be rendered as such.
[P8985] Neural Atlas Law — visual neural nodes must instantiate the exact metro node schema.
[P8986] Block Heatmap Law — district-scale heatmaps must aggregate over exact prefix districts.
[P8987] Symmetry Plot Law — symmetry renders must be keyed to explicit orbit or automorphism classes.
[P8988] Defect Map Law — defect visuals must be tied to exact defect functionals or corridors.
[P8989] Route Tree Law — route trees must derive from explicit prefix, rail, or replay transitions.
[P8990] Cancellation Torus Render Law — the hidden torus may be rendered only through the exact phase-support lattice.
[P8991] Hypercube Render Law — hypercube visuals require explicit lawful embedding and edge sets.
[P8992] Slice Viewer Law — slice viewers must expose typed coordinate restrictions.
[P8993] Dashboard Law — multi-panel dashboards must synchronize to one crystal state.
[P8994] Publication Figure Law — published figures must be theorem-anchored.
[P8995] Visual Seed Law — the full atlas must compress into a replay-bearing visual seed.
[P8996] N.19 Closing statement
[P8997] Appendix N defines the visualization and atlas grammar of the 256 Crystal branch. It takes the exact crystal laws already established—visible-board value law, 4D coordinate law, district hierarchy, nexus registry, metro node schema, phase-support lattice, Aether–Zero bundle, replay artifacts—and turns them into lawful visual objects: board renders, projections, metros, neural overlays, heatmaps, symmetry plots, defect maps, route trees, torus and hypercube renders, slice viewers, dashboards, publication figures, replay visual logs, and a visual seed. This appendix is therefore the exact support-layer realization of Chapter 9’s metro and neural-encoding section and of the explicit 4D metro-manifold derivation. Without Appendix N, the branch would know the crystal’s structure but could not lawfully show it. With Appendix N, the crystal acquires its atlas.
[P8998] Appendix N — Visualization, Metro Maps, and Neural Atlas
[P8999] Appendix O — Applications, Translations, and Domain Projections
[P9000] O.0 Appendix Function
[P9001] In the current live branch of The 256 Crystal Extraction, Appendix O is explicitly stabilized as “Applications, Translations, and Domain Projections.” Its 16 macro-cells are fixed as:
[P9002] Error-correcting code projection
[P9003] Cryptographic projection
[P9004] Cellular automata projection
[P9005] Data-organization projection
[P9006] Discrete dynamics projection
[P9007] Resonance engine projection

[P9012] Scheduling projection
[P9013] Bridge to AQM
[P9014] Bridge to CUT
[P9015] Bridge to metro systems
[P9016] Case-study library
[P9017] Application seed.
[P9018] Appendix O is therefore the exact support-layer realization of the branch’s outward translation law. Chapters 1–9 and Appendices A–N already established the crystal internally:
[P9019] as a canonical (4\times4) seed,
[P9020] as a primitive transform algebra,
[P9021] as a Gate-4 / hidden-coordinate object,
[P9022] as a recursively lifted visible branch (4\to16\to64\to256),
[P9023] as a (256^4) hyperaddress and tensor engine,
[P9024] as a symmetry/cancellation/branch-governance system,
[P9025] as a proof-carrying runtime,
[P9026] and as a neural metro / replay-return manifold.Appendix O now answers the next lawful question: how does this internal crystal project into other domains without losing its exact structure? The support corpus already gives the architectural answer. The Unified MATH Crystal Atlas treats the whole corpus as a proof-carrying translation and compiler architecture, with Chapter 18 explicitly defining token grammar, operator IR, backend renderers, multi-renderer consistency tests, and cross-backend equivalence proofs. Appendix O specializes that general translation doctrine to the 256 Crystal branch.
[P9027] The strongest application-side support comes from two adjacent corpus lines. First, Crystal Computing Framework interprets computation itself as motion through a structured crystal lattice, with algorithms as paths through a finite semantic coordinate system whose axes encode shape, flow, level, and pole. That makes it an explicit bridge for computational projections such as tensor computing, scheduling, discrete dynamics, and data organization. Second, AQM TEXT BOOK defines AQM as the program of replacing partial mathematics with accountable mathematics via typed states, channels, certificates, ledgers, and replay. That makes it the exact semantic bridge for the crystal’s projection into typed arithmetic, boundary-aware operators, and certified approximation theory. Appendix O is where those bridges are made explicit.

[P9050] O.1 Error-correcting code projection
[P9051] The first macro-cell is error-correcting code projection. The crystal already provides the exact raw ingredients of a coding-theoretic substrate:
[P9052] a finite tetradic alphabet,
[P9053] exact base-4 addressing,
[P9054] layered prefix structure,
[P9055] local holographic redundancy,
[P9056] complement and diagonal constraints,
[P9057] replay-bearing verification.These are the same structural components one expects from a code family: symbols, blocks, parity-like constraints, local redundancy, distance structure, and decoders. The projection is therefore not speculative but structural.
[P9058] Define the code projection by
[P9059] [
[P9060] \mathcal P_{\mathrm{ecc}}
[P9061] (\Sigma_4,\mathcal C_{\mathrm{word}},\mathcal P_{\mathrm{check}},d_{\mathrm{pref}},\mathcal D_{\mathrm{dec}},\Theta_{\mathrm{ecc}}),]where:
[P9062] (\Sigma_4={0,1,2,3}) is the quaternary code alphabet,
[P9063] (\mathcal C_{\mathrm{word}}) is the codeword family derived from seed/lift addresses,
[P9064] (\mathcal P_{\mathrm{check}}) is the parity and diagonal-check family,
[P9065] (d_{\mathrm{pref}}) is the address/prefix distance,
[P9066] (\mathcal D_{\mathrm{dec}}) is the replay-stable decoder family,
[P9067] (\Theta_{\mathrm{ecc}}) is the code truth stage.
[P9068] Two canonical projection modes are lawful:
[P9069] Address code mode.Treat the full base-4 address word as the codeword and the prefix hierarchy as a multilevel syndrome structure.
[P9070] State code mode.Treat the tensor-state tuple or seed-evaluation digits as the codeword and use diagonal/complement constraints as parity checks.
[P9071] This projection is especially natural because the branch already formalizes:
[P9072] prefix retrieval,
[P9073] suffix reconstruction,
[P9074] defect metrics,
[P9075] replay pathing. These are exactly the structures needed for error localization and correction.
[P9076] The governing laws are:
[P9077] Code Projection Law.A crystal-to-code projection is lawful when codewords, checks, and decoders are inherited from explicit address and invariant structure.
[P9078] No Decorative Coding Law.A code interpretation is not lawful if it does not preserve explicit distance, syndrome, and reconstruction semantics.
[P9079] O.2 Cryptographic projection
[P9080] The second macro-cell is cryptographic projection. The branch already carries:
[P9081] canonical address hashes,
[P9082] hash receipts,
[P9083] replay artifacts,
[P9084] verifier capsules,
[P9085] proof-carrying manifests,
[P9086] and deterministic reconstruction from generators plus sparse residuals.Those objects are the natural entry point to cryptographic interpretation. Appendix O does not claim that the crystal automatically yields a production-ready cipher. It claims that it yields a lawful cryptographic projection grammar based on hashing, commitment, and Merkle-like dependency closure.
[P9087] Define the cryptographic projection by
[P9088] [
[P9089] \mathcal P_{\mathrm{crypt}}
[P9090] (\mathcal H_{\mathrm{addr}},\mathcal H_{\mathrm{trace}},\mathcal H_{\mathrm{ledger}},\mathcal C_{\mathrm{commit}},\mathcal V_{\mathrm{caps}},\Theta_{\mathrm{crypt}}),]where:
[P9091] (\mathcal H_{\mathrm{addr}}) is the address-hash family,
[P9092] (\mathcal H_{\mathrm{trace}}) is the replay-trace hash family,
[P9093] (\mathcal H_{\mathrm{ledger}}) is the audit-ledger root family,
[P9094] (\mathcal C_{\mathrm{commit}}) is the commitment object family,
[P9095] (\mathcal V_{\mathrm{caps}}) is the verifier-capsule family,
[P9096] (\Theta_{\mathrm{crypt}}) is the cryptographic truth stage.
[P9097] The canonical lawful cryptographic readings are:
[P9098] content-addressed commitment — a crystal object is bound to its canonical serialization hash,
[P9099] Merkle-like dependency closure — proof bundles and replay artifacts carry dependency roots,
[P9100] trace integrity — reruns and runtime artifacts are sealed by trace hashes.
[P9101] This is supported directly by the mechanization corpus’s artifact model and by the branch’s own hash-receipt law.
[P9102] The governing laws are:
[P9103] Cryptographic Projection Law.A crystal-to-cryptography projection is lawful only when its commitment objects are tied to canonical serialization and replay closure.
[P9104] No Encryption Inflation Law.A branch object may support hashing, commitment, or integrity proofs without thereby automatically constituting a full encryption system.
[P9105] O.3 Cellular automata projection
[P9106] The third macro-cell is cellular automata projection. The 256 Crystal branch already describes the visible board as a finite addressable lattice, the recursive lift as a local substitution rule, and the hypercrystal as a tensorized state engine. These are exactly the ingredients of a cellular automaton interpretation: a lattice, local update rules, neighborhood structure, and state carriers.
[P9107] Define the CA projection by
[P9108] [
[P9109] \mathcal P_{\mathrm{ca}}
[P9110] (\mathcal L_{\mathrm{cell}},\mathcal N_{\mathrm{hood}},\mathcal U_{\mathrm{local}},\mathcal S_{\mathrm{state}},\mathcal R_{\mathrm{iter}},\Theta_{\mathrm{ca}}),]where:
[P9111] (\mathcal L_{\mathrm{cell}}) is the visible or hidden crystal lattice,
[P9112] (\mathcal N_{\mathrm{hood}}) is the neighborhood family,
[P9113] (\mathcal U_{\mathrm{local}}) is the local update family,
[P9114] (\mathcal S_{\mathrm{state}}) is the cell or hypercell state family,
[P9115] (\mathcal R_{\mathrm{iter}}) is the time-evolution rule,
[P9116] (\Theta_{\mathrm{ca}}) is the cellular-automaton truth stage.
[P9117] Two lawful CA modes exist:
[P9118] Visible-board CA.Cells are visible board sites ((r,c)), neighborhoods come from prefix or coordinate adjacency, and updates act on visible value/state.
[P9119] Hypercell CA.Cells are 4D hypercells, neighborhoods include tensor channels or hidden-axis fibers, and updates act on the eight-factor tensor state.
[P9120] This is one of the branch’s cleanest domain projections because the crystal already functions as a finite local update medium.
[P9121] The governing laws are:
[P9122] CA Projection Law.A lawful crystal-to-CA projection must specify lattice, neighborhood, local update, and replay regime.
[P9123] No Metaphorical Automaton Law.It is not enough that the crystal “looks iterative”; the update rule must be explicit.

[P9253] Define the tensor-computing projection by

[P9403] O.17 Canonical algorithmic form
[P9404] from dataclasses import dataclass
[P9405] from typing import Dict, Any, List
[P9406] @dataclass
[P9407] class ProjectionArtifact:
[P9408] domain_class: str
[P9409] source_ref: Any
[P9410] carrier_map: Dict[str, Any]
[P9411] invariant_map: Dict[str, Any]
[P9412] replay_ref: Any
[P9413] truth_stage: str
[P9414] def project_to_code(source_ref, address_word, parity_checks, replay_ref):
[P9415] return ProjectionArtifact(
[P9416] domain_class="error_correcting_code",
[P9417] source_ref=source_ref,
[P9418] carrier_map={"codeword": address_word, "checks": parity_checks},
[P9419] invariant_map={"distance_law": "prefix_distance", "reconstruction": "generator_plus_residual"},
[P9420] replay_ref=replay_ref,
[P9421] truth_stage="OK"
[P9422] )
[P9423] def project_to_tensor(source_ref, hyperstate, replay_ref):
[P9424] return ProjectionArtifact(
[P9425] domain_class="tensor_computing",
[P9426] source_ref=source_ref,
[P9427] carrier_map={"tensor_state": hyperstate, "factorization": "L4^⊗8"},
[P9428] invariant_map={"pairing_scheme": "canonical_visible_hidden", "exact_eval": True},
[P9429] replay_ref=replay_ref,
[P9430] truth_stage="OK"
[P9431] )
[P9432] def bridge_to_aqm(source_ref, replay_ref):
[P9433] return ProjectionArtifact(
[P9434] domain_class="AQM_bridge",
[P9435] source_ref=source_ref,
[P9436] carrier_map={"state_model": "typed_state", "operator_model": "channel_or_instrument"},
[P9437] invariant_map={"certificate_required": True, "replay_required": True},
[P9438] replay_ref=replay_ref,
[P9439] truth_stage="OK"
[P9440] )
[P9441] This canonical form compresses the appendix’s law: a lawful domain projection packages a crystal source, an explicit carrier map, an invariant map, and a replay anchor into one typed application artifact.
[P9442] O.18 Appendix-level laws
[P9443] Code Projection Law — code interpretations require explicit codewords, checks, and decoders.
[P9444] Cryptographic Projection Law — cryptographic readings require canonical hashes, commitments, and replay integrity.
[P9445] Cellular Automata Projection Law — automaton readings require explicit lattice, neighborhood, and update rules.
[P9446] Data-Organization Law — storage projections require address, prefix, residual, and reconstruction law.
[P9447] Discrete Dynamics Law — dynamical readings require explicit state, step, invariant, and iteration objects.
[P9448] Resonance Engine Law — resonance projections require exact phase and coherence structure.
[P9449] Memory Architecture Law — memory projections require seed, residual, version, and replay layers.
[P9450] AI Latent-Space Law — latent-space projections require exact manifold, route, and compression structure.
[P9451] Tesseract Logic Law — higher-dimensional logic projections require exact Gate-4 embeddings.
[P9452] Tensor Computing Law — tensor projections require explicit factorization and evaluator law.
[P9453] Scheduling Projection Law — scheduling projections require task order, budgets, and verifier gates.
[P9454] AQM Bridge Law — the crystal may bridge to AQM only by explicit state/operator/certificate/replay correspondence.
[P9455] CUT Bridge Law — the crystal may bridge to CUT only by explicit path/coherence/anti-region correspondence.
[P9456] Metro Bridge Law — the crystal may bridge to metro systems only through the exact node/rail/fiber schema.
[P9457] Application Seed Law — the whole application layer must compress into a replay-bearing seed.
[P9458] O.19 Closing statement
[P9459] Appendix O defines the application, translation, and domain-projection layer of the 256 Crystal branch. It takes the exact internal structures already proven elsewhere in the manuscript—base-4 addresses, recursive blocks, hidden coordinates, tensor states, branch corridors, replay artifacts, metro nodes, toroidal phase support—and shows how they project lawfully into other domains: error-correcting codes, cryptographic integrity structures, cellular automata, data organization, discrete dynamics, resonance engines, memory architectures, AI latent spaces, tesseract logic, tensor computing, scheduling systems, and the larger frameworks of AQM, CUT, and metro design. This appendix is therefore the exact support-layer realization of the branch’s “outward” law. Without Appendix O, the crystal would know itself but not how to translate itself. With Appendix O, the crystal acquires its domain grammar.

[P9461] Appendix P — Compression, Return Seeds, and Orbit Closure
[P9462] P.0 Appendix Function
[P9463] In the current live branch of The 256 Crystal Extraction, Appendix P is explicitly stabilized as “Compression, Return Seeds, and Orbit Closure.” Its 16 macro-cells are fixed as:
[P9464] Compression laws
[P9465] Seed emission laws
[P9466] Orbit return laws
[P9467] Endcapsule grammar
[P9468] Chapter return map
[P9469] Appendix return map
[P9470] Replay closure

[P9472] Migration hooks
[P9473] Future-question hooks
[P9474] Return proofs
[P9475] Regenerative closure
[P9476] Meta-seed structure
[P9477] Next-cycle compiler
[P9478] Final closure certificates
[P9479] Absolute return seed.
[P9480] A wider live corpus role-map gives the same appendix a second but fully compatible name: EndCapsules / Orbit Return / continuation queues / regenerative closure. The metro-wide documents also state the recursive end condition explicitly:[AppP \to \mathrm{SeedSummary} \to AppA,\qquad\mathrm{EndCapsule}\to \mathrm{OrbitReturn}\to \text{lawful re-entry gate}.]Thus Appendix P is not simply “the last appendix.” It is the lawful closure surface at which the branch compresses itself, seals itself, and emits the next admissible beginning.
[P9481] The strongest compression-side support comes from the recursive-manuscript seed corpus, which explicitly distinguishes four holographic forms:[\Omega \subset \Alpha^+ \subset \Delta^+ \subset \Omega^+,]where (\Omega) is the irreducible invariant, (\Alpha^+) the minimum reconstructive seed, (\Delta^+) the compressed source crystal preserving body, appendix, routing, and self-reproduction law, and (\Omega^+) the fully expanded manuscript civilization. The same support defines the cycle[\text{question}\to\text{seed}\to\text{body}\to\text{appendices}\to\text{metro}\to\text{living update}\to\text{next question},]which is the exact larger-family ancestor of Appendix P’s return law.
[P9482] A second support line specializes this to the 4⁴ crystal engine. Stories from the Void states explicitly:
[P9483] OMEGA+ = the complete crystal with all 256 gates populated,
[P9484] DELTA+ = the structural outline with gate addresses and type signatures,
[P9485] ALPHA+ = the seed plus zero point as minimal regenerative kernel,
[P9486] Omega = the irreducible one-line compression,and it closes the 4⁴ engine by the theorem that every completed crystal emits a return seed that re-enters through AppA. Appendix P is the 256 Crystal branch’s exact support-layer realization of that compression stack.
[P9487] Formally, define the Appendix P substrate by
[P9488] [
[P9489] \mathbb P_{\mathrm{return}}
[P9490] (\mathcal C_{\mathrm{comp}},\mathcal S_{\mathrm{emit}},\mathcal O_{\mathrm{return}},\mathcal E_{\mathrm{cap}},\mathcal M_{\mathrm{chap}},\mathcal M_{\mathrm{app}},\mathcal R_{\mathrm{replay}},\mathcal G_{\mathrm{gov}},\mathcal H_{\mathrm{mig}},\mathcal Q_{\mathrm{future}},\mathcal P_{\mathrm{proof}},\mathcal R_{\mathrm{regen}},\mathcal S_{\mathrm{meta}},\mathcal N_{\mathrm{next}},\mathcal C_{\mathrm{final}},\mathcal A_{\mathrm{seed}}),]where:
[P9491] (\mathcal C_{\mathrm{comp}}) is the compression-law family,
[P9492] (\mathcal S_{\mathrm{emit}}) is the seed-emission family,
[P9493] (\mathcal O_{\mathrm{return}}) is the orbit-return family,
[P9494] (\mathcal E_{\mathrm{cap}}) is the endcapsule family,
[P9495] (\mathcal M_{\mathrm{chap}}) is the chapter-return-map family,
[P9496] (\mathcal M_{\mathrm{app}}) is the appendix-return-map family,
[P9497] (\mathcal R_{\mathrm{replay}}) is the replay-closure family,
