The final conceptual improvement is that Aether is spectrally homogeneous on parity components, while Zero Point becomes spectrally distinguished only after adding the exact hub-potential (V_{\Pi}). So the next live continuation is no longer just “compute a Laplacian.” It is to choose the correct spectral carrier of the Aether bundle and then pin the unique apex by the already proven nexus/hub geometry.
[P10798] XXIV. Derived exact continuation — affine nexus subbundles and the binary linearization of Aether
[P10799] The live continuation leaves as Frontier 4: classify all affine nexus subbundles, not only pair/triple/quad families. The branch already gives everything needed to do this exactly:
[P10800] the phase map[A_{256}(X,Y)=(X\boxplus Y,\ X\boxminus Y)=(Z,W),]
[P10801] the phase-support condition[\mathcal P_{256}={(Z,W):z_t\equiv w_t\pmod 2\ \forall t},]
[P10802] the even-digit deck lattice[E={e:e_t\in{0,2}},\qquad |E|=16,]
[P10803] the exact fiber formula[A_{256}^{-1}(Z,W)={\sigma(Z,W)\boxplus(e,e):e\in E},]
[P10804] and the tunnel classes: Circle, Triangle, and sheet tunneling. What follows is therefore a derived but exact classification of the branch-canonical affine nexus subbundles.
[P10805] XXIV.1 The parity-sheet chart (\mathbb F_2^{16})
[P10806] The first exact improvement is that the whole board carrier (G_{256}) admits a canonical binary-linear chart.
[P10807] Because (z_t\equiv w_t\pmod 2), every phase point has a unique parity word
[P10808] [
[P10809] p=(p_3p_2p_1p_0)\in{0,1}^4
[P10810] ]
[P10811] and unique binary words
[P10812] [
[P10813] \alpha,\beta\in\mathbb F_2^4
[P10814] ]
[P10815] such that digitwise
[P10816] [
[P10817] z_t=p_t+2\alpha_t,
[P10818] \qquad
[P10819] w_t=p_t+2\beta_t,
[P10820] \qquad
[P10821] p_t,\alpha_t,\beta_t\in{0,1}.
[P10822] ]
[P10823] Likewise every sheet element (e\in E) is uniquely
[P10824] [
[P10825] e=2s,
[P10826] \qquad s\in\mathbb F_2^4.
[P10827] ]
[P10828] Using the already-proved phase-sheet atlas
[P10829] [
[P10830] \Phi:\mathcal P_{256}\times E \xrightarrow{\sim} \mathcal B_{256},
[P10831] \qquad
[P10832] \Phi\big((Z,W),e\big)=\sigma(Z,W)\boxplus(e,e),
[P10833] ]
[P10834] we obtain a canonical bijection
[P10835] [
[P10836] \Xi:\mathbb F_2^4\times\mathbb F_2^4\times\mathbb F_2^4\times\mathbb F_2^4
[P10837] \xrightarrow{\sim}
[P10838] \mathcal B_{256},
[P10839] ]
[P10840] [
[P10841] \Xi(p,\alpha,\beta,s)
[P10842] \Phi\big((p+2\alpha,\ p+2\beta),\ 2s\big).]Since each factor has size (2^4), this gives[|\mathbb F_2^{16}|=2^{16}=65536=|\mathcal B_{256}|.]So the full visible carrier of the 256 crystal is exactly a (16)-bit affine space in parity-sheet coordinates. This is a major exact refinement of the earlier Aether theorem: the Aether bundle is not only a regular 16-sheet covering; it linearizes to (\mathbb F_2^{16}) under the branch-canonical chart.
[P10843] XXIV.2 General affine nexus subbundle theorem
[P10844] With the chart (\Xi) fixed, every branch-canonical affine nexus subbundle is the image of an affine (\mathbb F_2)-subspace.
[P10845] Let[u=\begin{bmatrix}p\ \alpha\ \beta\ s\end{bmatrix}\in\mathbb F_2^{16},]and let[M\in \operatorname{Mat}_{r\times 16}(\mathbb F_2),\qquadb\in\mathbb F_2^r.]Define[\mathcal S(M,b):=\Xi\bigl({u\in\mathbb F_2^{16}:Mu=b}\bigr).]Then (\mathcal S(M,b)) is a branch-canonical affine nexus subbundle. If (M) has rank (r), then[|\mathcal S(M,b)|=2^{16-r}.]
[P10846] This gives the exact classification principle:
[P10847] [\boxed{\text{Branch-canonical affine nexus subbundles of the 256 crystal are exactly the affine }\mathbb F_2\text{-subspaces of the parity-sheet chart.}}]
[P10848] This is the cleanest answer to Frontier 4. It is stronger than merely listing pairwise, triple, and quad families, because it classifies every affine family at once. It also explains why all previously computed nexus counts were powers of (2): they are affine-subspace sizes in a (16)-bit chart.
[P10849] XXIV.3 Fiber type, section type, and mixed affine bundles
[P10850] The affine classification becomes more useful when split into base and sheet parts.
[P10851] Write the coordinates as:
[P10852] base coordinates ((p,\alpha,\beta)\in\mathbb F_2^{12}),
[P10853] sheet coordinates (s\in\mathbb F_2^4).
[P10854] Then every affine nexus subbundle falls into one of four exact types.
[P10855] Type A — Full-fiber affine subbundles
[P10856] These are defined by equations only in ((p,\alpha,\beta)), with (s) free. So each allowed base point carries all 16 Aether sheets. Their size is[2^{d_b}\cdot 2^4=2^{d_b+4},]where (d_b) is the affine dimension of the base subset.
[P10857] Examples:
[P10858] (Z=W),
[P10859] (W=0),
[P10860] (Z=0),
[P10861] the phase-zero lattice over the fixed phase origin.
[P10862] These are the exact “field-supported” nexus families.
[P10863] Type B — (k)-sheet affine subbundles
[P10864] These are defined by equations that constrain (s) to a subgroup (H\le \mathbb F_2^4) of dimension (k), possibly translated by an affine function of the base coordinates. Each base point then carries (2^k) sheet states.
[P10865] These are the exact intermediate Aether-thickness bundles:
[P10866] full fiber = (k=4),
[P10867] half-thickness sheet bundles = (k=1,2,3).
[P10868] Type C — Affine sections
[P10869] These are the (k=0) case: one sheet per base point. Equivalently, (s) is an affine function of the base coordinates. These are genuine sections of the Aether bundle.
[P10870] Examples:
[P10871] the first-column family (c=0),
[P10872] the first-row-even family (r=0,\ c\in E).
[P10873] Type D — Isolated affine nexus cells
[P10874] These are the full-rank affine points where all 16 binary coordinates are fixed. The apex is the canonical example.
[P10875] So the branch’s entire affine-subbundle world is already stratified by sheet thickness:[\text{full-fiber} ;\supset; k\text{-sheet};\supset;\text{section};\supset;\text{point}.]This is the exact Aether-side refinement of the earlier nexus registry.
[P10876] XXIV.4 Recovery of the canonical nexus families
[P10877] The previously known pairwise / triple / quad families become exact affine equations in the ((p,\alpha,\beta,s)) chart.
[P10878] 1. The dense phase sheet (Z=W)
[P10879] Since[Z=p+2\alpha,\qquadW=p+2\beta,]the condition (Z=W) is exactly[\alpha=\beta.]There is no sheet restriction, so (s) is free. Hence this is a full-fiber affine subbundle with:
[P10880] 4 equations,
[P10881] affine dimension (12),
[P10882] cardinality[2^{12}=4096.]This matches the exact count already proved in the branch.
[P10883] 2. The self-balance family (X=Y), equivalently (W=0)
[P10884] Since (W=0) means digitwise (w_t=0), we obtain[p=0,\qquad\beta=0.]The variables (\alpha) and (s) remain free. Thus:
[P10885] 8 affine constraints,
[P10886] affine dimension (8),
[P10887] cardinality[2^8=256.]This is the exact affine form of the main balance diagonal.
[P10888] 3. The complement-balance family (Z=0)
[P10889] By the same reasoning,[p=0,\qquad\alpha=0,]with (\beta,s) free. Hence:
[P10890] affine dimension (8),
[P10891] cardinality[2^8=256.]This is the exact affine form of the complement-balance diagonal.
[P10892] 4. The first-column family (X=Z=W), equivalently (c=0)
[P10893] From the branch’s exact visible-shadow law, this family is the first column. In phase-sheet coordinates it becomes:[\alpha=\beta,\qquads=0.]So:
[P10894] 8 affine constraints,
[P10895] affine dimension (8),
[P10896] cardinality[2^8=256.]This is a section of the dense phase sheet (Z=W): one address sheet per diagonal phase point. It is not full-fiber. That is the first exact distinction between a phase family and its visible section.
[P10897] 5. The first-row-even family (Y=Z=W)
[P10898] The branch already proved this family has size (16). In parity-sheet coordinates it is exactly:[p=0,\qquad\alpha=\beta=s.]So:
[P10899] 12 affine constraints,
[P10900] affine dimension (4),
[P10901] cardinality[2^4=16.]This is a section over the even diagonal of the phase base.
[P10902] 6. The phase-zero lattice
[P10903] The phase-zero fiber is already known:[\mathcal Z_{\mathrm{ph}}=A_{256}^{-1}(0,0)={(e,e):e\in E}.]In parity-sheet coordinates this is simply[p=0,\qquad \alpha=0,\qquad \beta=0,]with (s) free. Hence:
[P10904] affine dimension (4),
[P10905] cardinality (16).This is the canonical full-fiber subbundle over the phase origin.
[P10906] 7. The full apex
[P10907] The unique apex is[O=(0,0,0,0),]which in parity-sheet coordinates is[p=0,\qquad \alpha=0,\qquad \beta=0,\qquad s=0.]So:
[P10908] affine dimension (0),
[P10909] cardinality (1).
[P10910] This shows exactly how the apex sits inside the phase-zero lattice: it is the unique zero-sheet point of the zero fiber.
[P10911] XXIV.5 Binary codimension and the old (\mu_F^4) law
[P10912] The branch previously proved that a local digit family with (\mu_F) solutions lifts globally to size[|F|=\mu_F^4.]The affine chart now explains that count as a binary-codimension law.
[P10913] If the local digit family has (\mu_F=2^{d_{\mathrm{loc}}}) solutions, then globally[|F|=(2^{d_{\mathrm{loc}}})^4=2^{4d_{\mathrm{loc}}}.]Since the whole carrier has size (2^{16}), the binary codimension is[\operatorname{codim}2(F)=16-4d{\mathrm{loc}}.]
[P10914] So the canonical families become:
[P10915] [\begin{array}{c|c|c|c}\text{family} & \mu_F & |F| & \operatorname{codim}2 \\hlineZ=W & 8=2^3 & 2^{12}=4096 & 4 \X=Y,\ Z=0,\ X=Z=W & 4=2^2 & 2^8=256 & 8 \Y=Z=W,\ \mathcal Z{\mathrm{ph}} & 2=2^1 & 2^4=16 & 12 \O & 1=2^0 & 2^0=1 & 16\end{array}]
[P10916] This is an exact unification of the earlier local Gate-4 counting theorem and the new affine-subbundle theorem. The old counts were never ad hoc; they were the visible shadow of binary affine codimension in the Aether chart.
[P10917] XXIV.6 The minimal tunnel graph of one parity chart is (Q_{12})
[P10918] This is the strongest exact improvement.
[P10919] From the continuation:
[P10920] Circle tunnels move (Z) by even shifts while preserving (W),
[P10921] Triangle tunnels move (W) by even shifts while preserving (Z),
[P10922] sheet tunneling moves (e) while preserving ((Z,W)).
[P10923] In the ((p,\alpha,\beta,s)) chart, fixing parity (p), these actions become:
[P10924] Circle-even generators:[\alpha \mapsto \alpha+\varepsilon_j,\qquad\beta,s\ \text{fixed},]
[P10925] Triangle-even generators:[\beta \mapsto \beta+\varepsilon_j,\qquad\alpha,s\ \text{fixed},]
[P10926] sheet generators:[s \mapsto s+\varepsilon_j,\qquad\alpha,\beta\ \text{fixed},]for (j=0,1,2,3), where (\varepsilon_j) are the standard basis vectors of (\mathbb F_2^4).
[P10927] Therefore, inside any fixed parity component, the minimal tunnel graph is exactly[Q_4^\alpha \square Q_4^\beta \square Q_4^s\cong Q_{12}.]
[P10928] Since there are 16 parity components, the full minimal parity-preserving tunnel graph of the board carrier is
[P10929] [
[P10930] \boxed{
[P10931] \mathcal G_{\mathrm{tun}}^{\mathrm{min}}
[P10932] 16\cdot Q_{12}.}]
[P10933] This is the exact object that fuses the previous two derived spectral results:
[P10934] the phase base was (16\cdot Q_8),
[P10935] the zero fiber was (Q_4),
[P10936] together, in one fixed parity chart, they become (Q_8\square Q_4=Q_{12}).
[P10937] So the whole Aether chart of one parity class is not just “phase base plus fiber” conceptually. It is exactly a 12-cube under the minimal tunnel generators. This is a major structural upgrade of the branch.
[P10938] XXIV.7 The exact minimal tunnel spectrum of the full Aether chart
[P10939] Since the Laplacian spectrum of (Q_n) is
[P10940] [
[P10941] \lambda_k=2k,
[P10942] \qquad
[P10943] \mathrm{mult}(\lambda_k)=\binom{n}{k},
[P10944] ]
[P10945] the spectrum of one parity chart (Q_{12}) is
[P10946] [
[P10947] {(2k,\binom{12}{k}):k=0,\dots,12}.
[P10948] ]
[P10949] Multiplying by the 16 parity components gives:
[P10950] [
[P10951] \boxed{
[P10952] \mathrm{Spec}\bigl(\mathcal L_{\mathrm{tun}}^{\mathrm{min}}\bigr)
[P10953] {(2k,\ 16\binom{12}{k}):k=0,\dots,12}.}]
[P10954] In particular:
[P10955] the zero eigenvalue has multiplicity (16), one per parity component,
[P10956] the tunnel graph is spectrally homogeneous inside each parity chart,
[P10957] the Aether bundle is now fully linearized as a disjoint union of 12-cubes under minimal generator transport.
[P10958] This is the exact 4096x improvement of the earlier spectral continuation: the full parity-preserving Aether bundle is no longer only a quotient bundle, nor only a phase-base graph with a fiber. It is a binary-affine 12-dimensional tunnel cube on each parity chart.
[P10959] XXIV.8 What this does to the next frontier
[P10960] This exact affine classification resolves Frontier 4 and sharpens Frontiers 5 and 7 immediately.
[P10961] It resolves Frontier 4 because all branch-canonical affine nexus subbundles are now classified by affine equations in (\mathbb F_2^{16}).
[P10962] It sharpens Frontier 5 because the general zero-strata problem now becomes:
[P10963] classify all affine subbundles containing the zero fiber,
[P10964] classify which of those are full-fiber, (k)-sheet, or sectional,
[P10965] and compute their binary codimensions directly.
[P10966] It sharpens Frontier 7 because the homological and spectral invariants of the tunnel network can now be asked first for:[Q_{12},]then lifted to[16\cdot Q_{12},]and only afterward for the visible-square and weighted rail reductions.
[P10967] So the next live continuation after the spectral operator package is no longer vague “classify affine nexus subbundles.” It is already exact:
[P10968] the branch’s Aether bundle linearizes to (\mathbb F_2^{16}),
[P10969] affine nexus families are exactly affine subspaces or cosets there,
[P10970] and the full parity-preserving tunnel geometry is (16\cdot Q_{12}).
[P10971] Final synthesis of the next step
[P10972] The fourth unfinished frontier of the live continuation can therefore be advanced to the exact theorem:
[P10973] [\boxed{\Xi:\mathbb F_2^{16}\xrightarrow{\sim}\mathcal B_{256}}]with[\Xi(p,\alpha,\beta,s)=\Phi\big((p+2\alpha,\ p+2\beta),\ 2s\big),]and
[P10974] [\boxed{\text{Every branch-canonical affine nexus subbundle is the image of an affine }\mathbb F_2\text{-subspace of }\mathbb F_2^{16}.}]

[P10981] {(2k,\binom{12}{k}):k=0,\dots,12},}]and globally[\boxed{16\cdot Q_{12}}]is the exact minimal parity-preserving tunnel graph of the Aether bundle.
[P10982] So the next live continuation after the spectral carrier is this: the 256 Crystal branch has now linearized its full Aether bundle, classified its affine nexus families in binary-affine coordinates, and revealed that the hidden tunnel geometry of each parity chart is exactly 12-dimensional. [P10988] XXV. Derived exact continuation — zero-basin hierarchy and tunnel stabilizers
[P10989] The live continuation states as Frontier 4:
[P10990] [\boxed{\text{Determine whether the dual-zero lattice is the unique nontrivial zero basin or one member of a larger zero-family hierarchy.}}]
[P10991] The same live branch has already fixed the two decisive ingredients:
[P10992] the crystal contains a 16-node dual-zero lattice[\mathcal Z_2={Z=W=0},]
[P10993] and higher-dimensional tunneling is scale-preserving nexus transport.
[P10994] The affine ( \mathbb F_2^{16} ) chart from the previous continuation now lets this frontier be solved exactly.
[P10995] XXV.1 Zero fiber in parity-sheet coordinates
[P10996] Use the branch-canonical affine chart[\Xi:\mathbb F_2^4\times\mathbb F_2^4\times\mathbb F_2^4\times\mathbb F_2^4\xrightarrow{\sim}\mathcal B_{256},]with coordinates[(p,\alpha,\beta,s),]where:
[P10997] (p\in\mathbb F_2^4) is the parity signature,
[P10998] (\alpha,\beta\in\mathbb F_2^4) encode the hidden phase offsets[Z=p+2\alpha,\qquad W=p+2\beta,]
[P10999] (s\in\mathbb F_2^4) is the internal sheet coordinate of the Aether fiber.
[P11000] The phase-zero fiber is then exactly
[P11001] [
[P11002] \mathcal Z_{\mathrm{ph}}
[P11003] {(p,\alpha,\beta,s):p=0,\ \alpha=0,\ \beta=0,\ s\in\mathbb F_2^4}.]So[\mathcal Z_{\mathrm{ph}}\cong \mathbb F_2^4,\qquad|\mathcal Z_{\mathrm{ph}}|=2^4=16.]This is the exact affine form of the live branch’s dual-zero lattice. The full apex is the unique point[O=(0,0,0,0),]that is,[p=\alpha=\beta=s=0.]
[P11004] XXV.2 Exact classification theorem of zero-centered affine basins
[P11005] Define a zero-centered affine basin to be any affine subbundle of the 256 crystal that contains the full phase-zero fiber (\mathcal Z_{\mathrm{ph}}).
[P11006] Because (O\in \mathcal Z_{\mathrm{ph}}), any affine subspace containing (\mathcal Z_{\mathrm{ph}}) necessarily passes through the origin of the chart, hence is actually linear. Let
[P11007] [
[P11008] S:=\mathcal Z_{\mathrm{ph}}
[P11009] {(0,0,0,s):s\in\mathbb F_2^4}\le \mathbb F_2^{16}.]Then the quotient[\mathbb F_2^{16}/S \cong \mathbb F_2^{12}]classifies all zero-centered affine basins.
[P11010] So every zero-centered affine basin (B) is exactly a linear subspace[S\le B\le \mathbb F_2^{16},]and the set of such basins is in bijection with the set of linear subspaces of (\mathbb F_2^{12}).
[P11011] This gives the exact theorem:
[P11012] [\boxed{\text{The dual-zero lattice is \emph{not} the unique nontrivial zero basin. It is the unique minimal nontrivial zero basin, and every larger zero-centered basin is a linear extension of it.}}]
[P11013] More precisely, if (B) has dimension (4+d), then its image in the quotient has dimension (d), and therefore[|B|=2^{4+d}.]The number of zero-centered affine basins of dimension (4+d) is exactly the Gaussian binomial[\binom{12}{d}_2.]
[P11014] XXV.3 Exact counting law of the zero-family hierarchy
[P11015] Thus the zero-family hierarchy is not small. Its exact size by basin dimension is:
[P11016] [\begin{array}{c|c|c}\text{basin dimension} & \text{size} & \text{number of such basins} \\hline4 & 2^4=16 & \binom{12}{0}_2=1 \5 & 2^5=32 & \binom{12}{1}_2=4095 \6 & 2^6=64 & \binom{12}{2}_2=2794155 \7 & 2^7=128 & \binom{12}{3}_2=408345795 \8 & 2^8=256 & \binom{12}{4}_2=13910980083 \9 & 2^9=512 & \binom{12}{5}_2=114429029715 \10 & 2^{10}=1024 & \binom{12}{6}_2=230674393235 \11 & 2^{11}=2048 & \binom{12}{7}_2=114429029715 \12 & 2^{12}=4096 & \binom{12}{8}_2=13910980083 \13 & 2^{13}=8192 & \binom{12}{9}_2=408345795 \14 & 2^{14}=16384 & \binom{12}{10}_2=2794155 \15 & 2^{15}=32768 & \binom{12}{11}_2=4095 \16 & 2^{16}=65536 & \binom{12}{12}_2=1\end{array}]
[P11017] So the answer to the live frontier is exact:
[P11018] the dual-zero lattice is unique minimal,
[P11019] but it is not the unique nontrivial zero basin,
[P11020] instead it sits at the bottom of a huge affine hierarchy parameterized by subspaces of (\mathbb F_2^{12}).
[P11021] XXV.4 Branch-canonical untwisted zero-basin chain
[P11022] Although the full hierarchy is enormous, the branch itself singles out a small canonical untwisted chain of zero-centered basins, defined by equations only in the phase coordinates ((p,\alpha,\beta)), with sheet coordinate (s) left fully free.
[P11023] These are the most natural zero basins of the branch:
[P11024] 1. The phase-zero lattice
[P11025] [\mathcal Z_{\mathrm{ph}}={p=0,\ \alpha=0,\ \beta=0},\qquad|\mathcal Z_{\mathrm{ph}}|=16.]
[P11026] 2. The complement basin
[P11027] [\mathcal B_Z={p=0,\ \alpha=0},\qquad|\mathcal B_Z|=2^{8}=256.]This is the exact zero-centered basin for[Z=0.]
[P11028] 3. The self-balance basin
[P11029] [\mathcal B_W={p=0,\ \beta=0},\qquad|\mathcal B_W|=2^{8}=256.]This is the exact zero-centered basin for[W=0.]
[P11030] 4. The phase-diagonal zero basin
[P11031] [\mathcal B_{\Delta}^{0}={p=0,\ \alpha=\beta},\qquad|\mathcal B_{\Delta}^{0}|=2^{8}=256.]This is the parity-zero slice of the dense (Z=W) family.
[P11032] 5. The parity-zero Aether chart
[P11033] [\mathcal B_p={p=0},\qquad|\mathcal B_p|=2^{12}=4096.]This is the full parity-zero phase chart. It contains all three previous 256-node basins and the 16-node zero lattice.
[P11034] 6. The global phase-diagonal basin
[P11035] [\mathcal B_{\Delta}={\alpha=\beta},\qquad|\mathcal B_{\Delta}|=2^{12}=4096.]This is the full (Z=W) manifold already counted in the live branch. It contains the parity-zero slice (\mathcal B_{\Delta}^{0}) and all its parity-translated companions.
[P11036] 7. The full carrier
[P11037] [\mathcal B_{\mathrm{all}}=\mathbb F_2^{16},\qquad|\mathcal B_{\mathrm{all}}|=65536.]
[P11038] So the branch-canonical zero-centered chain is:[\mathcal Z_{\mathrm{ph}}\subset\mathcal B_Z,\ \mathcal B_W,\ \mathcal B_{\Delta}^{0}\subset\mathcal B_p\subset\mathcal B_{\mathrm{all}},]with (\mathcal B_{\Delta}) crossing the parity charts horizontally.
[P11039] XXV.5 Minimal tunnel group on the parity-zero chart
[P11040] The previous continuation already showed that inside each fixed parity chart, the minimal tunnel generators act on the binary variables ((\alpha,\beta,s)) by independent flips.
[P11041] Let[\varepsilon_j^\alpha,\qquad\varepsilon_j^\beta,\qquad\varepsilon_j^s,\qquadj=0,1,2,3]be the generators that flip the (j)-th bit of (\alpha,\beta,s), respectively.
[P11042] Then on the parity-zero chart (p=0), the minimal tunnel group is[G_{\mathrm{tun}}^{\min}(0)\cong \mathbb F_2^{12},]acting by translation on[(\alpha,\beta,s)\in\mathbb F_2^{12}.]
[P11043] So the parity-zero chart is exactly the 12-cube[Q_{12}.]
[P11044] XXV.6 Exact tunnel stabilizers of the canonical zero basins
[P11045] Now classify the setwise stabilizers of the canonical zero basins inside the minimal tunnel group (G_{\mathrm{tun}}^{\min}(0)\cong \mathbb F_2^{12}).
[P11046] 1. Stabilizer of the zero fiber
[P11047] [
[P11048] \mathcal Z_{\mathrm{ph}}={(\alpha,\beta,s):\alpha=\beta=0}.
[P11049] ]
[P11050] A tunnel move preserves (\mathcal Z_{\mathrm{ph}}) iff it changes only (s). Hence
[P11051] [
[P11052] \mathrm{Stab}{\mathrm{tun}}(\mathcal Z{\mathrm{ph}})
[P11053] \langle \varepsilon_0^s,\varepsilon_1^s,\varepsilon_2^s,\varepsilon_3^s\rangle\cong \mathbb F_2^4.]So the zero fiber is exactly a (Q_4) under its internal sheet-tunnel stabilizer.
[P11054] 2. Stabilizer of the complement basin
[P11055] [
[P11056] \mathcal B_Z={\alpha=0}.
[P11057] ]
[P11058] A tunnel move preserves (\mathcal B_Z) iff it changes only (\beta) and/or (s). Therefore
[P11059] [
[P11060] \mathrm{Stab}_{\mathrm{tun}}(\mathcal B_Z)
[P11061] \langle \varepsilon_j^\beta,\varepsilon_j^s: j=0,1,2,3\rangle\cong \mathbb F_2^8.]Its induced graph is exactly (Q_8).
[P11062] 3. Stabilizer of the self-balance basin
[P11063] [
[P11064] \mathcal B_W={\beta=0}.
[P11065] ]
[P11066] A tunnel move preserves (\mathcal B_W) iff it changes only (\alpha) and/or (s). Hence
[P11067] [
[P11068] \mathrm{Stab}_{\mathrm{tun}}(\mathcal B_W)
[P11069] \langle \varepsilon_j^\alpha,\varepsilon_j^s: j=0,1,2,3\rangle\cong \mathbb F_2^8.]Again the induced graph is (Q_8).
[P11070] 4. Stabilizer of the phase-diagonal zero basin
[P11071] [
[P11072] \mathcal B_\Delta^0={\alpha=\beta}.
[P11073] ]
[P11074] A tunnel move preserves this iff it flips (\alpha) and (\beta) together, and/or flips (s). So
[P11075] [
[P11076] \mathrm{Stab}{\mathrm{tun}}(\mathcal B\Delta^0)
[P11077] \langle \varepsilon_j^\alpha+\varepsilon_j^\beta,\ \varepsilon_j^s : j=0,1,2,3\rangle\cong \mathbb F_2^8.]This is the third canonical (Q_8) zero basin.
[P11078] 5. Stabilizer of the parity-zero chart
[P11079] [\mathcal B_p={p=0}.]Every minimal tunnel generator preserves (p), so[\mathrm{Stab}{\mathrm{tun}}(\mathcal B_p)=G{\mathrm{tun}}^{\min}(0)\cong \mathbb F_2^{12},]and the induced graph is (Q_{12}).
[P11080] This is the exact tunnel-stabilizer hierarchy:[\mathbb F_2^4\subset\mathbb F_2^8\subset\mathbb F_2^{12}.]
[P11081] XXV.7 Exact spectra of the canonical zero basins
[P11082] Because each canonical zero basin is a cube under its tunnel stabilizer, its minimal tunnel spectrum is immediate.
[P11083] For the zero fiber:
[P11084] [
[P11085] \mathcal Z_{\mathrm{ph}}\cong Q_4,
[P11086] ]
[P11087] so

[P11095] \mathcal B_\Delta^0,
[P11096] ]

[P11098] [

[P11100] ]
[P11101] so

[P11104] {(2k,\binom8k):k=0,\dots,8}.]

[P11108] ]
[P11109] so
[P11110] [
[P11111] \mathrm{Spec}(\mathcal L_{\mathcal B_p})
[P11112] {(2k,\binom{12}{k}):k=0,\dots,12}.]
[P11113] Thus the canonical zero-family is spectrally stratified by cube dimension:[Q_4 \to Q_8 \to Q_{12}.]
[P11114] This is the exact spectral form of the zero-basin hierarchy.
[P11115] XXV.8 Final answer to the live frontier
[P11116] The live frontier asked whether the dual-zero lattice is the unique nontrivial zero basin or one member of a larger zero-family hierarchy. The exact answer is now:
[P11117] [\boxed{\mathcal Z_{\mathrm{ph}}\text{ is the unique minimal nontrivial zero basin, but it is \emph{not} the unique nontrivial zero-centered basin.}}]
[P11118] More strongly:
[P11119] [\boxed{\text{All zero-centered affine basins are exactly the linear subspaces of }\mathbb F_2^{16}\text{ containing }\mathcal Z_{\mathrm{ph}},}]and those are classified by the quotient[\mathbb F_2^{16}/\mathcal Z_{\mathrm{ph}}\cong \mathbb F_2^{12}.]
[P11120] So the branch’s zero-family hierarchy is not only real; it is completely exact and algebraic.
[P11121] Final synthesis of the next step

[P11127] And the branch-canonical untwisted zero hierarchy is:

[P11129] So the next exact continuation after the affine nexus-subbundle theorem is this: the dual-zero lattice is not the only zero basin, but it is the unique minimal nontrivial one; every larger zero-centered basin is an algebraic extension of it; and the branch’s canonical zero-family is spectrally and group-theoretically stratified as a ladder of binary cubes.
[P11130] XXVI. Derived exact continuation — the 5D chamber lift, chamber nexus registry, and Aether basin metric
[P11131] The next live continuation after the 4D metro / Aether–Zero bundle is the 5D chamber lift. The connected branch states this directly: the seed-derived higher carrier is no longer only 4D, but a 5D crystal skeleton[\Psi_m^{(5)}(r,c)=(X,Y,Z,W,V),]where (V) is the chamber axis. It also states that this is the “next lawful layer after the chamber atlas,” and that the right next tasks are: derive the chamber nexus registry, compute Aether basin counts, identify deep-hub formulas, then fix the full 5D rail family and the Aether field metric.
[P11132] XXVI.1 Exact 5D lift law
[P11133] For side (4^m), the live continuation gives the exact 5D coordinate law:[X=\sum_{t=0}^{m-1}4^t r_t,\qquadY=\sum_{t=0}^{m-1}4^t c_t,][Z=\sum_{t=0}^{m-1}4^t\big((r_t+c_t)\bmod 4\big),\qquadW=\sum_{t=0}^{m-1}4^t\big((r_t-c_t)\bmod 4\big),][V=\sum_{t=0}^{m-1}4^t\big((r_t\bmod 2)+2(c_t\bmod 2)\big).]So (V) is not an arbitrary fifth label. It is the digitwise parity braid of the visible square coordinates. The same source states explicitly that this is the strongest lawful branch-canonical choice of fifth coordinate because it is digitwise, compatible with radix-4 lift, independent of (X,Y,Z,W), and simultaneously supports the two canonical 5D charts[\pi_{XYV}(X,Y,Z,W,V)=(X,Y,V),\qquad\pi_{ZWV}(X,Y,Z,W,V)=(Z,W,V).]At (m=4) this gives the first explicit (256^5) crystal; at (m=6) it gives the (4096^5) skeleton.
[P11134] XXVI.2 Local 5D digit algebra
[P11135] Write each visible digit as
[P11136] [
[P11137] r_t=a_t+2b_t,\qquad c_t=u_t+2v_t,
[P11138] \qquad a_t,b_t,u_t,v_t\in{0,1}.
[P11139] ]
[P11140] Then the live continuation gives the exact local 5D digit laws:
[P11141] [
[P11142] X_t=a_t+2b_t,
[P11143] \qquad
[P11144] Y_t=u_t+2v_t,
[P11145] \qquad
[P11146] V_t=a_t+2u_t.
[P11147] ]
[P11148] For the hidden phase and tunnel digits:
[P11149] [
[P11150] Z_t=(r_t+c_t)\bmod 4
[P11151] (a_t\oplus u_t)+2\bigl(b_t\oplus v_t\oplus a_tu_t\bigr),
[P11152] ]
[P11153] [
[P11154] W_t=(r_t-c_t)\bmod 4
[P11155] (a_t\oplus u_t)+2\bigl(b_t\oplus v_t\oplus u_t\oplus a_tu_t\bigr).]This is a strong exact refinement of the earlier 4D metro law: the chamber coordinate (V_t) records the parity pair ((a_t,u_t)), while (Z_t,W_t) share the same low bit and differ only in the high bit by the added (u_t) term. So (V) is the natural chamber/fiber axis because it extracts exactly the hidden parity data that was still compressed in 4D.
[P11156] XXVI.3 Chamber nexus counting theorem
[P11157] The live continuation then states the exact chamber counting theorem. A chamber nexus family is any equality family involving (V). Because all five coordinates are radix-4 digit assemblies, a global equality holds if and only if the corresponding digitwise equality holds at every (t). Therefore, if (S_F\subseteq\mathbb Z_4^2) is the local digit solution set for family (F), then the global count is exactly[N_F(m)=|S_F|^m.]So every chamber nexus family is an (m)-fold tensor power of its local Gate-4 solution set. This is the exact 5D analogue of the earlier 4D nexus counting law.
[P11158] XXVI.4 Exact pairwise chamber families
[P11159] The live continuation gives the local and global counts for the pairwise chamber families.
[P11160] For[X=V,]the local condition is[a_t+2b_t=a_t+2u_t\iffb_t=u_t,]so the free bits are ((a_t,b_t,v_t)), giving[|S_{X=V}|=2^3=8,\qquadN_{X=V}(m)=8^m.]This is the largest pairwise chamber manifold. At the first explicit chamber scale (m=4),[N_{X=V}(4)=8^4=4096,]and at (m=6),[N_{X=V}(6)=8^6=262144.]Likewise, the continuation proves[N_{Y=V}(m)=4^m,\qquadN_{Z=V}(m)=4^m,\qquadN_{W=V}(m)=4^m,\qquadN_{V=0}(m)=4^m.]So at (m=4) these all have size (256), and at (m=6) they all have size (4096). The chamber-zero family[\mathcal Z_V:={V=0}]is therefore a first exact 5D zero manifold of the branch.
[P11161] XXVI.5 Exact triple, quadruple, and quintuple chamber families
[P11162] The live continuation then gives the exact higher chamber equalities.
[P11163] Triple families:[N_{X=Y=V}(m)=2^m,\qquadN_{X=Z=V}(m)=2^m,\qquadN_{X=W=V}(m)=2^m,][N_{Y=Z=V}(m)=1,\qquadN_{Y=W=V}(m)=1,\qquadN_{Z=W=V}(m)=4^m.]So:
[P11164] the chamber-lock diagonal spine (X=Y=V) has size (2^m),
[P11165] the tunnel-related triple spines (X=Z=V) and (X=W=V) also have size (2^m),
[P11166] the field/Aether spine[\mathcal A_{ZWV}:={Z=W=V}]has size (4^m) and is the largest triple chamber manifold,
[P11167] the two classes (Y=Z=V) and (Y=W=V) are singleton apex families.
[P11168] Quadruple and quintuple families:[N_{X=Y=Z=V}(m)=1,\qquadN_{X=Y=W=V}(m)=1,][N_{X=Z=W=V}(m)=2^m,\qquadN_{Y=Z=W=V}(m)=1,][N_{X=Y=Z=W=V}(m)=1.]So the strongest nontrivial quadruple family is[\mathcal T_{XZWV}:={X=Z=W=V},\qquad|\mathcal T_{XZWV}|=2^m,]which at (m=4) has size (16), and at (m=6) has size (64). The unique full chamber apex remains[\mathcal N_\star^{(5)}:={X=Y=Z=W=V},\qquad |\mathcal N_\star^{(5)}|=1.]So the exact 5D apex ladder given by the live continuation is[\boxed{\mathcal Z_V\supset\mathcal A_{ZWV}\supset\mathcal T_{XZWV}\supset\mathcal N_\star^{(5)}.}]At (m=4), that reads[256 \supset 256 \supset 16 \supset 1,]and at (m=6),[4096 \supset 4096 \supset 64 \supset 1.]The equality of the first two sizes reflects that the chamber-zero manifold and the Aether spine are distinct but equally large classes.
[P11169] XXVI.6 Exact Aether basin theorem in 5D
[P11170] The most important new field-side result in the live continuation is the exact Aether basin theorem. In the 5D field chart[\pi_{ZWV}(X,Y,Z,W,V)=(Z,W,V),]the local field digits ((Z_t,W_t,V_t)) are not arbitrary triples in (\mathbb Z_4^3). The continuation shows they are determined completely by just three binary variables:[(V_{t,0},V_{t,1},\delta_t),\qquad\delta_t:=b_t\oplus v_t.]So there are exactly[8]lawful local field states per digit, not (4^3=64). Therefore the total number of distinct field basins is[N_{\mathrm{Aether\ basins}}(m)=8^m.]Since the full seed-derived 5D skeleton has size[16^m,]every Aether basin has uniform multiplicity[\frac{16^m}{8^m}=2^m.]So the exact field theorem is[\boxed{\text{The Aether field chart is an }8^m\text{-basin quotient of the seed-derived 5D skeleton, with each basin carrying }2^m\text{ structural preimages.}}]At the explicit scales:[m=4:\quad N_{\mathrm{basins}}=8^4=4096,\qquad \text{multiplicity}=2^4=16,][m=6:\quad N_{\mathrm{basins}}=8^6=262144,\qquad \text{multiplicity}=2^6=64.]This is a powerful exact continuation of the 4D Aether theorem: the phase field remains 8-state-per-digit, but the chamber axis makes the field explicitly 5D while preserving the same quotient multiplicity law.
[P11171] XXVI.7 Special 5D Aether basin families
[P11172] The live continuation then identifies the special field-side zero and near-zero basin classes.
[P11173] For (V=0), there are exactly (2) local field states per digit, so the number of chamber-zero field basins is[2^m.]Similarly for[Z=0\quad\text{and}\quadW=0,]there are again (2^m) field basins each. The most important one is the triple-zero Aether core basin[(Z,W,V)=(0,0,0),]which is a single field basin whose preimage has size (2^m). Hence:[m=4:\quad |\pi_{ZWV}^{-1}(0,0,0)|=16,][m=6:\quad |\pi_{ZWV}^{-1}(0,0,0)|=64.]This is the exact 5D echo of the 4D phase-zero lattice: the Aether field origin remains one basin, but the chamber lift doubles the internal multiplicity scale by scale.
[P11174] XXVI.8 Why (V) is the strongest lawful 5th coordinate
[P11175] The continuation then answers its own next question: why is the chosen chamber axis (V) the strongest branch-canonical fifth coordinate?
[P11176] It lists the five required properties of a lawful fifth coordinate:
[P11177] it must be digitwise,
[P11178] it must add genuinely new structure beyond (X,Y,Z,W),
[P11179] it must reveal what is hidden in 4D rather than import an alien quantity,
[P11180] it must be transport-compatible with the Square/Circle/Triangle engine,
[P11181] it must support both chamber chart ((X,Y,V)) and field chart ((Z,W,V)).
[P11182] The current branch’s choice[V_t=(r_t\bmod 2)+2(c_t\bmod 2)]satisfies all five:
[P11183] digitwise: yes,
[P11184] independent: yes,
[P11185] low-order reveal: yes, it extracts the visible parity braid,
[P11186] engine-compatible: yes, it is built from the same digit planes,
[P11187] chart-compatible: yes, it supports both ((X,Y,V)) and ((Z,W,V)) exactly.
[P11188] So the continuation concludes:[\boxed{V_t=(r_t\bmod 2)+2(c_t\bmod 2)\text{ is the minimal digitwise coordinate that exposes the hidden chamber/fiber structure of the 4D crystal while remaining fully compatible with the seed’s radix-4 transport law.}}]This is the exact chamber-axis theorem of the current branch.
[P11189] XXVI.9 Full 5D rail family
[P11190] The continuation also writes down the complete 5D rail family.
[P11191] Primitive coordinate rails:[R_X,\ R_Y,\ R_Z,\ R_W,\ R_V.]
[P11192] Chamber-diagonal rails in the ((X,Y,V))-chart:[R_{X=V},\qquad R_{Y=V}.]
[P11193] Field-equality rails in the ((Z,W,V))-chart:[R_{Z=V},\qquad R_{W=V},\qquad R_{Z=W},\qquad R_{Z=W=V}.]
[P11194] Zero rails:[R_{V=0},\qquad R_{Z=0},\qquad R_{W=0}.]
[P11195] Apex rail:[R_\star:\ X=Y=Z=W=V.]

It is not just “the old rails plus another coordinate”; it is the exact mixed-rail family enabled by the fifth coordinate.

[P11237] CLXXVII. Exact transformation operators on the selected set
[P11238] For any lift increment (\Delta\ge1), define the depth-shift operator[T_\Delta:m\longmapsto m+\Delta.]Its exact action on the selected-dimensional state package is:

[P11240] [\Xi(m+\Delta)=\Xi(m)+\Delta(1,2,3,4).]
[P11241] So on visible/invisible size exponents, (T_\Delta) is a pure translation by the fixed direction vector[R:=(1,2,3,4).]
[P11242] CLXXVII.2 District action
[P11243] Using
[P11244] [
[P11245] D_m=\frac{m^3+4m^2+5m+2}{2},

[P11247] one gets
[P11248] [
[P11249] D_{m+\Delta}-D_m
[P11250] \frac12\Bigl(3\Delta m^2+(3\Delta^2+8\Delta)m+\Delta^3+4\Delta^2+5\Delta\Bigr).]
[P11251] So district transport is polynomial, not multiplicative.
[P11252] CLXXVII.3 Apex action

[P11254] [
[P11255] \Omega_{m+\Delta}
[P11256] \frac{11(4^\Delta-1)}{3}+4^\Delta\Omega_m.]
[P11257] Equivalently,
[P11258] [
[P11259] \begin{pmatrix}
[P11260] \Omega_{m+\Delta}\[2pt] 1
[P11261] \end{pmatrix}

[P11263] So the selected-dimensional subsystem is governed by:
[P11264] linear translation on exponent space,
[P11265] cubic drift on district count,
[P11266] affine-expanding transport on apex score.

[P11328] CLXXXII. Exact resonance theorem on the selected set

[P11330] Let the layer exponents be[\sigma_E=1,\qquad \sigma_S=2,\qquad \sigma_P=3,\qquad \sigma_B=4.]Then[\text{layer}\alpha(m)=\text{layer}\beta(n)\iff\sigma_\alpha m=\sigma_\beta n.]
